Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
8 min
The Four Usul Return to Internal Speech
Critique of the four usul returning to human internal speech

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi-Ash'ari claim that the four usul (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) ultimately return to internal speech (kalam nafsi) and critique the view attributed to al-Amidi.

Core Idea
The four usul are merely revealers of Allah's internal speech; only His kalam nafsi is truly authoritative.

This lesson unpacks a subtle and often misunderstood claim in Hanafi usul: that all primary sources of Sharia—Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas—are in reality returns to the internal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah for the first two, and for the latter two to the internal speech of the consensus or the mujtahid. The author critically examines this view and clarifies that only Allah's internal speech carries genuine authority; human internal speech has no independent evidential weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about the four usul
Locate the statement that each source returns to a type of internal speech. Note which entity's kalam nafsi each source corresponds to according to the view transmitted from al-Amidi.
The view is presented to be critiqued, not endorsed.
2
Understand the author's objection
Analyze why the author finds this view 'far-fetched' (ba'id). Focus on the point that human internal speech is not a proof in itself unless it refers back to Allah's speech.
The key is the principle of authority: only Allah's speech is inherently hujja.
3
Apply to Qiyas specifically
Examine the problem for Qiyas: the mujtahid's internal speech cannot be a proof upon himself or another mujtahid. The equality (musawat) must be in the internal reality (al-amr al-nafsi), not in the mujtahid's utterance.
This preserves the objectivity of Qiyas.
4
Connect to the larger definition of kalam nafsi
Recognize that this discussion sets the stage for the upcoming definition of kalam nafsi as a mental ratio. The author is preparing to defend a specific ontological account of internal speech.
The critique of the Amidi view is intertwined with the author's own positive theory.

(ثم هذه الأصول الأربعة راجعة إلى كلام النفس) للباري عز وجل، فإنه هو الحاكم حقيقة بكلامه الأزلي هذه الدلائل كواشف عنه، وفي شرح المختصر مطابقاً لما نقل عن الآمدي أن الكتاب راجع إلى الكلام النفسي للباري الحق تعالى، والسنة إلى الكلام النفسي للرسول صلوات الله عليه وآله وأصحابه، والإجماع إلى النفسي للمجمعين، والقياس إلى النفسي للمجتهد، ولا يخفى بعد، فإن النفسي لما سوى الله تعالى لا حجة فيه أصلاً، ولو كانت فلأجل رجوعه إلى كلام الله تعالى مع أنه غير ظاهر في القياس، لأن المجتهد القائس كلامه ليس حجة عليه، بل المساواة النفس الأمرية، وإلا كان هو حاكماً على نفسه، ومقلده ليس حجة قياسه بل قوله فقط، وكذا ليس كلامه حجة على المجتهد الآخر، إذ لا يجوز له التقليد فافهم (وهو) أي كلام النفس (نسبة نفسية) قائمة بالنفس وكيفية ذهنية كالعلم والإرادة مجعولة معها مخلوطة بها إرادة إفادة المخاطب تلك النسبة بالضرورة الوجدانية فإنا إذا نراجع إلى وجداننا نعلم أن في أذهاننا نسبة تعلق إرادة إفادتها وليس عند تصور النسبة المفادة بكلام الغير النسبة المخلوطة معها الإرادة المذكورة، ثم الظاهر أن هذا تحقيق لمطلق الكلام النفسي الذي كلامه تعالى جزئي من جزئياته ففي هذا إشارة إلى أن الصفات الإلهية مجعولة، لكن المجعولية لا تكون إلا بالإيجاب فما وقع من المصنف فيما سبق أن الصفات واجبة بالذات فليست مجعولة ليس من مرضياته وإنما وقع مجاراة مع الخصم، ويمكن أن يكون تحقيقاً لكلام الإنسان النفسي ويقاس عليه كلامه تعالى والمراد بالجعل الجعل بالاختيار، وإذا ثبت بالوجدان اختلاط تلك النسبة بإرادة الإفادة دون الصورة العلمية فإنها قد تكون من غير تلك الإرادة فجاءت النسبة المذكورة حقيقة غير الصورة (العلمية وهذه النسبة كالكيفيات السارية في (الكميات وإذا ثبتت المغايرة فاندفع ما قيل في حواشي ميرزاجان تحقق نسبة في زيد قائم مغايرة لمفهوم الأخبار) وهي الحكاية وللنسبة الواقعية التي بينهما) وهي المحكى عنه ( وللصورة العلمية القائمة بالذهن الحاصلة منها مما يكذبه (الوجدان فإنه لا توجد نسبة إذا إلى الوجدان، وقيل فيها أيضاً الحق أنها هي الصورة العلمية للنسبة الخارجية من حيث روجع إفادة الكلام فهي من حيث إنها في الواقع نسبة خارجية ومن حيث إنها صورة مطابقة لها علم، ومن حيث إنها مفاد بالكلام كلام نفسي هذا ويحوم حوله ما نقله علي القاري رحمه الله في شرح الفقه الأكبر عن الإمام حجة الإسلام قدس سره أن الكلام النفسي حصة من العلم، ومعنى تكلم الله مع من اصطفاه جعله مطلعاً على علومه تعالى هذا: (نعم إثبات كونها حقيقة بسيطة غير العلم والإرادة عسير لا أنه باطل بالوجدان (فافهم ) أما كونها حقيقة بسيطة أصلاً، فإن هذه النسبة مدلول الكلام اللفظي على ما يعطى كلمات متأخري فلا يكاد يصح الأشعرية، وهي قد تكون إنشائية طلبية ،وغيرها، وقد تكون إخبارية وكلها متخالفة الحقيقة، فأين البساطة، وهل هذا إلا كما يقال : إن أمراً واحداً بسيطاً قد يكون فرساً، وقد يكون إنساناً قلت : لا أو باعتبار التعلقات ثم إن وجود النسبة وحدها من غير أن يكون معها المنتسبان غير معقول، وإذا كان فيما بين المنتسبين فلا تصح البساطة أصلاً، بل الذي يعقل على تقدير كون الكلام النفسي عبارة عن مدلول اللفظي هو المعاني الملحوظة بينها النسب الإنشائية أو الإخبارية المرتبة، حسب ترتب الألفاظ القائمة بالنفس، أو بذات الباري عز وجل وهي مغايرة للعلم بل هو متعلق بها لا غير، وكذا للإرادة بل هي متعلقة بإفادتها وأما عسر معرفة مغايرته إياهما فللاختلاط، فإن يصح أيضاً مغايرته للعلم ولا يتجاوز الحق عما قال هذا القائل، فإن هذه المعاني أو هذا الأمر البسيط مدلول اللفظي على ما ينادي ظواهر العبارات، فهي صورة قائمة بذات الباري أو النفس والعلم هو حصول صورة المعلوم للعالم ،قلت هذا هو الذي شجع هذا القائل على ما قال : لكنك عسيت أن لا ترتاب في أن هذا من هذيانات الفلاسفة، ولا نساعد عليه البتة، بل هو باطل محض على ما برهنا عليه في تعليقاتنا المتعلقة بشرح المواقف، ألم ترهم كيف يسيرون في هذه المسألة اتحاد العلم بالمعلوم كالحيارى في الصحارى لما كانوا على عمياء ولزمهم ما لزمهم من عدم كون العلم حقيقة واحدة، وكون شيء واحد جوهراً وكيفاً وتصوراً وتصديقاً وغير ذلك من المفاسد وهم يناقضون أنفسهم في تبيان هذه المسألة فافهم (قيل) في تلك الحواشي أيضاً : العلماء اختلفوا في أن الألفاظ موضوعة للأمر الخارجي للصورة الذهنية كما مر في صدر المبادىء اللغوية فالنفسي إذا كان مفاد للفظي) كما اشتهر (و) الحال أنه لا يكون أمراً خارجياً) وهو ظاهر لم يكن إلا الصورة العلمية) لا غير (أقول) هذا (منقوض بالإنشائي) من الكلام فإن الطلب غير تصور النسبة الطلبية ضرورة) كيف ومن تصور النسبة الطلبية في أضرب لا يسمى طالباً له وإنما يسمى به من قام الطلب به، وإذا كان له، مغايراً للتصور كان غير العلم قطعاً هذا كلام متين لا شك فيه لكن كلام هذا القائل بظاهره يدل على أن قوله مخصوص بالأخبار، اللهم إلا أن يقال : النسبة القائمة بنفس من في صدد الأخبار غير تصور النسبة الإخبارية بل الوافي في دفعه أن غاية ما لزم مما ذكر أن النفسي هو الصورة القائمة بالذهن، ولا يلزم منه أن يكون عين العلم، وإنما يلزم لو كان عبارة عن الصورة من المعلوم وليس كما علمت لا يقال أن كون الصورة القائمة بالنفس مدلول الكلام اللفظي ينافي ما قد مر أن الألفاظ موضوعة للمعاني من حيث هي لأن المراد من كون هذا القائم مدلول اللفظي كونه مدلولاً مع قطع النظر عن القيام فتدبر فيه ثم استدل في المختصر على أنها نسبة ذهنية بأنها متوقفة على تعقل المفردين بخلاف النسبة الخارجية قيل) في الحواشي : القدر الضروري إدراك المفردين ولا يلزم منه أن يكون حصولهما في الذهن بصورهما العقلية حتى يلزم التعقل أي كونه تعقلاً بل يجوز أن يكون هذا الإدراك (علماً حضورياً فلا يلزم التعقل، لأنه عبارة عن الحصولي، وهذا إنما يرد لو أريد بالتعقل هذا، أما لو أريد مطلق الإدراك فلا وهذه الإرادة شائعة في أمثال هذه الفنون (أقول : إنها نسبة حاكية، والحكاية إنما تكون بحصول صورة المحكي لا بوجوده بنفسه كما في العلم الحضوري، فلا يصح كونه حضورياً، فإن قلت إدراك النفس وصفاتها حضوري ولا بعد في إيقاع الربط
And as for the inclusion of istishab according to its proponents: it is nothing but inference from existence to continuation. So if the existence is established by the four proofs, then it is valid; otherwise, it is disregarded. Ponder this. As for us, we do not need to answer because it is not a proof in our school. Then these four principles return to the internal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah Almighty, for He is the true judge by His eternal speech, and these proofs are revealers of it. In Sharh al-Mukhtasar, in agreement with what is transmitted from al-Amidi, the Book returns to the internal speech of Allah the Exalted, the Sunnah to the internal speech of the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family and companions), Ijma to the internal speech of the mujtami'un, and Qiyas to the internal speech of the mujtahid. This is not subtle: for internal speech of anyone other than Allah is not a proof at all, and if it were, it would be because it returns to the speech of Allah, whereas it is not apparent in Qiyas, because the speech of the mujtahid who performs qiyas is not a proof upon him; rather, the equality is in the internal reality. Otherwise, he would be a judge over himself, and his follower's proof is not his qiyas but only his statement. And likewise, his speech is not a proof on another mujtahid, since he is not allowed to do taqlid. So understand. (And it) i.e., internal speech (is a mental ratio) subsisting in the soul, a mental quality like knowledge and will, created with them mixed with them, along with the intention of informing the addressee of that ratio, by existential necessity. For when we refer to our consciousness, we know that in our minds there is a ratio attached to an intention to inform it, and when we conceptualize the ratio conveyed by another's speech, we do not have the ratio mixed with that intention. Then it is apparent that this is a verification of absolute internal speech, of which the speech of Allah is a particular instance. In this there is an indication that divine attributes are created, but creation (ja'l) is only by necessity. So what the author mentioned earlier, that attributes are self-necessary and not created, is not from his sound opinions; rather it was a concession to the opponent. And it can be a verification of human internal speech, and the speech of Allah is analogized to it. By creation (ja'l) is meant creation by choice. And since it is established by consciousness that that ratio is mixed with the intention to inform, unlike the mental image, for it can be without that intention, therefore the mentioned ratio is truly other than the mental image. And this ratio is like qualities flowing in quantities. And when the difference is established, what was said in the glosses of Mirzajan is repelled: that a ratio in 'Zayd is standing' is different from the concept of the sentence—which is the narrative—and from the real ratio between them—which is the narrated—and from the mental image subsisting in the mind obtained from them, which the consciousness denies, for no ratio enters consciousness. And it is also said therein that the truth is that it is the mental image of the external ratio insofar as it is considered the import of speech. So it is, insofar as it is in reality an external ratio, and insofar as it is an image matching it, knowledge, and insofar as it is a speech-import, internal speech. This is a view, and around it is what 'Ali al-Qari (rahimahullah) transmitted in Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar from Imam Hujjat al-Islam (may Allah sanctify his secret) that internal speech is a portion of knowledge, and the meaning of Allah speaking to whomever He chooses is making him aware of His knowledge. This is so. (Yes, establishing that it is a simple essence, distinct from knowledge and will, is difficult, not that it is false by consciousness. (So understand.) As for its being a simple essence at all: this ratio, the meaning of verbal speech according to later scholars, the Ash'ari view can hardly be correct: it may be performative-demanding and other, and may be informative, and all these are heterogeneous in reality. So where is simplicity? Is this not like saying a single simple thing may be a horse and may be a human? I say: no, or by consideration of relations. Then the existence of the ratio alone without the two relata is inconceivable, and since it is between the two relata, simplicity is not valid at all. Rather, what is conceivable, assuming that internal speech is the meaning of verbal speech, is the meanings among which are the performative or informative ratios arranged according to the arrangement of words, subsisting in the soul or in the essence of Allah Almighty, and they are distinct from knowledge—rather knowledge is related to them—and likewise distinct from will—rather will is related to their communication. As for the difficulty of knowing its distinction from them, it is due to mixture. So it is also possible that it is distinct from knowledge, and the truth does not go beyond what this proponent said. For these meanings or this simple thing is the meaning of verbal speech as the apparent expressions indicate, so they are an image subsisting in the essence of Allah or the soul, and knowledge is the obtaining of the image of the known for the knower. I say: This is what emboldened this proponent to say what he said. But you should not doubt that this is from the ravings of the philosophers, and we do not support it at all; rather it is pure falsehood, as we demonstrated in our glosses on Sharh al-Mawaqif. Do you not see how they wander in this issue of the unity of knowledge with the known like the bewildered in deserts, since they are upon blindness? And they are compelled to what they are compelled: that knowledge is not a single reality, that one thing is substance and quality, conceptualization and assent, and other corruptions, while they contradict themselves in explaining this issue. So understand. (It was said) in those glosses also: The scholars differed over whether words are placed for external objects or mental images, as passed earlier in the beginning of linguistic principles. So internal speech, if it is the import of verbal speech (as is well-known) and the case is that it is not an external thing (which is apparent), then it is nothing but the mental image, no more. (I say:) This is (refuted by the performative) type of speech, for demand is necessarily other than the conceptualization of the demand ratio. How could it be? One who conceptualizes a demand ratio in a strike is not called a demander of it; rather, one in whom the demand subsists is called that. And since it is, for it is other than conceptualization, it is certainly other than knowledge. This is a solid statement, no doubt about it. But the statement of this proponent apparently indicates that his statement is specific to declarative sentences. Unless it is said: the ratio subsisting in the soul of one about to declare is other than the conceptualization of the declarative ratio. But the sufficient in refutation is that the utmost that follows from what was mentioned is that internal speech is the image subsisting in the mind, and it does not necessitate that it be the same as knowledge. That would only follow if it were the image of the known, and it is not as you have learned. It cannot be said that the fact that the image subsisting in the soul is the meaning of verbal speech contradicts what has passed that words are placed for meanings per se, because what is meant by this subsisting being the meaning of verbal speech is that it is a meaning without consideration of its subsistence. So ponder. Then in al-Mukhtasar it was argued that it is a mental ratio because it depends on conceptualizing the two single terms, unlike the external ratio. (It was said) in the glosses: The necessary extent is perception of the two single terms, and it does not necessitate that they be obtained in the mind by their mental images so that conceptualization (i.e., being a conceptualization) is necessitated. Rather, it is possible that this perception is (knowledge by presence), so conceptualization—which is representational—is not necessitated. This is a rejoinder only if by conceptualization is meant this; but if absolute perception is meant, then not. And this latter meaning is common in such arts. (I say:) It is a representational ratio, and representation occurs only by the obtaining of an image of the represented, not by its own existence as in knowledge by presence, so it cannot be knowledge by presence. If you say: The soul's perception of itself and its attributes is knowledge by presence, and there is no harm in positing the linkage.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analytical expansion on the claim that the four fundamental sources of Sharia (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas) ultimately return to internal speech (kalam nafsi). It begins by noting the inclusion of istishab (presumption of continuity) as a proof according to some, but states that the Hanafi school does not accept istishab as a proof. The author then discusses a view reported from al-Amidi that each source corresponds to the internal speech of a particular entity: the Qur'an to Allah's internal speech, Sunnah to the Prophet's, Ijma to the consensus of the mujtahids, and Qiyas to the internal speech of the mujtahid. The author criticizes this view because internal speech of anyone other than Allah carries no authority; if it did, it would only be by reference back to Allah's speech. Moreover, in Qiyas, the mujtahid's own speech cannot be a proof upon himself. The passage then defines kalam nafsi as a mental ratio (nisba nafsiyya) that subsists in the soul, akin to a mental quality, mixed with the intention to inform. This ratio is distinct from the mental image (sura 'ilmiyya) because the latter may exist without the intention to inform. The author argues that this ratio is not a simple essence because it can be performative (insha'i) or informative (ikhbari), and those are different realities. Even within the same type, the ratio involves both relata, so it cannot be simple. The author also refutes the idea that internal speech is merely the mental image of the external ratio, arguing that performative speech like commands involves a demand (talab) that is other than the conceptualization of the demand. He further argues that if internal speech were knowledge by presence (ilm huduri), it could not be representational (hikaya) because representation requires an image of the represented, not the represented itself. The passage engages with several glosses and opposing views, ultimately defending the Ash'ari position that internal speech is distinct from knowledge and will, and that it is a composite of meanings rather than a simple reality.

Key Terms
الكلام النفسي (al-kalam al-nafsi): Internal speech: the mental ratio (nisba nafsiyya) that is the meaning conveyed by verbal speech, distinct from knowledge and will.
المساواة النفس الأمرية (al-musawat al-nafs al-amriyya): The internal reality equality; the objective commonality that exists in reality, not merely in the mind of the mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the view that Qiyas returns to the internal speech of the mujtahid?
A) Because the mujtahid's internal speech is not eternal.
B) Because the mujtahid's speech cannot be a proof upon himself or other mujtahids.
C) Because Qiyas is not a source of law at all.
D) Because the mujtahid's internal speech is identical to his knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Only Allah's internal speech is inherently authoritative; the four usul are revealers of that speech, not independent voices of human internal speech.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
10 min
Kalam Nafsi as Mental Ratio: Definition and Defense
Definition of internal speech as mental ratio with intentionality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define kalam nafsi as a mental ratio (nisba nafsiyya) and distinguish it from the mental image (sura 'ilmiyya) and from knowledge and will.

Core Idea
Internal speech is a mental ratio mixed with intention to inform, not a mere mental image.

After clarifying that only Allah's internal speech is authoritative, the author now defines what internal speech is: a mental ratio (nisba nafsiyya) subsisting in the soul, akin to a quality, and crucially mixed with the intention to inform. This definition distinguishes kalam nafsi from the mere mental image of an object, which can exist without that intention. The author appeals to immediate consciousness (wijdan) to establish this, and also notes the theological implication that divine attributes are created (maj'ula) by choice, a point that caused some controversy.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of kalam nafsi
Read the definition: 'a mental ratio (nisba nafsiyya) subsisting in the soul, like a mental quality, created with it, mixed with the intention to inform.'
The ratio is what connects two concepts (e.g., subject and predicate).
2
Understand the term 'mixed with intention' (mukhtalita biha irada ifadat)
The ratio in the mind is accompanied by an intention to convey it to another. This is key: without intention, it's just a concept (sura 'ilmiyya).
This is established by self-reflection (wijdan).
3
Distinguish from mental image (sura 'ilmiyya)
A mental image can exist without any intention to inform; it's a mere concept. Kalam nafsi always involves the intention to communicate.
Example: thinking of a horse vs. intending to tell someone that the horse is running.
4
Consider the theological implication: divine attributes as created
The author notes that if kalam nafsi is a mental ratio that is created (maj'ul), then divine attributes would be created, contradicting the earlier statement that attributes are necessary. He clarifies that this definition applies to human speech; for God, it is analogical and the creation (ja'l) is by choice.
The author is careful to avoid theological inconsistency.

وأما اندراج الاستصحاب عند قائليه : فلأنه ليس إلا الاستدلال بالوجود على البقاء، فالوجود إن كان ثابتاً بالأدلة الأربعة فهي وإلا فلا عبرة به فتأمل فيه، وأما نحن فلا نحتاج إلى الجواب لعدم كونه حجة عندنا (ثم هذه الأصول الأربعة راجعة إلى كلام النفس) للباري عز وجل، فإنه هو الحاكم حقيقة بكلامه الأزلي هذه الدلائل كواشف عنه، وفي شرح المختصر مطابقاً لما نقل عن الآمدي أن الكتاب راجع إلى الكلام النفسي للباري الحق تعالى، والسنة إلى الكلام النفسي للرسول صلوات الله عليه وآله وأصحابه، والإجماع إلى النفسي للمجمعين، والقياس إلى النفسي للمجتهد، ولا يخفى بعد، فإن النفسي لما سوى الله تعالى لا حجة فيه أصلاً، ولو كانت فلأجل رجوعه إلى كلام الله تعالى مع أنه غير ظاهر في القياس، لأن المجتهد القائس كلامه ليس حجة عليه، بل المساواة النفس الأمرية، وإلا كان هو حاكماً على نفسه، ومقلده ليس حجة قياسه بل قوله فقط، وكذا ليس كلامه حجة على المجتهد الآخر، إذ لا يجوز له التقليد فافهم (وهو) أي كلام النفس (نسبة نفسية) قائمة بالنفس وكيفية ذهنية كالعلم والإرادة مجعولة معها مخلوطة بها إرادة إفادة المخاطب تلك النسبة بالضرورة الوجدانية فإنا إذا نراجع إلى وجداننا نعلم أن في أذهاننا نسبة تعلق إرادة إفادتها وليس عند تصور النسبة المفادة بكلام الغير النسبة المخلوطة معها الإرادة المذكورة، ثم الظاهر أن هذا تحقيق لمطلق الكلام النفسي الذي كلامه تعالى جزئي من جزئياته ففي هذا إشارة إلى أن الصفات الإلهية مجعولة، لكن المجعولية لا تكون إلا بالإيجاب فما وقع من المصنف فيما سبق أن الصفات واجبة بالذات فليست مجعولة ليس من مرضياته وإنما وقع مجاراة مع الخصم، ويمكن أن يكون تحقيقاً لكلام الإنسان النفسي ويقاس عليه كلامه تعالى والمراد بالجعل الجعل بالاختيار، وإذا ثبت بالوجدان اختلاط تلك النسبة بإرادة الإفادة دون الصورة العلمية فإنها قد تكون من غير تلك الإرادة فجاءت النسبة المذكورة حقيقة غير الصورة (العلمية وهذه النسبة كالكيفيات السارية في (الكميات وإذا ثبتت المغايرة فاندفع ما قيل في حواشي ميرزاجان تحقق نسبة في زيد قائم مغايرة لمفهوم الأخبار) وهي الحكاية وللنسبة الواقعية التي بينهما) وهي المحكى عنه ( وللصورة العلمية القائمة بالذهن الحاصلة منها مما يكذبه (الوجدان فإنه لا توجد نسبة إذا إلى الوجدان، وقيل فيها أيضاً الحق أنها هي الصورة العلمية للنسبة الخارجية من حيث روجع إفادة الكلام فهي من حيث إنها في الواقع نسبة خارجية ومن حيث إنها صورة مطابقة لها علم، ومن حيث إنها مفاد بالكلام كلام نفسي هذا ويحوم حوله ما نقله علي القاري رحمه الله في شرح الفقه الأكبر عن الإمام حجة الإسلام قدس سره أن الكلام النفسي حصة من العلم، ومعنى تكلم الله مع من اصطفاه جعله مطلعاً على علومه تعالى هذا: (نعم إثبات كونها حقيقة بسيطة غير العلم والإرادة عسير لا أنه باطل بالوجدان (فافهم ) أما كونها حقيقة بسيطة أصلاً، فإن هذه النسبة مدلول الكلام اللفظي على ما يعطى كلمات متأخري فلا يكاد يصح الأشعرية، وهي قد تكون إنشائية طلبية ،وغيرها، وقد تكون إخبارية وكلها متخالفة الحقيقة، فأين البساطة، وهل هذا إلا كما يقال : إن أمراً واحداً بسيطاً قد يكون فرساً، وقد يكون إنساناً قلت : لا أو باعتبار التعلقات ثم إن وجود النسبة وحدها من غير أن يكون معها المنتسبان غير معقول، وإذا كان فيما بين المنتسبين فلا تصح البساطة أصلاً، بل الذي يعقل على تقدير كون الكلام النفسي عبارة عن مدلول اللفظي هو المعاني الملحوظة بينها النسب الإنشائية أو الإخبارية المرتبة، حسب ترتب الألفاظ القائمة بالنفس، أو بذات الباري عز وجل وهي مغايرة للعلم بل هو متعلق بها لا غير، وكذا للإرادة بل هي متعلقة بإفادتها وأما عسر معرفة مغايرته إياهما فللاختلاط، فإن يصح أيضاً مغايرته للعلم ولا يتجاوز الحق عما قال هذا القائل، فإن هذه المعاني أو هذا الأمر البسيط مدلول اللفظي على ما ينادي ظواهر العبارات، فهي صورة قائمة بذات الباري أو النفس والعلم هو حصول صورة المعلوم للعالم ،قلت هذا هو الذي شجع هذا القائل على ما قال : لكنك عسيت أن لا ترتاب في أن هذا من هذيانات الفلاسفة، ولا نساعد عليه البتة، بل هو باطل محض على ما برهنا عليه في تعليقاتنا المتعلقة بشرح المواقف، ألم ترهم كيف يسيرون في هذه المسألة اتحاد العلم بالمعلوم كالحيارى في الصحارى لما كانوا على عمياء ولزمهم ما لزمهم من عدم كون العلم حقيقة واحدة، وكون شيء واحد جوهراً وكيفاً وتصوراً وتصديقاً وغير ذلك من المفاسد وهم يناقضون أنفسهم في تبيان هذه المسألة فافهم (قيل) في تلك الحواشي أيضاً : العلماء اختلفوا في أن الألفاظ موضوعة للأمر الخارجي للصورة الذهنية كما مر في صدر المبادىء اللغوية فالنفسي إذا كان مفاد للفظي) كما اشتهر (و) الحال أنه لا يكون أمراً خارجياً) وهو ظاهر لم يكن إلا الصورة العلمية) لا غير (أقول) هذا (منقوض بالإنشائي) من الكلام فإن الطلب غير تصور النسبة الطلبية ضرورة) كيف ومن تصور النسبة الطلبية في أضرب لا يسمى طالباً له وإنما يسمى به من قام الطلب به، وإذا كان له، مغايراً للتصور كان غير العلم قطعاً هذا كلام متين لا شك فيه لكن كلام هذا القائل بظاهره يدل على أن قوله مخصوص بالأخبار، اللهم إلا أن يقال : النسبة القائمة بنفس من في صدد الأخبار غير تصور النسبة الإخبارية بل الوافي في دفعه أن غاية ما لزم مما ذكر أن النفسي هو الصورة القائمة بالذهن، ولا يلزم منه أن يكون عين العلم، وإنما يلزم لو كان عبارة عن الصورة من المعلوم وليس كما علمت لا يقال أن كون الصورة القائمة بالنفس مدلول الكلام اللفظي ينافي ما قد مر أن الألفاظ موضوعة للمعاني من حيث هي لأن المراد من كون هذا القائم مدلول اللفظي كونه مدلولاً مع قطع النظر عن القيام فتدبر فيه ثم استدل في المختصر على أنها نسبة ذهنية بأنها متوقفة على تعقل المفردين بخلاف النسبة الخارجية قيل) في الحواشي : القدر الضروري إدراك المفردين ولا يلزم منه أن يكون حصولهما في الذهن بصورهما العقلية حتى يلزم التعقل أي كونه تعقلاً بل يجوز أن يكون هذا الإدراك (علماً حضورياً فلا يلزم التعقل، لأنه عبارة عن الحصولي، وهذا إنما يرد لو أريد بالتعقل هذا، أما لو أريد مطلق الإدراك فلا وهذه الإرادة شائعة في أمثال هذه الفنون (أقول : إنها نسبة حاكية، والحكاية إنما تكون بحصول صورة المحكي لا بوجوده بنفسه كما في العلم الحضوري، فلا يصح كونه حضورياً، فإن قلت إدراك النفس وصفاتها حضوري ولا بعد في إيقاع الربط
And as for the inclusion of istishab according to its proponents: it is nothing but inference from existence to continuation. So if the existence is established by the four proofs, then it is valid; otherwise, it is disregarded. Ponder this. As for us, we do not need to answer because it is not a proof in our school. Then these four principles return to the internal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah Almighty, for He is the true judge by His eternal speech, and these proofs are revealers of it. In Sharh al-Mukhtasar, in agreement with what is transmitted from al-Amidi, the Book returns to the internal speech of Allah the Exalted, the Sunnah to the internal speech of the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family and companions), Ijma to the internal speech of the mujtami'un, and Qiyas to the internal speech of the mujtahid. This is not subtle: for internal speech of anyone other than Allah is not a proof at all, and if it were, it would be because it returns to the speech of Allah, whereas it is not apparent in Qiyas, because the speech of the mujtahid who performs qiyas is not a proof upon him; rather, the equality is in the internal reality. Otherwise, he would be a judge over himself, and his follower's proof is not his qiyas but only his statement. And likewise, his speech is not a proof on another mujtahid, since he is not allowed to do taqlid. So understand. (And it) i.e., internal speech (is a mental ratio) subsisting in the soul, a mental quality like knowledge and will, created with them mixed with them, along with the intention of informing the addressee of that ratio, by existential necessity. For when we refer to our consciousness, we know that in our minds there is a ratio attached to an intention to inform it, and when we conceptualize the ratio conveyed by another's speech, we do not have the ratio mixed with that intention. Then it is apparent that this is a verification of absolute internal speech, of which the speech of Allah is a particular instance. In this there is an indication that divine attributes are created, but creation (ja'l) is only by necessity. So what the author mentioned earlier, that attributes are self-necessary and not created, is not from his sound opinions; rather it was a concession to the opponent. And it can be a verification of human internal speech, and the speech of Allah is analogized to it. By creation (ja'l) is meant creation by choice. And since it is established by consciousness that that ratio is mixed with the intention to inform, unlike the mental image, for it can be without that intention, therefore the mentioned ratio is truly other than the mental image. And this ratio is like qualities flowing in quantities. And when the difference is established, what was said in the glosses of Mirzajan is repelled: that a ratio in 'Zayd is standing' is different from the concept of the sentence—which is the narrative—and from the real ratio between them—which is the narrated—and from the mental image subsisting in the mind obtained from them, which the consciousness denies, for no ratio enters consciousness. And it is also said therein that the truth is that it is the mental image of the external ratio insofar as it is considered the import of speech. So it is, insofar as it is in reality an external ratio, and insofar as it is an image matching it, knowledge, and insofar as it is a speech-import, internal speech. This is a view, and around it is what 'Ali al-Qari (rahimahullah) transmitted in Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar from Imam Hujjat al-Islam (may Allah sanctify his secret) that internal speech is a portion of knowledge, and the meaning of Allah speaking to whomever He chooses is making him aware of His knowledge. This is so. (Yes, establishing that it is a simple essence, distinct from knowledge and will, is difficult, not that it is false by consciousness. (So understand.) As for its being a simple essence at all: this ratio, the meaning of verbal speech according to later scholars, the Ash'ari view can hardly be correct: it may be performative-demanding and other, and may be informative, and all these are heterogeneous in reality. So where is simplicity? Is this not like saying a single simple thing may be a horse and may be a human? I say: no, or by consideration of relations. Then the existence of the ratio alone without the two relata is inconceivable, and since it is between the two relata, simplicity is not valid at all. Rather, what is conceivable, assuming that internal speech is the meaning of verbal speech, is the meanings among which are the performative or informative ratios arranged according to the arrangement of words, subsisting in the soul or in the essence of Allah Almighty, and they are distinct from knowledge—rather knowledge is related to them—and likewise distinct from will—rather will is related to their communication. As for the difficulty of knowing its distinction from them, it is due to mixture. So it is also possible that it is distinct from knowledge, and the truth does not go beyond what this proponent said. For these meanings or this simple thing is the meaning of verbal speech as the apparent expressions indicate, so they are an image subsisting in the essence of Allah or the soul, and knowledge is the obtaining of the image of the known for the knower. I say: This is what emboldened this proponent to say what he said. But you should not doubt that this is from the ravings of the philosophers, and we do not support it at all; rather it is pure falsehood, as we demonstrated in our glosses on Sharh al-Mawaqif. Do you not see how they wander in this issue of the unity of knowledge with the known like the bewildered in deserts, since they are upon blindness? And they are compelled to what they are compelled: that knowledge is not a single reality, that one thing is substance and quality, conceptualization and assent, and other corruptions, while they contradict themselves in explaining this issue. So understand. (It was said) in those glosses also: The scholars differed over whether words are placed for external objects or mental images, as passed earlier in the beginning of linguistic principles. So internal speech, if it is the import of verbal speech (as is well-known) and the case is that it is not an external thing (which is apparent), then it is nothing but the mental image, no more. (I say:) This is (refuted by the performative) type of speech, for demand is necessarily other than the conceptualization of the demand ratio. How could it be? One who conceptualizes a demand ratio in a strike is not called a demander of it; rather, one in whom the demand subsists is called that. And since it is, for it is other than conceptualization, it is certainly other than knowledge. This is a solid statement, no doubt about it. But the statement of this proponent apparently indicates that his statement is specific to declarative sentences. Unless it is said: the ratio subsisting in the soul of one about to declare is other than the conceptualization of the declarative ratio. But the sufficient in refutation is that the utmost that follows from what was mentioned is that internal speech is the image subsisting in the mind, and it does not necessitate that it be the same as knowledge. That would only follow if it were the image of the known, and it is not as you have learned. It cannot be said that the fact that the image subsisting in the soul is the meaning of verbal speech contradicts what has passed that words are placed for meanings per se, because what is meant by this subsisting being the meaning of verbal speech is that it is a meaning without consideration of its subsistence. So ponder. Then in al-Mukhtasar it was argued that it is a mental ratio because it depends on conceptualizing the two single terms, unlike the external ratio. (It was said) in the glosses: The necessary extent is perception of the two single terms, and it does not necessitate that they be obtained in the mind by their mental images so that conceptualization (i.e., being a conceptualization) is necessitated. Rather, it is possible that this perception is (knowledge by presence), so conceptualization—which is representational—is not necessitated. This is a rejoinder only if by conceptualization is meant this; but if absolute perception is meant, then not. And this latter meaning is common in such arts. (I say:) It is a representational ratio, and representation occurs only by the obtaining of an image of the represented, not by its own existence as in knowledge by presence, so it cannot be knowledge by presence. If you say: The soul's perception of itself and its attributes is knowledge by presence, and there is no harm in positing the linkage.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analytical expansion on the claim that the four fundamental sources of Sharia (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas) ultimately return to internal speech (kalam nafsi). It begins by noting the inclusion of istishab (presumption of continuity) as a proof according to some, but states that the Hanafi school does not accept istishab as a proof. The author then discusses a view reported from al-Amidi that each source corresponds to the internal speech of a particular entity: the Qur'an to Allah's internal speech, Sunnah to the Prophet's, Ijma to the consensus of the mujtahids, and Qiyas to the internal speech of the mujtahid. The author criticizes this view because internal speech of anyone other than Allah carries no authority; if it did, it would only be by reference back to Allah's speech. Moreover, in Qiyas, the mujtahid's own speech cannot be a proof upon himself. The passage then defines kalam nafsi as a mental ratio (nisba nafsiyya) that subsists in the soul, akin to a mental quality, mixed with the intention to inform. This ratio is distinct from the mental image (sura 'ilmiyya) because the latter may exist without the intention to inform. The author argues that this ratio is not a simple essence because it can be performative (insha'i) or informative (ikhbari), and those are different realities. Even within the same type, the ratio involves both relata, so it cannot be simple. The author also refutes the idea that internal speech is merely the mental image of the external ratio, arguing that performative speech like commands involves a demand (talab) that is other than the conceptualization of the demand. He further argues that if internal speech were knowledge by presence (ilm huduri), it could not be representational (hikaya) because representation requires an image of the represented, not the represented itself. The passage engages with several glosses and opposing views, ultimately defending the Ash'ari position that internal speech is distinct from knowledge and will, and that it is a composite of meanings rather than a simple reality.

Key Terms
النسبة النفسية (al-nisba al-nafsiyya): The mental ratio subsisting in the soul, which is the meaning of a proposition (e.g., 'Zayd is standing'). It is mixed with the intention to inform.
الصورة العلمية (al-sura al-'ilmiyya): The mental image or concept of an object; the form of the known in the mind. It may exist without the intention to inform.
الوجدان (al-wijdan): Consciousness or introspection; immediate self-awareness used as an epistemological tool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes kalam nafsi from a mental image (sura 'ilmiyya) according to the author?
A) Kalam nafsi is external while the mental image is internal.
B) Kalam nafsi is always mixed with the intention to inform, while a mental image can exist without that intention.
C) Kalam nafsi is a simple essence, while the mental image is composite.
D) The mental image is a ratio, while kalam nafsi is a quality.

Key Takeaway
Kalam nafsi is a mental ratio mixed with the intention to inform, distinct from mere mental imagery and from knowledge.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Refuting the Simplicity of Kalam Nafsi: The Argument from Performative Speech
Refutation of the simplicity of kalam nafsi using performative speech and ratio analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that kalam nafsi is a simple essence (basiṭa) by citing the variety of speech acts (performative vs. informative) and the requirement of two relata for a ratio.

Core Idea
Kalam nafsi cannot be simple because it involves a relation between two relata and can be performative or informative, each a different reality.

In this dense passage, the author tackles a key point of contention: is kalam nafsi a simple, indivisible reality or a composite? He argues forcefully that it cannot be simple. The evidence is twofold: first, a ratio (nisba) necessarily requires two relata, so it cannot be simple. Second, performative speech (insha'i) like commands involves a demand (talab) that is distinct from the conceptualization of a ratio, and this demand is a different type of mental content. The author also refutes the idea that internal speech is merely the mental image of the external ratio, using the performative counterexample. He then addresses a possible rejoinder that seeks to reduce kalam nafsi to knowledge, but he dismisses it as philosophical raving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two arguments against simplicity
First, a ratio requires two relata (e.g., subject and predicate), so it cannot be simple. Second, performative and informative speech have different realities; a single simple essence cannot encompass both.
Simplicity means no internal composition; but a relation is inherently composite.
2
Understand the performative counterexample
In a command (e.g., 'Stand!'), the internal speech includes a demand (talab). This is not a mere conceptualization of a ratio; it is a volitional element. Demand is other than the image of a demand.
One can conceptualize a demand without actually demanding it; internal speech of command includes actual demand.
3
Refute the objection that internal speech is the mental image of the external ratio
If internal speech were just the mental image of an external ratio, then for declarative sentences it might work, but for performatives there is no external ratio to image (e.g., a command does not describe an existing state).
The author says the opponent's view applies only to informatives, not to performatives.
4
Analyze the author's dismissal of the 'simple essence' view
The author labels the view that kalam nafsi is a simple essence as 'ravings of the philosophers' (hadiyanat al-falasifa) and rejects it as false, citing his own detailed refutation elsewhere.
Thestrong language indicates the author's firm stance: simplicity is untenable.

وأما اندراج الاستصحاب عند قائليه : فلأنه ليس إلا الاستدلال بالوجود على البقاء، فالوجود إن كان ثابتاً بالأدلة الأربعة فهي وإلا فلا عبرة به فتأمل فيه، وأما نحن فلا نحتاج إلى الجواب لعدم كونه حجة عندنا (ثم هذه الأصول الأربعة راجعة إلى كلام النفس) للباري عز وجل، فإنه هو الحاكم حقيقة بكلامه الأزلي هذه الدلائل كواشف عنه، وفي شرح المختصر مطابقاً لما نقل عن الآمدي أن الكتاب راجع إلى الكلام النفسي للباري الحق تعالى، والسنة إلى الكلام النفسي للرسول صلوات الله عليه وآله وأصحابه، والإجماع إلى النفسي للمجمعين، والقياس إلى النفسي للمجتهد، ولا يخفى بعد، فإن النفسي لما سوى الله تعالى لا حجة فيه أصلاً، ولو كانت فلأجل رجوعه إلى كلام الله تعالى مع أنه غير ظاهر في القياس، لأن المجتهد القائس كلامه ليس حجة عليه، بل المساواة النفس الأمرية، وإلا كان هو حاكماً على نفسه، ومقلده ليس حجة قياسه بل قوله فقط، وكذا ليس كلامه حجة على المجتهد الآخر، إذ لا يجوز له التقليد فافهم (وهو) أي كلام النفس (نسبة نفسية) قائمة بالنفس وكيفية ذهنية كالعلم والإرادة مجعولة معها مخلوطة بها إرادة إفادة المخاطب تلك النسبة بالضرورة الوجدانية فإنا إذا نراجع إلى وجداننا نعلم أن في أذهاننا نسبة تعلق إرادة إفادتها وليس عند تصور النسبة المفادة بكلام الغير النسبة المخلوطة معها الإرادة المذكورة، ثم الظاهر أن هذا تحقيق لمطلق الكلام النفسي الذي كلامه تعالى جزئي من جزئياته ففي هذا إشارة إلى أن الصفات الإلهية مجعولة، لكن المجعولية لا تكون إلا بالإيجاب فما وقع من المصنف فيما سبق أن الصفات واجبة بالذات فليست مجعولة ليس من مرضياته وإنما وقع مجاراة مع الخصم، ويمكن أن يكون تحقيقاً لكلام الإنسان النفسي ويقاس عليه كلامه تعالى والمراد بالجعل الجعل بالاختيار، وإذا ثبت بالوجدان اختلاط تلك النسبة بإرادة الإفادة دون الصورة العلمية فإنها قد تكون من غير تلك الإرادة فجاءت النسبة المذكورة حقيقة غير الصورة (العلمية وهذه النسبة كالكيفيات السارية في (الكميات وإذا ثبتت المغايرة فاندفع ما قيل في حواشي ميرزاجان تحقق نسبة في زيد قائم مغايرة لمفهوم الأخبار) وهي الحكاية وللنسبة الواقعية التي بينهما) وهي المحكى عنه ( وللصورة العلمية القائمة بالذهن الحاصلة منها مما يكذبه (الوجدان فإنه لا توجد نسبة إذا إلى الوجدان، وقيل فيها أيضاً الحق أنها هي الصورة العلمية للنسبة الخارجية من حيث روجع إفادة الكلام فهي من حيث إنها في الواقع نسبة خارجية ومن حيث إنها صورة مطابقة لها علم، ومن حيث إنها مفاد بالكلام كلام نفسي هذا ويحوم حوله ما نقله علي القاري رحمه الله في شرح الفقه الأكبر عن الإمام حجة الإسلام قدس سره أن الكلام النفسي حصة من العلم، ومعنى تكلم الله مع من اصطفاه جعله مطلعاً على علومه تعالى هذا: (نعم إثبات كونها حقيقة بسيطة غير العلم والإرادة عسير لا أنه باطل بالوجدان (فافهم ) أما كونها حقيقة بسيطة أصلاً، فإن هذه النسبة مدلول الكلام اللفظي على ما يعطى كلمات متأخري فلا يكاد يصح الأشعرية، وهي قد تكون إنشائية طلبية ،وغيرها، وقد تكون إخبارية وكلها متخالفة الحقيقة، فأين البساطة، وهل هذا إلا كما يقال : إن أمراً واحداً بسيطاً قد يكون فرساً، وقد يكون إنساناً قلت : لا أو باعتبار التعلقات ثم إن وجود النسبة وحدها من غير أن يكون معها المنتسبان غير معقول، وإذا كان فيما بين المنتسبين فلا تصح البساطة أصلاً، بل الذي يعقل على تقدير كون الكلام النفسي عبارة عن مدلول اللفظي هو المعاني الملحوظة بينها النسب الإنشائية أو الإخبارية المرتبة، حسب ترتب الألفاظ القائمة بالنفس، أو بذات الباري عز وجل وهي مغايرة للعلم بل هو متعلق بها لا غير، وكذا للإرادة بل هي متعلقة بإفادتها وأما عسر معرفة مغايرته إياهما فللاختلاط، فإن يصح أيضاً مغايرته للعلم ولا يتجاوز الحق عما قال هذا القائل، فإن هذه المعاني أو هذا الأمر البسيط مدلول اللفظي على ما ينادي ظواهر العبارات، فهي صورة قائمة بذات الباري أو النفس والعلم هو حصول صورة المعلوم للعالم ،قلت هذا هو الذي شجع هذا القائل على ما قال : لكنك عسيت أن لا ترتاب في أن هذا من هذيانات الفلاسفة، ولا نساعد عليه البتة، بل هو باطل محض على ما برهنا عليه في تعليقاتنا المتعلقة بشرح المواقف، ألم ترهم كيف يسيرون في هذه المسألة اتحاد العلم بالمعلوم كالحيارى في الصحارى لما كانوا على عمياء ولزمهم ما لزمهم من عدم كون العلم حقيقة واحدة، وكون شيء واحد جوهراً وكيفاً وتصوراً وتصديقاً وغير ذلك من المفاسد وهم يناقضون أنفسهم في تبيان هذه المسألة فافهم (قيل) في تلك الحواشي أيضاً : العلماء اختلفوا في أن الألفاظ موضوعة للأمر الخارجي للصورة الذهنية كما مر في صدر المبادىء اللغوية فالنفسي إذا كان مفاد للفظي) كما اشتهر (و) الحال أنه لا يكون أمراً خارجياً) وهو ظاهر لم يكن إلا الصورة العلمية) لا غير (أقول) هذا (منقوض بالإنشائي) من الكلام فإن الطلب غير تصور النسبة الطلبية ضرورة) كيف ومن تصور النسبة الطلبية في أضرب لا يسمى طالباً له وإنما يسمى به من قام الطلب به، وإذا كان له، مغايراً للتصور كان غير العلم قطعاً هذا كلام متين لا شك فيه لكن كلام هذا القائل بظاهره يدل على أن قوله مخصوص بالأخبار، اللهم إلا أن يقال : النسبة القائمة بنفس من في صدد الأخبار غير تصور النسبة الإخبارية بل الوافي في دفعه أن غاية ما لزم مما ذكر أن النفسي هو الصورة القائمة بالذهن، ولا يلزم منه أن يكون عين العلم، وإنما يلزم لو كان عبارة عن الصورة من المعلوم وليس كما علمت لا يقال أن كون الصورة القائمة بالنفس مدلول الكلام اللفظي ينافي ما قد مر أن الألفاظ موضوعة للمعاني من حيث هي لأن المراد من كون هذا القائم مدلول اللفظي كونه مدلولاً مع قطع النظر عن القيام فتدبر فيه ثم استدل في المختصر على أنها نسبة ذهنية بأنها متوقفة على تعقل المفردين بخلاف النسبة الخارجية قيل) في الحواشي : القدر الضروري إدراك المفردين ولا يلزم منه أن يكون حصولهما في الذهن بصورهما العقلية حتى يلزم التعقل أي كونه تعقلاً بل يجوز أن يكون هذا الإدراك (علماً حضورياً فلا يلزم التعقل، لأنه عبارة عن الحصولي، وهذا إنما يرد لو أريد بالتعقل هذا، أما لو أريد مطلق الإدراك فلا وهذه الإرادة شائعة في أمثال هذه الفنون (أقول : إنها نسبة حاكية، والحكاية إنما تكون بحصول صورة المحكي لا بوجوده بنفسه كما في العلم الحضوري، فلا يصح كونه حضورياً، فإن قلت إدراك النفس وصفاتها حضوري ولا بعد في إيقاع الربط
And as for the inclusion of istishab according to its proponents: it is nothing but inference from existence to continuation. So if the existence is established by the four proofs, then it is valid; otherwise, it is disregarded. Ponder this. As for us, we do not need to answer because it is not a proof in our school. Then these four principles return to the internal speech (kalam nafsi) of Allah Almighty, for He is the true judge by His eternal speech, and these proofs are revealers of it. In Sharh al-Mukhtasar, in agreement with what is transmitted from al-Amidi, the Book returns to the internal speech of Allah the Exalted, the Sunnah to the internal speech of the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family and companions), Ijma to the internal speech of the mujtami'un, and Qiyas to the internal speech of the mujtahid. This is not subtle: for internal speech of anyone other than Allah is not a proof at all, and if it were, it would be because it returns to the speech of Allah, whereas it is not apparent in Qiyas, because the speech of the mujtahid who performs qiyas is not a proof upon him; rather, the equality is in the internal reality. Otherwise, he would be a judge over himself, and his follower's proof is not his qiyas but only his statement. And likewise, his speech is not a proof on another mujtahid, since he is not allowed to do taqlid. So understand. (And it) i.e., internal speech (is a mental ratio) subsisting in the soul, a mental quality like knowledge and will, created with them mixed with them, along with the intention of informing the addressee of that ratio, by existential necessity. For when we refer to our consciousness, we know that in our minds there is a ratio attached to an intention to inform it, and when we conceptualize the ratio conveyed by another's speech, we do not have the ratio mixed with that intention. Then it is apparent that this is a verification of absolute internal speech, of which the speech of Allah is a particular instance. In this there is an indication that divine attributes are created, but creation (ja'l) is only by necessity. So what the author mentioned earlier, that attributes are self-necessary and not created, is not from his sound opinions; rather it was a concession to the opponent. And it can be a verification of human internal speech, and the speech of Allah is analogized to it. By creation (ja'l) is meant creation by choice. And since it is established by consciousness that that ratio is mixed with the intention to inform, unlike the mental image, for it can be without that intention, therefore the mentioned ratio is truly other than the mental image. And this ratio is like qualities flowing in quantities. And when the difference is established, what was said in the glosses of Mirzajan is repelled: that a ratio in 'Zayd is standing' is different from the concept of the sentence—which is the narrative—and from the real ratio between them—which is the narrated—and from the mental image subsisting in the mind obtained from them, which the consciousness denies, for no ratio enters consciousness. And it is also said therein that the truth is that it is the mental image of the external ratio insofar as it is considered the import of speech. So it is, insofar as it is in reality an external ratio, and insofar as it is an image matching it, knowledge, and insofar as it is a speech-import, internal speech. This is a view, and around it is what 'Ali al-Qari (rahimahullah) transmitted in Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar from Imam Hujjat al-Islam (may Allah sanctify his secret) that internal speech is a portion of knowledge, and the meaning of Allah speaking to whomever He chooses is making him aware of His knowledge. This is so. (Yes, establishing that it is a simple essence, distinct from knowledge and will, is difficult, not that it is false by consciousness. (So understand.) As for its being a simple essence at all: this ratio, the meaning of verbal speech according to later scholars, the Ash'ari view can hardly be correct: it may be performative-demanding and other, and may be informative, and all these are heterogeneous in reality. So where is simplicity? Is this not like saying a single simple thing may be a horse and may be a human? I say: no, or by consideration of relations. Then the existence of the ratio alone without the two relata is inconceivable, and since it is between the two relata, simplicity is not valid at all. Rather, what is conceivable, assuming that internal speech is the meaning of verbal speech, is the meanings among which are the performative or informative ratios arranged according to the arrangement of words, subsisting in the soul or in the essence of Allah Almighty, and they are distinct from knowledge—rather knowledge is related to them—and likewise distinct from will—rather will is related to their communication. As for the difficulty of knowing its distinction from them, it is due to mixture. So it is also possible that it is distinct from knowledge, and the truth does not go beyond what this proponent said. For these meanings or this simple thing is the meaning of verbal speech as the apparent expressions indicate, so they are an image subsisting in the essence of Allah or the soul, and knowledge is the obtaining of the image of the known for the knower. I say: This is what emboldened this proponent to say what he said. But you should not doubt that this is from the ravings of the philosophers, and we do not support it at all; rather it is pure falsehood, as we demonstrated in our glosses on Sharh al-Mawaqif. Do you not see how they wander in this issue of the unity of knowledge with the known like the bewildered in deserts, since they are upon blindness? And they are compelled to what they are compelled: that knowledge is not a single reality, that one thing is substance and quality, conceptualization and assent, and other corruptions, while they contradict themselves in explaining this issue. So understand. (It was said) in those glosses also: The scholars differed over whether words are placed for external objects or mental images, as passed earlier in the beginning of linguistic principles. So internal speech, if it is the import of verbal speech (as is well-known) and the case is that it is not an external thing (which is apparent), then it is nothing but the mental image, no more. (I say:) This is (refuted by the performative) type of speech, for demand is necessarily other than the conceptualization of the demand ratio. How could it be? One who conceptualizes a demand ratio in a strike is not called a demander of it; rather, one in whom the demand subsists is called that. And since it is, for it is other than conceptualization, it is certainly other than knowledge. This is a solid statement, no doubt about it. But the statement of this proponent apparently indicates that his statement is specific to declarative sentences. Unless it is said: the ratio subsisting in the soul of one about to declare is other than the conceptualization of the declarative ratio. But the sufficient in refutation is that the utmost that follows from what was mentioned is that internal speech is the image subsisting in the mind, and it does not necessitate that it be the same as knowledge. That would only follow if it were the image of the known, and it is not as you have learned. It cannot be said that the fact that the image subsisting in the soul is the meaning of verbal speech contradicts what has passed that words are placed for meanings per se, because what is meant by this subsisting being the meaning of verbal speech is that it is a meaning without consideration of its subsistence. So ponder. Then in al-Mukhtasar it was argued that it is a mental ratio because it depends on conceptualizing the two single terms, unlike the external ratio. (It was said) in the glosses: The necessary extent is perception of the two single terms, and it does not necessitate that they be obtained in the mind by their mental images so that conceptualization (i.e., being a conceptualization) is necessitated. Rather, it is possible that this perception is (knowledge by presence), so conceptualization—which is representational—is not necessitated. This is a rejoinder only if by conceptualization is meant this; but if absolute perception is meant, then not. And this latter meaning is common in such arts. (I say:) It is a representational ratio, and representation occurs only by the obtaining of an image of the represented, not by its own existence as in knowledge by presence, so it cannot be knowledge by presence. If you say: The soul's perception of itself and its attributes is knowledge by presence, and there is no harm in positing the linkage.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analytical expansion on the claim that the four fundamental sources of Sharia (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas) ultimately return to internal speech (kalam nafsi). It begins by noting the inclusion of istishab (presumption of continuity) as a proof according to some, but states that the Hanafi school does not accept istishab as a proof. The author then discusses a view reported from al-Amidi that each source corresponds to the internal speech of a particular entity: the Qur'an to Allah's internal speech, Sunnah to the Prophet's, Ijma to the consensus of the mujtahids, and Qiyas to the internal speech of the mujtahid. The author criticizes this view because internal speech of anyone other than Allah carries no authority; if it did, it would only be by reference back to Allah's speech. Moreover, in Qiyas, the mujtahid's own speech cannot be a proof upon himself. The passage then defines kalam nafsi as a mental ratio (nisba nafsiyya) that subsists in the soul, akin to a mental quality, mixed with the intention to inform. This ratio is distinct from the mental image (sura 'ilmiyya) because the latter may exist without the intention to inform. The author argues that this ratio is not a simple essence because it can be performative (insha'i) or informative (ikhbari), and those are different realities. Even within the same type, the ratio involves both relata, so it cannot be simple. The author also refutes the idea that internal speech is merely the mental image of the external ratio, arguing that performative speech like commands involves a demand (talab) that is other than the conceptualization of the demand. He further argues that if internal speech were knowledge by presence (ilm huduri), it could not be representational (hikaya) because representation requires an image of the represented, not the represented itself. The passage engages with several glosses and opposing views, ultimately defending the Ash'ari position that internal speech is distinct from knowledge and will, and that it is a composite of meanings rather than a simple reality.

Key Terms
الإنشائي (al-insha'i): Performative speech: utterances that create a new reality (e.g., commands, prohibitions, contracts). Contrasted with informative speech (ikhbari) which describes reality.
الطلب (al-talab): Demand: the mental content in a command that urges the action. Distinct from conceptualization of the action.
البساطة (al-basata): Simplicity: the property of having no internal parts. The author argues kalam nafsi is not simple.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a reason given by the author for rejecting the simplicity of kalam nafsi?
A) A ratio requires two relata.
B) Performative and informative speech have different realities.
C) Consciousness clearly shows internal speech is composite.
D) The author has a personal dislike for philosophers.

Key Takeaway
Internal speech cannot be simple because it involves a relation between two relata and encompasses distinct types (performative and informative) with different realities.

The Basmalah: Its Status and Ruling in Khatm
Hanafi ruling on basmalah as a single verse and its necessity in khatm Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the basmalah as a Quranic verse and apply it to the obligation of recitation during khatm al-Qur'an.

Core Idea
The basmalah is one independent verse of the Quran, not part of any surah, and must be recited once in a complete khatm.

This lesson clarifies the legal status of the basmalah (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim) within the Hanafi school. Understanding whether it is part of the Quran, and whether it belongs to a surah, directly affects the obligation of reciting it when completing the Quran (khatm). The passage also briefly contrasts the Hanafi view with the Maliki and Shafi'i positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Extract from the passage the precise definition: 'al-basmalah min al-Qur'an ayah wahidah' – the basmalah is one verse of the Quran, not part of any surah.
This is the foundational premise for all subsequent rules.
2
Understand the implication for khatm
Because the basmalah is an independent verse, an oath to complete the Quran (khatm) requires reciting it once. The text states: 'la tabarru' al-dhimmah' – the obligation is not discharged without it.
Contrast with reciting basmalah before each surah, which is not required.
3
Contrast with other schools
Note that the Maliki school denies the basmalah is Quranic at all, while the Shafi'i school considers it part of each surah except Bara'ah. The disagreement applies only to basmalah at the beginnings of surahs, not to the verse in Surah al-Naml (27:30).
This highlights the Hanafi specificity and the practical difference in recitation frequency.
4
Apply to taraweeh practice
The text extends the ruling to taraweeh prayers: the basmalah should be recited aloud once during the khatm in taraweeh, and the sunnah of khatm is not achieved without it.
This is a direct application of the definition to a common communal practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(مسألة: البسملة من القرآن آية واحدة فتقرأ في الختم مرة) فمن نذر أن يختم القرآن يجب عليه قراءة البسملة مرة واحدة ولا تخلص الذمة بدون قراءتها إن قرأ القرآن دونها، وعلى هذا ينبغي أن يقرأها في التراويح بالجهر مرة ولا تتأدى سنة الختم دونها (وليست) جزءاً من السورة ، وقيل : ليست جزءاً (منه) أي القرآن أصلاً، وعليه أصحاب مالك (وقيل) هي جزء (منها) أي من السورة إلا من سورة براءة، ومحل الخلاف البسملة التي في أوائل السور لا
(Issue: The basmalah is one verse of the Quran; it is recited once in the khatm). So whoever vows to complete the Quran must recite the basmalah once, and his obligation is not fulfilled without reciting it if he recites the Quran without it. Accordingly, he should recite it aloud once in taraweeh, and the sunnah of khatm is not achieved without it. (And it is not) a part of the surah, and it is said: it is not a part of it (the Quran) at all, and upon this are the followers of Malik. (And it is said) it is a part (of it) i.e., of the surah, except for Surah Bara'ah. And the subject of disagreement is the basmalah that is at the beginnings of surahs, not...
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling (mas'alah) from the matn of Musallam al-Thubut, stating the Hanafi position on basmalah. The basmalah (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim) is one independent verse of the Quran, but it is not part of any surah. Therefore, when completing a full recitation of the Quran (khatm), one must recite the basmalah once (presumably at the beginning of the recitation or before starting a new surah). The text notes that some (Malikis) hold it is not part of the Quran at all, while others say it is part of each surah except Bara'ah (al-Tawbah). The disagreement only concerns the basmalah at the beginnings of surahs, not the one in Surah al-Naml (which is part of that verse).

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' as a single verse of the Quran, not part of any surah.
ختم القرآن (khatm al-Qur'an): Completing the recitation of the entire Quran from beginning to end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position stated in the text, what is the status of the basmalah in relation to the Quran?
A) It is part of every surah except Bara'ah.
B) It is one independent verse of the Quran, not part of any surah.
C) It is not part of the Quran at all.
D) It is part of Surah al-Fatihah only.

Key Takeaway
The basmalah is one independent Quranic verse that must be recited once during a complete khatm.

The Quran Contains No Useless or Ambiguous Words
Refuting claims that the Quran contains meaningless or redundant expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-muhmal and al-hashw in Hanafi usul, and apply the Hanafi argument that the Quran is free from both by classifying questionable expressions as mutashabihat or tawkid.

Core Idea
The Quran is free from meaningless words (muhmal) and useless repetition (hashw); all expressions serve a purpose.

One of the foundational beliefs of the Hanafi school is that the Quran is perfect in eloquence and free from any defect. This lesson addresses two types of defects that some groups have claimed exist in the Quran: muhmal (words with no meaning) and hashw (useless additions). We will examine the definitions, the claims of the Hashwiyya, and the Hanafi response using the concepts of mutashabihat and tawkid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claims being refuted
The passage states that the Quran contains no muhmal and no hashw. Understand what each claim implies about the Quran's perfection.
2
Define muhmal and hashw
Muhmal is a word that conveys no meaning literally or figuratively. Hashw is an addition that provides no benefit. Note that both are considered defects in speech.
These definitions are crucial for understanding the Hanafi position.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
The theological proof: speaking with imperfection (like muhmal or hashw) is impossible for Allah, therefore such defects cannot occur in the Quran.
This is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on Allah's perfection.
4
Examine the Hashwiyya's examples
The Hashwiyya claimed the disjointed letters (huruf muqatta'at) are muhmal because they don't indicate their usual linguistic meanings. They also claimed the phrase 'ilāhainithnain' (two gods, two) is hashw due to repetition.
Identify the exact examples: the huruf muqatta'at and the verse 16:51.
5
Apply the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response classifies huruf muqatta'at as mutashabihat (with hidden meaning) and the repetition as tawkid (emphasis). Thus neither qualifies as muhmal or hashw.
Understand how the categories of mutashabihat and tawkid preserve the Quran's perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : لا يشتمل القرآن على المهمل وهو الذي لم يدل على معنى لا حقيقة ولا مجازاً (و) لا على (الحشو) وهو الزيادة من غير فائدة خلافاً للحشوية، لنا : التكلم به نقص مستحيل عليه تعالى فلا يصح الوقوع أصلاً ، الحشوية قالوا فيه الحروف المقطعة) ولم يقصد مدلولاتها اللغوية ولا غيرها، فصارت مهملة (و) فيه (نحو إِلَهَيْنِ اثْنينِ ﴾ [النحل : ٥١]) والثاني مكرر لا فائدة فيه قلنا : الأول من الألفاظ (المتشابهة) فله معنى خفي لا يرجى الوقوف عليه لأحد أو لغير الراسخين فليس مهملاً الثاني من (التأكيد) أي من قبيله، وتقرير ما قبله لا التأكيد النحوي، ولا يخفى ما فيه من الفوائد، فلا حشو فافهم.
Issue: The Quran does not contain the muhmal, which is that which does not indicate a meaning neither literally nor figuratively, nor does it contain al-hashw, which is an increase without benefit, contrary to the Hashwiyya. For us: Speaking with it is an imperfection impossible for Him, exalted, so its occurrence is not valid at all. The Hashwiyya said: There are in it the disconnected letters, and they did not intend their linguistic meanings nor others, so they became muhmal. And in it (like 'two gods, two') [al-Nahl 16:51] and the second is a repetition with no benefit. We said: The first is from the mutashabihat (ambiguous) terms, so it has a hidden meaning that cannot be hoped to be known by anyone or by other than the firmly grounded, so it is not muhmal. The second is from takid (emphasis), i.e., of its kind, confirming what precedes it, not the grammatical emphasis. And the benefits in it are not hidden, so there is no hashw, so understand.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of two Quranic principles: that the Quran contains no muhmal (words with no meaning, literal or figurative) and no hashw (useless additions). The author refutes the Hashwiyya (a group accused of holding such views) who claimed that the disjointed letters (huruf muqatta'ah) are muhmal, and that phrases like 'ilāhainithnain' (two gods, two) are redundant. The response is twofold: the first are mutashabihat (ambiguous) with a hidden meaning understandable only to the firmly grounded, thus not muhmal; the second is emphasis (takid) which reinforces the preceding statement, serving a rhetorical benefit. Therefore, the Quran is free from any deficiency or superfluity.

Key Terms
المهمل (al-muhmal): A word that does not indicate any meaning, either literally or figuratively.
الحشو (al-hashw): An addition to speech that provides no benefit.
المتشابه (al-mutashabih): A term with a hidden meaning not easily understood, in this context referring to the huruf muqatta'at.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how is the phrase 'ilāhainithnain' (two gods, two) in Surah al-Nahl explained?
A) It is an example of grammatical error corrected by later scholars
B) It is an example of hashw (useless redundancy)
C) It is an example of tawkid (emphasis) with a clear benefit
D) It is a mutashabih term with no known meaning

Key Takeaway
The Quran is free from meaningless words and useless repetition; apparent cases are explained as mutashabihat or tawkid, preserving the perfection of divine speech.

Ruling on a Qualified Command: Condition Becomes Obligatory
Rule in usul al-fiqh: effect of a qualified command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a qualified command makes the condition obligatory and the act without it prohibited, and identify the reasoning from al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
When a mubah act is commanded with a condition, observing the condition is wajib and the act without it is haram.

This lesson explores a fundamental principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: how a command (amr) that is qualified by a condition (qayd) transforms the ruling. The act itself is originally permissible, but the command redirects its permissibility to the condition, making the condition obligatory and the act without it forbidden. We will see how this applies to the Quranic command regarding the number of wives.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rule
Identify the rule: when a mubah act is commanded with a condition, observing the condition is wajib and performing the act without the condition is haram.
The act is originally mubah, but the command diverts its permissibility to the condition.
2
Identify the basis
The command (amr) inherently indicates obligation. Since the act is mubah, the obligation attaches to the condition, making the condition wajib and the act without it haram.
This is supported by statements of the author of al-Hidayah in multiple places.
3
Apply to the marriage example
The Quranic command to marry with a specified number (4:3) qualifies the act of marriage. Thus, observing the number is wajib and marrying beyond it is haram.
The passage argues that the verse was revealed to establish this obligation, not mere permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحق أن يقال: إن الحكم الذي يكون مباحاً إذا قيد بقيد وأمر به يكون مراعاة القيد واجبة، فيحرم ذلك الفعل مع ترك القيد وقد صرح به صاحب الهداية في مواضع عديدة منها في باب الربا والسرقة أن حقيقة الأمر للوجوب، والفعل المتعلق به الأمر لما كان مباحاً انصرف إلى قيده، فيكون إتيان القيد واجباً وترك القيد أي اتيانه مجرداً عن القيد بل في ضمن مقيد آخر حراماً قطعاً، وههنا قد أمر بنكاح مقيد بالعدد فيكون مراعاته واجبة ويحرم الزيادة عليه، والنص سيق لهذا الإيجاب، لأن نفس الحل لكونه ظاهراً في الدين لا يصلح للمقصودية، وأيضاً إنه عدول عن الحقيقة من غير قرينة وباعث مع أن شأن النزول أيضاً يقتضي أن سوقها لإيجاب الله العدد كما لا يخفى على من تتبع كتب التفسير، وهو مراد من قال : إن بيان العدد لا يتم إلا بأن تكون الزيادة منفية، فافهم وإن خفي مراده
And the truth is to say: When a ruling that is permissible (mubah) is qualified by a condition and commanded, then observing the condition becomes obligatory, and that act without the condition becomes prohibited. The author of al-Hidayah has explicitly stated in many places, including in the chapters of riba and theft, that the reality of a command is for obligation, and the act connected to the command, since it was permissible, is diverted to its condition, so performing the condition becomes obligatory and abandoning the condition – i.e., performing it stripped of the condition, or within another qualified [act] – is absolutely prohibited. And here, marriage has been commanded qualified by number, so observing it becomes obligatory and exceeding it is prohibited. The text was brought for this obligation, because the mere permissibility, being apparent in the religion, is not suitable for being the intended purpose. Also, it would be a departure from the literal meaning without a contextual indicator and motive, while the occasion of revelation also requires that its context is for Allah to obligate the number, as is not hidden from one who studies the books of tafsir. And that is what is meant by one who said: The clarification of the number is not complete unless the increase is negated. So understand, even if his intention is hidden.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a rule of usul al-fiqh regarding the nature of a command that is qualified by a condition. The author begins by stating the rule: when an act is originally permissible (mubah) but is then commanded with a specific condition (qayd), observing that condition becomes wajib (obligatory), and performing the act without that condition becomes haram (prohibited). He supports this by citing the authority of al-Hidayah, which affirms that the essence of a command (amr) is obligation. The act itself, being mubah, is directed to its condition, making the condition obligatory. The application given is the command to marry with a specified number (e.g., four wives in Quran 4:3). The command to marry is qualified by the condition of not exceeding the number, so respecting that number is wajib and marrying more is haram. The passage argues that the verse was revealed to establish this obligation, not merely to permit. It refutes the idea that the purpose was only to state permissibility, because permissibility is already well-known and does not require emphasis. The context of revelation (sha'n al-nuzul) supports that the intent is obligation. The lesson concludes by emphasizing that the clarification of the number is not complete without negating the increase.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): The command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) according to the Hanafi school.
القيد (al-qayd): A condition attached to a command that restricts the act and must be fulfilled.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Legal obligation that must be fulfilled; failure incurs sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle discussed, when Allah commands an act that is originally mubah with a condition, what is the ruling on performing the act without that condition?
A) It remains mubah.
B) It becomes haram.
C) It becomes wajib.
D) It becomes makruh.

Key Takeaway
When a command is qualified, the condition is wajib and the act without the condition is haram.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
