12 min
Al-Khafi: Obscure Text and the Thief Example
Defines al-khafi and applies it to the thief example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a text as al-khafi, explain why the pickpocket is included in the verse of theft while the grave robber is not, and apply the Hanafi rule of al-khafi to similar cases.

Core Idea
A text clear in its general meaning can be obscure in some individuals due to an external cause—the pickpocket is a thief; the grave robber is not.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi usul category of al-khafi—a text that is apparent (zahir) in its general meaning but becomes obscure in some particular applications due to an external factor. The classic example is the word 'thief' in the Quranic verse on amputation (5:38). While the verse is clear, its application to the pickpocket (tarrar) and grave robber (nabbash) is initially uncertain because each has a distinct name. By analyzing the definition of theft, we discover that the pickpocket is a complete thief but the grave robber is not, leading to different rulings. This lesson sharpens your ability to parse textual categories and apply them to real legal cases.

Guided Path
1
Define al-khafi
Start with the definition: a text that is clear (zahir) but becomes obscure in some of its individuals due to an external cause, not the wording itself. The obscurity is less than that of al-khafi's counterpart, al-mushkil.
Memorize the key: 'zahir in meaning, khafi in application'.
2
Identify the source text
The Quranic verse (5:38) provides the general word 'thief' (al-sariq). The verse is apparent in its ruling, but its application to specific individuals can be obscure.
We are dealing with istinbat from a nass.
3
Analyze the pickpocket and grave robber
Check each against the legal definition of theft: taking secretly from a secure place (hirz). The pickpocket meets all conditions; the grave robber does not (no hirz, no secrecy from the living, weak ownership of the deceased).
This is tahqiq al-manat.
4
Understand the source of obscurity
The obscurity arises because each has a distinct name (tarrar, nabbash) used in contrast to 'thief', causing doubt. The author distinguishes between specification that contrasts with the general term (causing doubt) and specification that does not.
Contrast with 'stone' and 'tree', which are still clearly 'bodies'.
5
Derive the ruling
The pickpocket is explicitly included under 'thief' by the wording (dalalah), so hadd applies. The grave robber is not included, so no hadd. This shows how al-khafi is resolved through reflection (ta'ammul) on the meaning.
This is the practical outcome of the usul analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معطوف على قوله : إن ظهر (فأما) يكون خفاؤه (لعارض) غير الصيغة (فهو الخفي وهو أقل خفاء كالظاهر أقل (ظهوراً، وقد يجتمعان) فيما إذا كان المدلول ظاهر، أو يكون الخفاء في بعض أفراده ( كالسارق ظاهر في مفهومه الشرعي بل اللغوي فإن السرقة لغة وشرعاً أخذ مال الغير خفية من حرز (خفي في الطرار والنباش للاختصاص) أي لاختصاص كل (باسم) غير اسم السارق، فيختفي السارق فيهما، فيختفي الحكم (لكن بتأمل ما يظهر أن في الأول زيادة) في السرقة، لأنه يأخذ أشد (فيجب الحد وهو القطع (و) يظهر أن في الثاني نقصاناً) في السرقة، لأن الاختفاء لا يكون من الميت فلا يجب الحد واعترض أولاً بأن اختصاص بعض الأنواع باسم لا يورث الخفاء في إطلاق الجنس، فاختصاص الحجر والشجر باسم لا يورث الخفاء في إطلاق الجسم وهكذا، وثانياً بأنه هل هما من أفراد السارق أم لا؟ على الأول: يجب خفياً كان أم لا، وعلى الثاني : لا يجب الحد ولا خفاء والحق في تحقيق المقام أن يقال: إن معنى السرقة معلوم، ويزعم في باديء الرأي أن الطرار والنباش من أفراده حقيقة، ثم اختصاص كل منهما باسم خاص يورث الشبهة فيه، بل يوجب أن يكونا غير السارق، فإذا تأمل علم أن الطرار من الأفراد الكاملة للسارق بوجود السرقة فيه على الكمال واختصاصه كاختصاص بعض أنواع الجنس بالاسم فوجب الحد بعموم السارق إياه عبارة والنباش لما علم عدم وجود معنى السرقة فيه لعدم الحرز وعدم وجود الخفية وعدم الملك التام لأن المالك للكفن الميت وملكه ضعيف لا اعتداد به فلم يدخل في عموم السارق، فلا يجب الحد لعدم الدليل. والمراد بالخفاء في التعريف هو الخفاء في بعض الأفراد لعروض عارض، فالحاصل أنه إنما حد الطرار لكونه سارقاً حقيقة، ولم يحد النباش لكونه غير سارق حقيقة، فلم تتناوله الآية، إلاّ أنه علم بتأمل. واعلم أن الإمام فخر الإسلام بعدما بين أن النباش لا يأخذ من مال حافظ ولا ماله خطر قال : وهذا الذي دل عليه اسم النباش في غاية القصور والهوان، والتعدية بمثله في الحدود خاصة باطلة ؛ وقال بعدما بين فضل الجناية في الطرّار وهذه السرقة في غاية الكمال وتعدية الحدود في مثله في نهاية الصحة والاستقامة، فقال صاحب الكشف»: لم يرد بالتعدية الحد المتبادر، وهو اطراد حكم الأصل في الفرع بالقياس، بل أراد بالتعدية اطراد الحكم بالدلالة، فإن ثبوت الحكم في الطرار بالدلالة ولا تستقيم هذه الدلالة في النباش لضعف المناط، وتبعه صاحب «التحرير»، وليس الأمر كما ظنه هذا الحبر، فإنه قد أثبت هذا الإمام وجود مفهوم السرقة في الطرار على الكمال وهذا يوجب تناول الصيغة عبارة، فلا وجه للدلالة، مع أن ضعف المناط أيضاً لا يوجب انتفاء الدلالة في النباش، بل الحق أن مراد هذا الإمام بالتعدية المعنى اللغوي، وهو اطراد الحكم ومقصوده أنه لما وجد الأخذ خفية في الطرار على الكمال اطرد حكم السارق وتعدى إليه وثبت فيه عبارة وهذا في غاية الحسن والاستقامة، وأما النباش فلما لم يوجد فيه المعنى على الكمال قيوداته من الحرز وكون بجميع المأخوذ ذا خطر لم يتناوله اسم السارق، فالتعدية أي سراية الحكم إليه في غاية الضعف، بعدم دلالة العبارة ؛ وهل هذا إلا كما تعدى حكم الإنسان في الفرس لوجود الحيوانية، فافهم والجواب عن الأول : أنه فرق بين الاختصاص الذي فيهما واختصاص أنواع جنس واحد، فإن الاختصاص فيهما بحيث يطلق كل منهما في مقابلة السارق حتى يقال : هذا طرار وهذا سارق أو نباش، فعلم بالتأمل أن معنى المثال المضروب أنه ليس سارقاً ضعيفاً، بل قوياً، وأنه من أفراده، بخلاف أنواع الجنس، فإنه لا يطلق في مقابلة الجنس أصلاً، والمورث للشبهة هو الاختصاص الأول دون هذا هذا غاية الكلام في هذا المقام احفظه فإنه دقيق
Connected to his saying: 'If it appears (then) its obscurity is due to an accidental cause not the wording, then it is al-khafi, and it is less obscure just as the apparent is less apparent. And they may combine when the indicated meaning is apparent, or the obscurity may be in some of its individuals – like 'thief' is apparent in its legal and even linguistic meaning, because theft linguistically and legally is taking the property of another secretly from a secure place – but it is obscure in the pickpocket and grave robber due to specification, i.e., each is specified by a name other than the name 'thief', so 'thief' becomes obscure in them, and thus the ruling becomes obscure. But upon reflection, it appears that in the first there is an increase in theft because he takes more severely, so the hadd (amputation) is obligatory; and in the second there is a decrease in theft because concealment does not occur from the dead, so the hadd is not obligatory. An objection was raised: first, that specification of some types by a name does not cause obscurity in the application of the genus; e.g., specification of stone and tree by names does not cause obscurity in the application of 'body'. Second, whether these two are individuals of 'thief' or not? If yes, the hadd is obligatory whether obscure or not; if not, then no hadd and no obscurity. The truth in investigating this matter is to say: The meaning of theft is known, and at first glance one claims that the pickpocket and grave robber are truly its individuals. Then each being specified by a particular name causes doubt, even makes them seem not thieves. Upon reflection, one knows that the pickpocket is a complete individual of thief because theft exists in him completely, and his specification is like the specification of some types of a genus by a name, so the hadd is obligatory by the generality of 'thief' via explicit wording. As for the grave robber, since the meaning of theft is not present due to lack of secure place, lack of concealment, and lack of complete ownership because the owner of the shroud is the deceased and his ownership is weak and not considered, he is not included in the generality of 'thief', so the hadd is not obligatory for lack of proof. What is meant by obscurity in the definition is obscurity in some individuals due to an accidental cause. The conclusion is that the pickpocket is punished because he is truly a thief, and the grave robber is not punished because he is not truly a thief, so the verse does not include him, but this is known through reflection. Know that Imam Fakhr al-Islam, after explaining that the grave robber does not take from protected property nor is his property significant, said: 'What the name grave robber indicates is of extreme deficiency and lowliness, and extending (ta'diya) the like in hudud is specifically invalid.' And after explaining the excellence of the crime in the pickpocket and that this theft is in extreme perfection, he said: 'Extending hudud in such a case is of utmost correctness and uprightness.' Then the author of al-Kashf said: 'By ta'diya he did not mean the obvious meaning, which is the extension of the ruling from the original to the branch by qiyas; rather by ta'diya he meant the extension of the ruling by implication (dalalah), for the ruling is established in the pickpocket by implication, and this implication does not hold in the grave robber due to the weakness of the link.' The author of al-Tahrir followed him. But it is not as this scholar thought, because this Imam has established the existence of the concept of theft in the pickpocket completely, which requires the wording to include him explicitly, so there is no need for implication. Moreover, the weakness of the link does not negate implication in the grave robber. Rather the truth is that by ta'diya this Imam meant the linguistic meaning, which is the extension of the ruling. His intent is that since taking secretly exists in the pickpocket completely, the ruling of thief extends to him and is established explicitly, and this is excellent and upright. As for the grave robber, since the meaning [of theft] does not exist completely due to the absence of secure place and that all taken is of significant value, the name 'thief' does not include him, so the extension of the ruling to him is extremely weak due to lack of explicit implication. Is this not like extending the ruling of human to a horse due to the existence of animality? So understand. And the answer to the first objection: There is a difference between the specification in these two and the specification of types of a single genus. The specification in these two is such that each is used in contrast to 'thief' – one says 'this is a pickpocket' and 'this is a thief' or 'grave robber' – so upon reflection one knows that the meaning of the example given is that he is not a weak thief but a strong one, and that he is an individual of it. Unlike types of a genus, they are not used in contrast to the genus at all. What causes doubt is the first type of specification, not this one. This is the full discussion on this subject; preserve it, for it is subtle.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definition and application of the usul category 'al-khafi' (the obscure). The author first defines al-khafi as a text that is clear in itself but becomes obscure in some of its applications due to an external cause ('arad). He introduces the example of the word 'thief' (al-sariq), which is clear in its legal and linguistic meaning, but becomes obscure when applied to specific individuals like the pickpocket (al-tarrar) and the grave robber (al-nabbash) because each has a separate name. The ruling of theft (hadd of amputation) is clear for a thief, but its application to these two is uncertain. The author then analyzes each: the pickpocket takes from a secure place with concealment, so he is a complete thief and the hadd applies; the grave robber does not take from a secure place (the grave is not considered a proper secure place for property), there is no secrecy from the dead, and ownership of the shroud is weak, so he is not a true thief and the hadd does not apply. The passage then addresses objections. The first objection is that specification by a name does not cause obscurity in the genus (e.g., 'stone' and 'tree' are still 'bodies'). The second objection is a dilemma: either they are thieves or not; if yes, hadd applies regardless; if no, no hadd and no obscurity. The author resolves by showing that the pickpocket is a complete individual of 'thief' explicitly, while the grave robber is not. He then discusses the views of Imam Fakhr al-Islam and later commentators about 'ta'diya' (extension). The correct understanding is that the pickpocket is covered by the explicit wording of the verse, not by analogy or implication. The final answer to the first objection distinguishes between two types of specification: one that contrasts with the general term (like pickpocket vs thief) causing doubt, and the other that does not (like stone vs body). The lesson is described as subtle and important to preserve.

Key Terms
الخفي (al-khafi): A text that is clear (zahir) in its general meaning but obscure in some of its specific applications due to an external cause (arad).
السارق (al-sariq): One who takes the property of another secretly from a secure place (hirz).
الطرّار (al-tarrar): A pickpocket who takes from a person's clothing or pocket with skill, considered a complete thief.
النباش (al-nabbash): One who digs up graves to steal the shroud; considered not a true thief due to lack of hirz and weak ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school not apply the hadd of amputation to the grave robber (al-nabbash)?
A) Because the grave robber does not steal from a secure place.
B) Because the grave robber is not mentioned in the Quran.
C) Because the grave is considered a secure place.
D) Because the deceased owns the shroud completely.

Key Takeaway
A text that is clear in its general meaning can become obscure in specific applications due to an external cause; resolving this requires a thorough analysis of the definition to see if the instance truly falls under the general term.

Al-Mushkil: Resolving Ambiguity Through Context
Defines al-mushkil and demonstrates resolution via qara'in.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mushkil and apply contextual analysis (qara'in) to resolve the ambiguity of a word with multiple meanings using the Quranic example of 'anna'.

Core Idea
A muskil text's ambiguity is resolved not by guesswork but by contextual reasoning (qara'in) guided by the Shari'ah's objectives.

In Hanafi usul, not every unclear text is problematic; some can be clarified by context. This lesson introduces al-mushkil, a type of text whose ambiguity stems from the wording itself, and shows how reason and context uncover the intended meaning. The Quranic example of 'anna' in Surah al-Baqarah illustrates this method in action.

Guided Path
1
Define al-mushkil
Identify that al-mushkil is a text whose obscurity (khafa') arises from the wording itself (al-sigha), not from an external cause. The wording has multiple possible meanings, and the intended meaning is grasped by reason using contextual clues (qara'in).
Contrast with other types of unclear texts like al-mujmal, which requires external explanation.
2
Locate the Quranic example
The example is from Quran 2:223: 'Your women are tilth for you, so go to your tilth as you wish (anna shi'tum).' The word 'anna' is the source of ambiguity.
Write the verse reference: Al-Baqarah 2:223.
3
Identify the ambiguous word and its possible meanings
The word 'anna' (أنى) is used in two ways: (1) as 'ayn (أين) meaning 'where', and (2) as 'kayfa' (كيف) meaning 'how'. Both are lexically valid, so the text is muskil.
List the two meanings: 'where' and 'how'.
4
Apply contextual clues (qara'in) to resolve ambiguity
Two clues are mentioned: (a) 'tilth' (حرث) implies seeking offspring, which excludes the disliked place (anus); (b) the prohibition of harm (أذى) in the menstruation verse (2:222) reinforces that only the customary manner is allowed. These clues indicate that 'anna' means 'how' (manner), not 'where' (place).
Note that the qara'in are both textual (tilth) and contextual (related verse).
5
Derive the final ruling
The intended ruling is that intercourse with one's wife is permissible in any position (sitting, standing, lying) as long as it is in the vagina; anal intercourse is forbidden.
This ruling is derived by preferring the meaning 'how' over 'where'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإما للصيغة) عطف على قوله : إما لعارض أي إما أن يكون خفاؤه لأجل الصيغة بأن تكون هي محتملة لمعان كثيرة (فإما أن يدرك المراد بالعقل) بملاحظة السباق والسياق وغير ذلك من القرائن فهو المشكل، كأنى شئتم في قوله تعالى: ﴿ نِسَاؤُكُمْ حَرْثٌ لَكُمْ فَأْتُوا حَرْثَكُمْ أَنَّى شِئْتُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۲۳] (لاستعماله (كأين تارة، فلو حمل عليه كان المعنى : فأتوا في أي موضع شئتم من نسائكم، فيتناول الموضع المكروه أيضاً (و) استعماله مثل (كيف) تارة أخرى، فيكون المعنى : فأتوهن بأي كيفية شئتم من القعود والقيام والاضطجاع وغير ذلك، لكن المأتى به هو الفعل المعتاد فيظهر بقرينة الحرث المذكور في السياق وتحريم الأذى المذكور في آية الحيض (أن المراد الثاني) أما دلالة القرينة الأولى، فلأن الموضع المكروه لا يطلب منه الولد وأما دلالة الثانية فلأن الأذى
(And as for the wording) is connected to his saying: 'either due to an accidental cause' – meaning either its obscurity is due to the wording, in that it is susceptible to many meanings. (Then either the intended meaning is grasped by reason) by considering the context (sayaq and siyaq) and other indications, then it is al-mushkil. Like 'anna shi'tum' in His saying: 'Your women are tilth for you, so go to your tilth as you wish' (Quran 2:223). Because it is used sometimes as 'ayn' (where), so if taken that way, the meaning would be: 'come to your women from any place you wish,' which would include the disliked place [i.e., anus]. And it is also used like 'kayfa' (how), so the meaning would be: 'approach them in any manner you wish, whether sitting, standing, lying down, etc.' But the intended act is the customary one, and it becomes clear through the indication of 'tilth' mentioned in the context and the prohibition of harm mentioned in the verse of menstruation that the second meaning is intended. As for the indication of the first qarina, because the disliked place does not produce offspring; and as for the indication of the second, because harm...
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage defines al-mushkil (the problematic) as a type of unclear text where the ambiguity arises from the wording itself (al-sigha) because the word has multiple possible meanings. The intended meaning can be discerned by reason through contextual clues (sayaq/siyaq). The example given is the word 'anna' in Quran 2:223. The word 'anna' has two possible meanings: (1) as an interrogative adverb meaning 'where', and (2) as an adverb of manner meaning 'how'. If taken as 'where', it would permit intercourse in any place, including the anus (which is forbidden). If taken as 'how', it permits different positions. The context clarifies that the second meaning is intended. The passage mentions two contextual clues: the word 'tilth' (which implies seeking offspring, not the disliked place) and the prohibition of harm in the menstruation verse. So the correct understanding is that 'anna' here means 'how', allowing various positions but not anal intercourse. The text cuts off at 'al-adha' but it's part of the same explanation.

Key Terms
المشكل (al-mushkil): A text whose obscurity arises from the wording itself because the word has multiple possible meanings, requiring reason and context to determine the intended meaning.
أنى (anna): A word that can mean 'where' or 'how' depending on context.
القرينة (al-qarina): A contextual indicator that helps determine the intended meaning of an ambiguous word.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Quran 2:223, the word 'anna' is ambiguous. Which contextual clue indicates that it means 'how' rather than 'where'?
A) The word 'wives'
B) The word 'tilth'
C) The word 'wish'
D) The word 'go'

Key Takeaway
Al-mushkil is resolved by contextual clues; the word 'anna' in Quran 2:223 means 'how' (manner), not 'where', based on the 'tilth' and prohibition of harm clues.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Three Categories of Textual Ambiguity: Mushkil, Mujmal, Mutashabih
Defines three types of textual ambiguity and provides examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a text as mushkil, mujmal, or mutashabih and explain the method for resolving each category according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A text's meaning may be unclear; whether reason, transmission, or only divine knowledge can resolve it determines its category.

In Hanafi usul, not all unclear texts are the same. The scholars classified obscurity arising from wording into three types, each with a distinct path to clarification. This lesson will equip you to recognize these types and understand how a mujtahid approaches each one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of obscurity
Determine if the ambiguity arises from the wording itself (sigha) rather than from external factors like narration chain or contextual contradiction.
This classification only applies when the wording is inherently capable of multiple meanings.
2
Distinguish the three ways to know the intended meaning
If the intended meaning can be grasped by reason using contextual clues (qarain), the text is mushkil. If it requires a transmitted explanation (bayan) from the Lawgiver, it is mujmal. If it is knowable only by divine inspiration or not at all, it is mutashabih.
These categories correspond to increasing degrees of dependence on external sources.
3
Apply the definitions to the provided examples
For each category, confirm why the given example fits. 'Anna' is mushkil because context resolves its ambiguity. 'Mawali' and shariah terms like salat and riba are mujmal because their precise legal meaning is not known linguistically. The hand, eye, and descending of Allah are mutashabih because human reason cannot grasp their true nature.
4
Analyze the mushkil example in detail
Trace how the contextual clue (qarīnah) from 'harath' (tilth) eliminates the locative meaning of 'anna' and confirms the manner meaning. This illustrates the role of the mujtahid's reasoning.
The process involves considering both the immediate context and related Quranic prohibitions.
5
Recognize the practical consequence for ijtihad
Each category demands a different ijtihad approach. Mushkil requires reasoning with qarain. Mujmal requires seeking the Lawgiver's clarification. Mutashabih requires tafwid (affirming without asking how) and avoiding ta'wil.
This classification helps the mujtahid know when to stop seeking further meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإما للصيغة) عطف على قوله : إما لعارض أي إما أن يكون خفاؤه لأجل الصيغة بأن تكون هي محتملة لمعان كثيرة (فإما أن يدرك المراد بالعقل) بملاحظة السباق والسياق وغير ذلك من القرائن فهو المشكل، كأنى شئتم في قوله تعالى: ﴿ نِسَاؤُكُمْ حَرْثٌ لَكُمْ فَأْتُوا حَرْثَكُمْ أَنَّى شِئْتُمْ ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۲۳] (لاستعماله (كأين تارة، فلو حمل عليه كان المعنى : فأتوا في أي موضع شئتم من نسائكم، فيتناول الموضع المكروه أيضاً (و) استعماله مثل (كيف) تارة أخرى، فيكون المعنى : فأتوهن بأي كيفية شئتم من القعود والقيام والاضطجاع وغير ذلك، لكن المأتى به هو الفعل المعتاد فيظهر بقرينة الحرث المذكور في السياق وتحريم الأذى المذكور في آية الحيض (أن المراد الثاني) أما دلالة القرينة الأولى، فلأن الموضع المكروه لا يطلب منه الولد وأما دلالة الثانية فلأن الأذى لا يوجد في الموضع المكروه وأيضاً فإن قلت الأذى وهو النجاسة، كما أنه يوجد في الموضع المكروه يوجد في الموضع المعتاد أيضاً، فلا يراد مطلقه، بل أذى مخصوص بالحيض، وهو يوجد في الموضع المكروه فلا دلالة للأذى . قلت : المراد بالأذى النجاسة التي تنفر عنها الطبائع السليمة، كالدم ،والغائط، ولا شك أن كليهما مما تستقذره الطبائع السليمة، هذا (أو) لا ( يدرك) المراد بالعقل بل (بالنقل ) عن المجمل (فهو المجمل، كمشترك تعذر ترجيحه لعدم قرينة معينة للمراد (كالوصية لمواليه وله موال (أعلون) وهم المعتقون بالكسر (وأسفلون) وهم المعتقون بالفتح ، ولا يتبين المراد إلا ببيان الموصي، ولذا تبطل لو مات من غير بيان (ومنه الأسماء الشرعية كالصلاة فإنا نعلم قطعاً أن لغويها وهو الدعاء غير مراد فلا بد من معنى آخر شرعي، وهو غير مدرك إلا ببيان من الشارع (والربا) وهو لغة الزيادة، ولا شك أنه ليس كل زيادة محرمة فهي زيادة مخصوصة في الشرع، وهي غير معلومة إلا ببيان منه (أو لا يدرك) المراد (أصلاً) لا بالعقل ولا بالنقل، بل إن علم علم بمشاهدة موهوبة منه تعالى (فهو المتشابه، كالحروف في أوائل السور واليد المذكور في قوله تعالى: ﴿يَدُ اللَّهِ فَوقَ أَيْدِيهِمْ ﴾ [الفتح: ١٠] (والعين) في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِتُصْنَعَ عَلَى عَيْنِي ﴾ [طه: ۳۹] والنزول) كما ورد في السنة الصحيحة ينزل ربنا كل ليلة إلى السماء الدنيا إلى غير ذلك نحو الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى [طه: 5] .
And as for the wording (sigha): it is connected to his statement: 'either due to a preventer.' That is, either its obscurity is due to the wording, because it is susceptible to many meanings. Then either the intended meaning is grasped by reason (by considering the context, the verbal and situational context, and other indicators) — that is the mushkil, like 'anna shi'tum' in the verse {Your women are a tilth for you, so come to your tilth as you wish} [al-Baqarah: 223]. Because it is used sometimes like 'ayna' (where), so if interpreted that way, the meaning would be: 'come in any place you wish from your women,' which would include the disliked place (anus). And it is used sometimes like 'kayfa' (how), so the meaning would be: 'come to them in any manner you wish, whether sitting, standing, lying down, etc.' But the intended act is the usual one, and by the context of 'tilth' mentioned in the context and the prohibition of harm mentioned in the verse of menstruation, it becomes clear that the second meaning (how) is intended. As for the indication of the first context, because the disliked place (anus) does not produce offspring. As for the indication of the second, because harm (adha) is not found in the disliked place. But if you say: harm, i.e., impurities, exists in the disliked place as it exists in the usual place, so the absolute harm is not intended, but rather harm specific to menstruation, and that exists in the disliked place, so harm has no indication. I say: what is meant by harm is the impurities that sound natures abhor, like blood and feces, and there is no doubt that both are considered filthy by sound natures. This. Or he does not grasp the intended meaning by reason but rather by transmission from the corpus (mujmal) — that is the mujmal, like a homonym (mushtarak) whose preponderance is impossible due to the lack of a specific indicator for the intended meaning. Example: 'bequest to his mawali' while he has higher mawali (manumitters, with kasr) and lower mawali (manumitted slaves, with fatha), and the intended meaning is not clarified except by the testator's statement; hence it becomes invalid if he dies without clarification. Among them are the shariah terms (asma' shar'iyyah) like prayer (salat); we know certainly that its linguistic meaning (supplication) is not intended, so there must be another shariah meaning, which is not grasped except by clarification from the Lawgiver. And riba, which linguistically means increase; undoubtedly not every increase is prohibited, so it is a specific increase in shariah, and it is not known except by clarification from Him. Or the intended meaning is not grasped at all, neither by reason nor by transmission; rather, if it is known, it is known by an inspired witnessing from Allah — that is the mutashabih, like the disjointed letters at the beginnings of surahs, and the 'hand' mentioned in the verse {The hand of Allah is above their hands} [al-Fath: 10], and the 'eye' in {That you might be formed under My eye} [Ta-Ha: 39], and the 'descending' as reported in the authentic hadith: 'Our Lord descends every night to the nearest heaven,' and similar such as {The Most Merciful, above the Throne, established} [Ta-Ha: 5].
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage defines the causes of obscurity in texts arising from the wording itself. It presents a three-fold classification based on how the intended meaning can be known. The first category is al-mushkil (ambiguous but resolvable by reason), illustrated by the word 'anna' in the Quranic verse {... as you wish}. The word has two possible meanings (where and how), but context and other clues indicate the intended meaning is 'how.' The second category is al-mujmal (ambiguous and requiring external clarification from the Lawgiver). Examples include homonyms without contextual preference, such as 'mawali' which can mean both manumitters and manumitted slaves, and shariah terms like salat and riba, whose precise legal definitions are not known linguistically but must be learned from revelation. The third category is al-mutashabih (inherently unknowable to human reason), like the 'hand' and 'eye' of Allah and the 'descending.' For these, the meaning is known only by divine inspiration or not at all. The passage thus provides a systematic taxonomy of textual ambiguity essential for usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
المشكل (al-mushkil): A text whose intended meaning can be grasped by reason through contextual clues despite initial ambiguity.
المجمل (al-mujmal): A text whose intended meaning cannot be known by reason alone and requires clarification (bayan) from the Lawgiver (e.g., shariah terms).
المتشابه (al-mutashabih): A text whose intended meaning is unknowable to human reason and transmission, and is known only by divine inspiration or not at all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which category of ambiguous text is the term 'salat' (prayer) according to this passage?
A) Al-mushkil, because it can be understood from context.
B) Al-mujmal, because its shariah meaning must be learned from the Lawgiver.
C) Al-mutashabih, because its meaning is ultimately unknowable.
D) Al-mufassar, because it is clearly explained in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Textual ambiguity in Hanafi usul is classified by the knowability of its intended meaning: mushkil (resolvable by reason), mujmal (requiring transmission), and mutashabih (known only by divine inspiration).

Takhsis al-Amm in the Khums Verse
Applying usul principle of takhsis al-amm to the verse on khums for relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of takhsis al-amm to a Quranic text and evaluate the strength of the evidence used for specification.

Core Idea
A general Quranic term can be specified by contextual evidence, even if that evidence is zanni.

This passage explores a classic usul debate: does the general term 'dhu al-qurba' (relative) in the khums verse include all relatives or only the poor among them? The Hanafi school argues for specification based on the principle that khums is compensation for zakah, which is for the poor. This lesson walks through the proofs and counter-arguments, sharpening your ability to trace derivation chains and assess the weight of different evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general term and the claimed specification
Locate the phrase 'وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى' in the khums verse (al-Anfal 8:41). The Hanafi position is that it is specified to the poor relatives only.
The term is general (amm) in its linguistic form, but the Hanafis restrict its application.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof: the compensation hadith
Understand the argument that the Prophet's statement about khums as compensation for zakah implies that the share for relatives should go to the poor, since zakah recipients are the poor.
This is a khabar wahid with indications of compensation, not an explicit wording.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
The opposing school holds that the general text must be taken literally; a khabar wahid cannot specify the Quran, especially if it only implies the specification by implication (isharah).
This objection challenges both the epistemological weight (thubut) and the clarity of the evidence (dalala).
4
Follow the Hanafi response: practice of the Caliphs and further specification
The Hanafis cite that the Rightly Guided Caliphs restricted the khums distribution to orphans, needy, and wayfarers, effectively excluding rich relatives. Also, the term 'dhu al-qurba' is itself historically specified because certain relatives were excluded.
This strengthens the Hanafi position by providing a precedent and additional contextual specification.
5
Evaluate the epistemological weight
Consider whether the specification is definitive (qat'i) or probable (zanni). The passage does not declare a definitive ruling, indicating that the Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school but remains a matter of valid ikhtilaf.
This step develops your ability to assess the authority level of a legal ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها حمل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى ) في كريمة ﴿وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُم مِّن شَيْءٍ فَأَنَّ لِلَّهِ حُمُسَهُ وَلِلرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَمَى وَالْمَسَكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ ﴾ [الأنفال: ٤١] (على الفقراء منهم سد خلة المحتاج) دليل للحمل (مع أن القرابة ربما تجعل سبباً للاستحقاق مع الغنى تشريفاً للنبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم) فهذه العلة ملائمة لعموم الحكم وقد تركوا وأوّلوا العلة محتملة (وأجيب بأن ذلك ليس لما ذكرتم من العلة بل لقوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم : يا بني هاشم إن الله كره لكم أوساخ الناس وهي الزكاة (وعوضكم عنها الخمس والمعوض عنه للفقير ) فكذا العوض فوجب التخصيص، قال الشيخ ابن الهمام في فتح القدير لم يوجد لفظ العوض في كتب الحديث، لكن الأمر سهل، لأن ابن أبي حاتم رواه عن ابن عباس قال: رغبت لكم في غسالة الأيدي، لأن لكم في خمس الخمس ما يغنيكم ويكفيكم، وفيه إشارة إلى العوضية. وقد ورد نص من أمير المؤمنين علي رضي الله عنه موقوفاً في العوضية، لكن يرد عليه أن العوضية إن دل فإنما يدل على الاختصاص بالفقراء بالإشارة دون العبارة، فلا يكون معارضاً للنص القرآني، فلا يصلح مخصصاً، مع أن هذا خبر الواحد، وقد أصررتم على عدم جواز تخصيص عام الكتاب ،به فإن هذا لم يخص بقاطع أصلاً، ولا يبعد أن يقال في دفع الثاني أن ذوي القربي عام مخصوص، لأنه أخرج نوفل، وبنو عبد شمس مع دخول بني المطلب وهم وهؤلاء في القرابة سواء، ثم فيه إشكال آخر ذكره الشيخ ابن الهمام في فتح القدير»، هو أن هذا لو تم لدل على أن استحقاق خمس الخمس للفقراء منهم مع أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم كان يعطي العباس ابن عبد المطلب ولم يكن هو فقيراً قط وقد صح عن الخلفاء الراشدين) رضوان الله تعالى عليهم أنهم لم يعطوا ذوي القربى من الصدقات) أي الأخماس لا الزكاة سماها صدقة لأنه من مال الله تعالى لأنهم صاروا أغنياء إذ ذاك فلم يبقوا مصارف) روى الإمام أبو يوسف عن الكلبي عن أبي صالح عن ابن عباس أن الخمس كان يقسم على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على خمسة أسهم : لله وللرسول سهم، ولذي القربي سهم، ولليتامى سهم، وللمساكين سهم، ولابن السبيل سهم. ثم قسمه أبو بكر وعمر وعثمان وعلي ثلاثة أسهم : سهم لليتامى، وسهم للمساكين، وسهم لابن السبيل لكن الكلبي ضعيف عند أهل الحديث، لكن الأمر سهل لأنه اعتضد برواية الطحاوي رحمه الله عن محمد بن إسحاق قال : سألت أبا جعفر يعني محمد بن علي فقلت : أرأيت علي بن أبي طالب حين ولي العراق ولما ولي من أمر الناس كيف صنع منه بنو
And among them is the interpretation of His statement: 'And for the relative' in the noble verse: 'And know that whatever spoils you take, a fifth is for Allah and the Messenger and for the relative and the orphans and the needy and the wayfarer' [al-Anfal 41] as meaning the poor among them to meet the need of the destitute—an evidence for the interpretation—even though kinship might be a cause for entitlement even if rich, as an honor for the Prophet. So this rationale fits the generality of the ruling, but they left it and interpreted a probable rationale. And it was answered that this is not due to the rationale you mentioned, but due to his saying: 'O Banu Hashim, Allah has disliked for you the impurities of people, which is zakah, and has compensated you with khums, and the compensation is for the poor.' So the compensation necessitates specification. Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: the word 'compensation' is not found in hadith books, but it is easy because Ibn Abi Hatim narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'I desired for you the washing of hands, because you have in the fifth of the fifth what suffices you.' And there is an indication of compensation. And a text has come from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, as a mawquf report regarding compensation. But it is objected that compensation, if it indicates, indicates specification to the poor by implication (isharah) not by explicit wording, so it does not oppose the Quranic text, thus it is not valid as a specifier, especially since this is a khabar wahid, and you have insisted on the impermissibility of specifying the general of the Book with it. For this has not been specified by a definitive proof at all. And it is not far-fetched to say in rebutting the second point that 'dhu al-qurba' is a general term but has been specified, because it excludes Nawfal and Banu Abd Shams while including Banu al-Muttalib, though they are equal in kinship. Then there is another problem mentioned by Shaykh Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir: that if this were valid, it would indicate that entitlement to the fifth of the khums is for the poor among them, even though the Messenger of Allah used to give al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib, and he was never poor. And it has been authentically reported from the Rightly Guided Caliphs that they did not give the relatives from the charities—meaning the khums, not zakah, calling it charity because it is from the wealth of Allah—because they had become wealthy at that time, so they were no longer recipients. Imam Abu Yusuf narrated from al-Kalbi from Abu Salih from Ibn Abbas that the khums was divided in the time of the Prophet into five shares: for Allah and the Messenger a share, for the relative a share, for orphans a share, for the needy a share, and for the wayfarer a share. Then Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali divided it into three shares: share for orphans, share for needy, share for wayfarer. But al-Kalbi is weak according to hadith scholars, but it is easy because it is supported by the narration of al-Tahawi from Muhammad ibn Ishaq who said: I asked Abu Ja'far, meaning Muhammad ibn Ali: Did you see Ali ibn Abi Talib when he was in charge of Iraq and when he took charge of people's affairs, how did he deal with the Banu?
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a usul discussion on the specification (takhsis) of a general term (amm) in the Quran. The verse under analysis is the khums verse (al-Anfal 8:41), which includes the phrase 'and for the relative' (wa li dhi al-qurba). The author presents the Hanafi position that this general term is specified to mean only the poor among the relatives, not all relatives. The rationale given is that the share is to meet the need of the destitute (sadd khallat al-muhtaj). However, an objection arises: kinship might be a cause for entitlement even if the relative is rich, as an honor to the Prophet. The author then provides a counter-argument: the specification is not based on that rationale but on a hadith where the Prophet says that Allah has compensated Banu Hashim for zakah with khums, implying that khums is a substitute for zakah, and zakah is for the poor, so khums for relatives is also for the poor. The author notes that Ibn al-Humam points out that the exact word 'compensation' is not found in hadith, but an indication exists in a narration from Ibn Abbas. He then raises a further objection: if the hadith indicates compensation, it does so by implication (isharah) not explicit wording, so it cannot oppose the clear Quranic text, especially since it is a khabar wahid, and the Hanafi school generally does not allow specification of a general Quranic text with a khabar wahid. The author then offers another argument: the term 'dhu al-qurba' is itself already specified because the practice of the Salaf excluded certain relatives (Nawfal, Banu Abd Shams) while including Banu al-Muttalib, though they are equally related. Finally, he mentions a practical problem: if khums is only for the poor relatives, how did the Prophet give to al-Abbas, who was wealthy? And the Rightly Guided Caliphs later restricted the distribution to only orphans, needy, and wayfarers, indicating that relatives were not given because they became wealthy. The passage thus illustrates the complexity of takhsis al-amm and the need to consider multiple evidences.

Key Terms
تخصيص العام (takhsis al-amm): The specification of a general term to exclude some of its individuals, here using circumstantial evidence.
العوضية (al-'iwadiyyah): The principle that khums is a compensation (iwad) for the prohibition of zakah on Banu Hashim.
القرابة (al-qarabah): Kinship or relationship by blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, what is the rationale for specifying 'وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى' in the khums verse to the poor only?
A) The verse explicitly states 'poor'
B) Khums is compensation for zakah, which is for the poor
C) The Prophet never gave khums to rich relatives
D) The Caliphs unanimously decided so

Key Takeaway
The specification of a general term in the Quran can be achieved by a sound khabar wahid when supported by contextual evidence and practice, as in the case of khums for relatives.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
15 min
Specifying the Share of Relatives in Khums
Dispute over specifying dhawil-qurba in khums verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the specification of dhawil-qurba in the khums verse and evaluate the proofs each school presents.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school specifies the general verse on khums to the poor of the Prophet's relatives using the compensation principle and companion consensus.

This lesson examines a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh: can a general Quranic verse be specified by a hadith that is zanni al-thubut or by the practice of the caliphs? The case is the khums verse (al-Anfal 8:41) and the share of the Prophet's relatives. The Hanafis argue for restriction to the poor, while the Shafi'is uphold generality. Understanding this dispute clarifies how the Hanafi school prioritizes qati vs zanni proofs and the role of ijma in specifying the Quran.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its dalil
Identify what the Hanafis claim: the share of relatives in khums is restricted to the poor among Banu Hashim. Then note their primary proof: the hadith of compensation (iwad) indicating khums replaces zakah, plus the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.
The compensation hadith is narrated by Ibn Abbas but not with the exact word 'iwad'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and their dalil
The Shafi'is hold that the general wording of the verse includes all relatives, rich or poor. Their proof is the apparent generality of the Quranic text (amm), and they argue that the compensation hadith is either weak or merely indicative, not explicit.
The Shafi'is also question the consensus because Ahl al-Bayt may not have agreed.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal via caliphal practice
The Hanafis cite that the four caliphs (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali) did not give the share to relatives, and all companions were present without objection, forming a consensus. They also narrate that Ali followed the same path.
Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir argues this is an explicit consensus, not silent, because the companions collectively agreed to put the share into jihad.
4
Evaluate the force of the consensus argument
Consider the Shafi'i objection that the consensus is zanni (conjectural) and cannot oppose a qati verse. The Hanafis respond that the consensus is explicit (sarih) as narrated by Qays ibn Muslim al-Jadali, thus decisive.
The author of the text sides with the Hanafi position, finding the explicit consensus stronger.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis give khums share only to poor relatives; Shafi'is give to all relatives equally. This affects distribution of spoils in contemporary contexts.

الخليفة، وقال قائل : سهم النبي للخليفة من بعده، فاجتمع رأي أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يجعلوا هذين السهمين في الخيل والعدة في سبيل الله ، فكان كذلك من خلافة أبي بكر وعمر، وهذا صريح في The first principle/the book. For Allah is the fifth. Because the intended meaning. And it was raised by Abdullah bin Abi Bakr from al-Zuhri, raised from the Mother of the Believers Hafsa, may Allah be pleased with her. As for the second: because al-Daraqutni said it is unique to Abdullah bin Abbad from al-Fadl with this chain, all are trustworthy. Al-Bayhaqi scrutinized it because Abdullah bin Abbad is not famous and Yahya bin Ayyub is not strong and he is among its narrators. And Abdullah bin Abbad al-Basri used to turn over reports. And it was said that Rawh bin al-Faraj narrated from him a fabricated copy. Our noble teachers gave precedence to the authentic hadith of fasting Ashura, agreed upon its authenticity, and acted upon its wording and indication, and acted upon this disputed matter where it agreed with analogy. This is how it should be understood, so understand. And among them is the carrying of His statement Exalted: 'and to the relatives' in the noble verse 'And know that whatever of spoils you take, verily for Allah is its fifth, and for the Messenger, and for the relatives, and the orphans, and the needy, and the wayfarer' [al-Anfal 41] upon the poor among them to fill the need of the needy, a proof for the carrying, even though kinship may sometimes be a cause for entitlement despite wealth as an honor for the Prophet, may Allah bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace. So this cause is suitable for the generality of the ruling, and they abandoned and interpreted the probable cause. And it was answered that that is not due to the cause you mentioned, but due to his saying, may Allah bless him and his family and companions: 'O Banu Hashim, Allah disliked for you the impurities of the people, which is zakah, and compensated you with khums, and the compensated is for the poor.' Thus the compensation necessitated specification. Sheikh Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: the word compensation is not found in the hadith books. But the matter is easy, because Ibn Abi Hatim narrated it from Ibn Abbas: 'I desired for you the washing of hands, because you have in the fifth of the fifth what suffices you.' In it is an indication of compensation. And a text has come from the Commander of the Faithful Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, stopped, regarding compensation. But it is objected that compensation, if it indicates, only indicates specification to the poor by indication, not by explicit wording. Thus it cannot oppose the Quranic text, so it is not suitable as a specifier, especially since this is a solitary report, and you have insisted on the impermissibility of specifying the general of the Book by it. This was not specified by a decisive text at all. And it is not far to say in repelling the second that dhawil-qurba is a general that has been specified, because it excluded Nawfal and Banu Abd Shams while including Banu al-Muttalib, and they and these are equal in kinship. Then there is another problem mentioned by Sheikh Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir: that if this were complete, it would indicate that entitlement to the fifth of the fifth is for the poor among them, whereas the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions, used to give al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib and he was never poor. And it has been authentically reported from the Rightly Guided Caliphs, may Allah be pleased with them, that they did not give to the relatives from the alms – meaning the khums, not zakah – calling it alms because it is from the wealth of Allah, because they had become rich at that time, so they no longer remained recipients. Imam Abu Yusuf narrated from al-Kalbi from Abu Salih from Ibn Abbas: the khums was divided during the time of the Messenger of Allah into five shares: for Allah and the Messenger a share, for the relative a share, for the orphans a share, for the needy a share, and for the wayfarer a share. Then Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali divided it into three shares: a share for orphans, a share for needy, a share for wayfarer. But al-Kalbi is weak according to hadith scholars, but the matter is easy because it is supported by the narration of al-Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, from Muhammad ibn Ishaq: I asked Abu Ja'far, meaning Muhammad ibn Ali: 'What do you think? When Ali ibn Abi Talib took over Iraq and when he took charge of the people's affairs, how did he deal with the share of the relatives?' He said: 'By Allah, he followed the path of Abu Bakr and Umar.' I said: 'How, and you say what you say?' He said: 'By Allah, his family only acted upon his opinion.' I said: 'What prevented him?' He said: 'By Allah, he disliked being called to a way other than the practice of Abu Bakr and Umar.' Sheikh Ibn al-Humam said in Fath al-Qadir: So it is known from this that the Rightly Guided Caliphs did not give, and all the companions were present and none objected, so it became consensus. And he said: Imam al-Shafi'i only said what he said because he claims that the Ahl al-Bayt did not agree with it, so it was not consensus. And it was answered regarding that: The Commander of the Faithful Ali is too far above ruling according to what he sees as false. How could he be, for it involves preventing the entitled from his right, and he is innocent of this. If the reason were this, he would not have disagreed regarding the sale of mothers of children. So it is known that this is from his own opinion. This has apparent reflection, because it is possible that the lack of objection from the companions was because it was after their opinion had been settled upon him, and there is no objection to a ruler after the opinion is settled. Silence is only evidence of agreement before the opinions are settled. Or because he only did this action with the permission of the rights holder, as Ibn al-Mundhir narrated: The Commander of the Faithful Umar used to pay it to the Commander of the Faithful Ali, and once he said to him: 'This is your share, Ahl al-Bayt, of the khums. Some Muslims have become difficult and their need has intensified.' He said: 'Yes.' As for his mention that the Commander of the Faithful Ali is too far above ruling against his opinion, that is true and sound. But this indicates the weakness of this report and the hidden interruption in it, not that it necessitates that his opinion was not to give. Then the Sheikh objected to him: The verse is for explaining the recipients, so it is permissible to give to one category without another. So it is possible that the non-giving of the caliphs was of this type due to the severe need of others. This does not benefit al-Shafi'i, because he claims entitlement. Yes, it harms us and benefits Malik. And it is also objected that this type of consensus is conjectural, with weak conjecture, so how can it oppose the decisive verse? Then there is another reflection: if this explanation were complete, it would indicate abrogation of the verse, not specification to the poor. And it is as you see, so reflect on it. And what this servant has is to argue with what was reported by Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shayba, and Ibn Abi Hatim from Qays ibn Muslim al-Jadali: I asked al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Abi Talib ibn al-Hanafiyya about the saying of Allah Most High: 'And know that whatever of spoils you take, verily for Allah is its fifth, and for the Messenger' [al-Anfal 41]. He said: This is the key to the speech of the world and the hereafter: for the Messenger and for the relatives. They differed after the death of the Messenger of Allah regarding these two shares. One said: the share of the relatives is for the relatives of the Messenger of Allah. Another said: the share of the relatives is for the relatives of the caliph. Another said: the share of the Prophet is for the caliph after him. Then the opinion of the companions of the Messenger of Allah agreed to put these two shares into horses and equipment for the cause of Allah. So it continued from the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar. This is explicit consensus, and the objection from Fath al-Qadir does not stand against it, because it is explicit that they did not leave the recipients, and this agreement was not silent so as to be conjectural. As for the objection of necessitating abrogation of the verse, it is repelled because the share was for the relatives for supporting the Prophet, as Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Jubayr ibn Mut'im: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and his family and companions, divided the share of the relatives among Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib. I and Uthman ibn Affan walked in and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, these are our brothers from Banu Hashim – we do not deny their virtue due to your position which Allah has placed you among them – what do you think of our brothers from Banu al-Muttalib: you gave them and not us, though we are... until
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute over the specification (takhsis) of the general term 'dhawil-qurba' (relatives) in the khums verse (al-Anfal 8:41). The Hanafis argue that the share is restricted to the poor among the Prophet's relatives, while the Shafi'is maintain it includes both rich and poor.

The Hanafi proof begins with a literal carrying of the verse onto the poor by necessity (sadd khalat al-muhtaj). They note that although kinship could be a reason for entitlement even if rich (as an honor), they interpret the verse accordingly. The opponent objects that this is not the cause; rather, a hadith states: 'O Banu Hashim, Allah disliked for you the impurities of people (zakah) and compensated you with khums; the compensated is for the poor.' This implies specification to the poor. However, Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir notes the word 'compensation' (iwad) is not found in hadith books, but a variant from Ibn Abbas uses 'washing of hands' as an indication.

The opponent then raises: this indication is only by allusion, not explicit wording, so it cannot oppose the clear Quranic text. Moreover, it is a solitary report (khabar wahid), and the Hanafis themselves require a decisive text to specify the general of the Quran.

The Hanafis counter that dhawil-qurba is already a general that has been specified (e.g., excluding Banu Nawfal and Banu Abd Shams). They also cite the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali are reported to have given only three shares (orphans, needy, wayfarer), omitting the shares for Allah/the Prophet and relatives. This is reported by Abu Yusuf via al-Kalbi, but al-Kalbi is weak. However, it is supported by al-Tahawi's narration from Muhammad ibn Ishaq that Ali followed the path of Abu Bakr and Umar in not giving the share to relatives. Ibn al-Humam argues this shows consensus (ijma) because all companions were present and no one objected.

Al-Shafi'i objects that the Ahl al-Bayt did not agree, so there is no consensus. The Hanafis respond that Ali himself is unlikely to rule wrongly, and his silence indicates agreement. They also note that Umar consulted Ali about the share, and Ali consented to redirect it due to need.

Finally, the author presents a stronger proof: a report from Qays ibn Muslim al-Jadali that the companions agreed to use the Prophet's share and the relatives' share for horses and equipment in the path of Allah during the caliphates of Abu Bakr and Umar. This is explicit consensus (ijma sarih), not merely silent, so it is decisive. The objection of abrogation is repelled because the share was originally for supporting the Prophet, and after his death, the cause changed.

In summary, the Hanafi position relies on the practice of the caliphs and explicit consensus to specify the general verse, whereas the Shafi'i position holds the general text until a clear specifier is proven.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term to a subset of its individuals.
العوضية (al-iwadiyya): The principle that khums is a compensation to Banu Hashim for being forbidden from zakah, and thus takes the same ruling as zakah (i.e., for the poor).
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the companions on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafis consider the consensus of the companions on khums distribution to be decisive (qati)?
A) The consensus was recorded in mutawatir hadith.
B) The companions explicitly agreed verbally that the share should go to the poor.
C) The consensus is explicit (sarih) as reported by Qays ibn Muslim al-Jadali, not just silent.
D) The Quranic verse itself indicates the consensus.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi specification of dhawil-qurba to the poor relies on an explicit companion consensus that is considered qati, overriding the general verse.

The Core Dispute: Lam for Ownership or Allocation?
Debating the meaning of the lam in the zakat verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the lam in Q9:60, identify their respective proofs, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The lam indicates allocation (sarf), not ownership, allowing zakat to a single category.

This lesson introduces the central usul dispute over the preposition 'li' in the zakat verse. The Hanafis interpret it as specifying recipients (bayan al-masraf), while the Shafi'is see it as conferring ownership (tamlik). The practical consequence is whether one category can receive all zakat or must be distributed across all categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested term
Find the word 'lil-fuqara' in Q9:60 and note that the dispute is about the meaning of the lam (li).
The lam is a preposition that can indicate ownership or allocation.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis hold that the lam indicates allocation (sarf), so the verse explains where zakat should go, not who owns it.
This permits giving to a single category.
3
State the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'is hold that the lam indicates ownership (tamlik), so each category must receive a share.
They also require at least three individuals per category due to the plural.
4
Identify the proof for each
Hanafis rely on context (9:58) and prophetic practice; Shafi'is rely on the literal meaning of lam and the plural form.
The dispute is not easily resolved; both positions have linguistic and practical evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that Hanafis allow giving all zakat to one category, while Shafi'is require distribution across all categories.
This affects how zakat is administered in practice.

(مع أن اللام ظاهر في الملك) فالحمل على بيان المصرف عدول عن الحقيقة من غير باعث والشافعية يحملون على الملك، فيكون الأصناف كلهم ملاكاً فلا يجوز الصرف إلى واحد، وأيضاً: عندهم الفقراء، وأمثالها باقية على معنى الجمعية، فلا يصرف إلى أقل من ثلاثة ودفع ابن الحاجب) ذلك بأن السباق وهو رد لمزهم في المعطين ورضاهم عنهم إذا أعطوهم وسخطهم إياهم إذا منعوا يقتضي بيان المصارف قال الله تعالى قبل هذه الآية: ﴿وَمِنْهُم مَّن يَلْمِزُكَ فِي الصَّدَقَاتِ فَإِنْ أَعْطُوا مِنْهَا رَضُوا وَإِن لَّمْ يُعْطَوا مِنْهَا إِذَا هُمْ يَسْخَطُونَ ﴾ [التوبة : ٥٨] نزلت في المنافقين حيث قالوا عند شياطينهم إن صاحبكم لا يعدل في القسمة وفشا ذلك، وقال ذو الخويصرة منهم في المجلس الشريف كما في (صحيح البخاري، فأنزل الله تعالى هذه الآية لئلا يتوهم أنهم مختارون في المنع والعطاء) فهذا يدل على أن الغرض بيان المصرف (ورد) في شرح المختصر » (بأن ذلك يحصل بيان الاستحقاق أيضاً، فإنهم إذا كانوا مستحقين ملاكاً فالعدول عنهم ليس في يد القاسمين المعطين (فلا يصلح صارفاً عن الظاهر فإن قلت : يبقى اللمز في إعطاء الواحد من الأصناف، قلت: لا يجوز عندهم ذلك، فليس ذلك اللمز باطلاً، لكن ورد في بعض الروايات من كتب الحديث أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أعطى أبا سفيان ومعاوية ويزيد بن أبي سفيان من غنائم حنين فقيل ما قيل فأنزل الله تعالى هذه الآية، فاللمز حينئذ بسبب إعطاء البعض وتركهم، ودفع هذا اللمز لا يكون إلا ببيان المصارف لا ببيان الاستحقاق، وهذا وجه وجيه لكن ظاهر عبارة ابن الحاجب ينبو عنه فتدبر (أقول) في الجواب مطابقاً لما أفاد صدر الشريعة العموم) مناف للتمليك فإن تملك كل فقير كل صدقة غير معقول (لا) للمصرف فإن كل فقير يصلح مصرفاً فلا بد من (صرف) إما للعموم وإما للام وصرف العموم يستلزم التمليك لغير معين فإنه إذا انصرف اللفظ عن العموم فإما أن يراد الجنس ويكون المعنى جنس الصدقة مملوك لجنس الفقير فمع كونه خلاف مذهبهم من وجوب الإعطاء للثلاثة من كل صنف تمليك لغير معين أو يكون الجمعية مقصودة كما في النكارة، فمع كونه صرفاً للام عن الحقيقة تمليك أيضاً لغير معين (وهو) أي التمليك لغير المعين (لم يعهد) في الشرع فصرف اللام إلى المصرف هو الوجه لا غير ، فلا يكون تأويلاً بعيداً، وأجاب في «فتح القدير» بوجه آخر هو أن كون اللام ظاهراً في الملك وموضوعـاً لـه ممنوع وإنما اللام للاختصاص أعم من أن يكون على سبيل الملك أو غيره، فالحمل على خصوص الملك حمل على غير الظاهر من غير دليل فرجع المحذور قهقرى
And among them is their interpretation like the Malikis and Hanbalis? That is, the Hanafis' interpretation like the interpretation of the Malikis and Hanbalis of His saying: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor' (9:60) as indicating the allocation (of the funds) so that it is permissible to give to one category among those categories, despite the fact that the lam is apparently for ownership. So interpreting it as allocation is a departure from the reality without a motivator. The Shafi'is interpret it as ownership, so all the categories are owners, and it is not permissible to give to one only. Also, according to them, 'the poor' and similar terms retain the meaning of collectivity, so one should not give to less than three. And Ibn al-Hajib refuted that by saying that the context – which is refuting their criticism of those who give and their pleasure when they give and their anger when they are prevented – necessitates the explanation of the allocations. Allah said before this verse: 'And among them are some who criticize you concerning the charities; if they are given from them, they become satisfied, and if not given, they become angry' (9:58). This was revealed concerning the hypocrites who said to their demons that their companion does not act justly in distribution, and that became widespread, and Dhu al-Khuwaysira from among them said in the noble gathering as in Sahih al-Bukhari. So Allah revealed this verse lest they think that they have a choice in preventing or giving. So this indicates that the purpose is to explain the allocation. And it was replied in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that this also achieves the explanation of entitlement, because if they are entitled as owners, then turning away from them is not in the hands of the givers, so it does not justify departure from the apparent meaning. If you say: The criticism remains in giving to only one of the categories; I say: That is not permissible according to them, so that criticism is not invalid. But it has been reported in some hadith works that the Messenger of Allah gave to Abu Sufyan, Muawiyah, and Yazid ibn Abi Sufyan from the spoils of Hunayn, and something was said, so Allah revealed this verse. Then the criticism was due to giving to some and leaving others, and repelling this criticism can only be by explaining the allocations, not by explaining entitlement. And this is a strong point, but the apparent wording of Ibn al-Hajib recoils from it, so reflect. I say: In the response matching what Sadr al-Shariah stated: The generality conflicts with ownership, because every poor person owning every charity is unintelligible, but not for allocation, because every poor person is a valid recipient. So there must be a turn away either from the generality or from the lam. Turning away from generality entails ownership to an unspecified person, because if the word is turned away from generality, then either the genus is intended, meaning the genus of charity is owned by the genus of the poor – which, besides being against their school of giving to three from each category, is ownership to an unspecified person – or collectivity is intended, as in the case of 'nakaarah' (denial), then even though it is a turning away from the lam's reality, it is also ownership to an unspecified person. And that (ownership to an unspecified person) is not known in the Sharia, so turning the lam to allocation is the only correct option, and thus it is not a far-fetched interpretation. And it was answered in Fath al-Qadir with another point: that it is denied that the lam is apparently for ownership and placed for it; rather, the lam is for specification, more general than being on the basis of ownership or other. So interpreting it specifically as ownership is interpreting by the non-apparent without proof, so the [same] problem returns retreating.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the interpretation of the lam in the zakat verse (9:60). The Hanafis, along with Malikis and Hanbalis, interpret the lam as indicating allocation (sarf) of the funds, meaning the zakat is to be distributed to the eight categories, and it is permissible to give to one category only. The Shafi'is interpret the lam as ownership (tamlik), meaning each category must receive a share, and due to the plural form, they require distribution to at least three individuals from each category. The author then presents a defense by Ibn al-Hajib, who argues from the context (siyaq) of the preceding verses (9:58) that the purpose is to explain where the zakat should go, not who owns it. However, a reply in Sharh al-Mukhtasar counters that the context also explains entitlement. The author then mentions a variant hadith where the Prophet gave to specific individuals, showing the criticism was about giving to some and not others, which is better addressed by explaining allocation. The discussion continues with Sadr al-Shariah's point that interpreting 'generality' leads to unintelligible ownership, so the lam must be for allocation. Finally, Fath al-Qadir argues that the lam is for specification (ikhtisas) not necessarily ownership, so the Hanafi interpretation is not a departure from the apparent.

Key Terms
اللام (al-lam): The preposition 'li' in 'lil-fuqara' – debated whether it indicates ownership (tamlik) or specification/allocation (sarf/ikhtisas).
بيان المصرف (bayan al-masraf): Explaining where the zakat should be allocated – the Hanafi interpretation.
السباق (al-siyaq): The context of the preceding verses that helps determine the meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis in this passage, what does the lam in 'lil-fuqara' (Q9:60) indicate?
A) Ownership (tamlik) of each poor person
B) Allocation (sarf) of the zakat to the categories
C) The poor are the sole owners of all zakat
D) The verse is abrogated

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of the lam as allocation (sarf) permits giving zakat to a single category, while the Shafi'i interpretation as ownership (tamlik) requires distribution to all categories with at least three recipients per category.

The Context (Siyaq) Argument for Allocation
Focusing on the siyaq argument and its rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafis use the context of verse 9:58 as a qarinah for interpreting the lam in 9:60 as allocation, and identify the rebuttal from Sharh al-Mukhtasar.

Core Idea
The siyaq of 9:58 reveals the verse is about explaining allocations, not ownership.

This lesson focuses on the specific argument from context (siyaq) presented by Ibn al-Hajib. The preceding verse criticizes the distribution of charity, so the later verse must be about explaining where the funds go. We also examine the rebuttal that the context equally supports entitlement (ownership).

Guided Path
1
Locate the context verse
Read verse 9:58 about the hypocrites' criticism of charity distribution.
This verse is just before the zakat verse (9:60).
2
Understand the Hanafi inference
The criticism was about where the charity was given, so the purpose of the following verse is to explain the categories of recipients (bayan al-masraf).
Thus the lam indicates allocation.
3
Study the rebuttal from Sharh al-Mukhtasar
The rebuttal says that the context also explains entitlement; if the poor are entitled as owners, the criticism is about not giving them what they deserve.
This rebuttal challenges the exclusive inference to allocation.
4
Evaluate the hadith report from Hunayn
The passage mentions a hadith where the Prophet gave to specific individuals, and the criticism was about giving to some and leaving others. This supports allocation over entitlement.
The author considers this a strong point.
5
Assess the overall strength of the siyaq argument
Despite the rebuttal, the Hanafis maintain that the siyaq strongly favors allocation, especially with the hadith evidence.
The siyaq is a key tool in Hanafi usul.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And among them is their interpretation like the Malikis and Hanbalis? That is, the Hanafis' interpretation like the interpretation of the Malikis and Hanbalis of His saying: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor' (9:60) as indicating the allocation (of the funds) so that it is permissible to give to one category among those categories, despite the fact that the lam is apparently for ownership. So Allah revealed this verse lest they think that they have a choice in preventing or giving. So this indicates that the purpose is to explain the allocation. And it was replied in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that this also achieves the explanation of entitlement, because if they are entitled as owners, then turning away from them is not in the hands of the givers, so it does not justify departure from the apparent meaning. If you say: The criticism remains in giving to only one of the categories; I say: That is not permissible according to them, so that criticism is not invalid. But it has been reported in some hadith works that the Messenger of Allah gave to Abu Sufyan, Muawiyah, and Yazid ibn Abi Sufyan from the spoils of Hunayn, and something was said, so Allah revealed this verse. Then the criticism was due to giving to some and leaving others, and repelling this criticism can only be by explaining the allocations, not by explaining entitlement. And this is a strong point, but the apparent wording of Ibn al-Hajib recoils from it, so reflect. I say: In the response matching what Sadr al-Shariah stated: The generality conflicts with ownership, because every poor person owning every charity is unintelligible, but not for allocation, because every poor person is a valid recipient. So there must be a turn away either from the generality or from the lam. Turning away from generality entails ownership to an unspecified person, because if the word is turned away from generality, then either the genus is intended, meaning the genus of charity is owned by the genus of the poor – which, besides being against their school of giving to three from each category, is ownership to an unspecified person – or collectivity is intended, as in the case of 'nakaarah' (denial), then even though it is a turning away from the lam's reality, it is also ownership to an unspecified person. And that (ownership to an unspecified person) is not known in the Sharia, so turning the lam to allocation is the only correct option, and thus it is not a far-fetched interpretation. And it was answered in Fath al-Qadir with another point: that it is denied that the lam is apparently for ownership and placed for it; rather, the lam is for specification, more general than being on the basis of ownership or other. So interpreting it specifically as ownership is interpreting by the non-apparent without proof, so the [same] problem returns retreating.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the interpretation of the lam in the zakat verse (9:60). The Hanafis, along with Malikis and Hanbalis, interpret the lam as indicating allocation (sarf) of the funds, meaning the zakat is to be distributed to the eight categories, and it is permissible to give to one category only. The Shafi'is interpret the lam as ownership (tamlik), meaning each category must receive a share, and due to the plural form, they require distribution to at least three individuals from each category. The author then presents a defense by Ibn al-Hajib, who argues from the context (siyaq) of the preceding verses (9:58) that the purpose is to explain where the zakat should go, not who owns it. However, a reply in Sharh al-Mukhtasar counters that the context also explains entitlement. The author then mentions a variant hadith where the Prophet gave to specific individuals, showing the criticism was about giving to some and not others, which is better addressed by explaining allocation. The discussion continues with Sadr al-Shariah's point that interpreting 'generality' leads to unintelligible ownership, so the lam must be for allocation. Finally, Fath al-Qadir argues that the lam is for specification (ikhtisas) not necessarily ownership, so the Hanafi interpretation is not a departure from the apparent.

Key Terms
السياق (al-siyaq): The context of the preceding verses that helps determine the meaning.
القرينة (al-qarinah): A contextual clue that helps specify the intended meaning of a text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith of Hunayn mentioned in the passage demonstrate?
A) That the Prophet distributed charity only to the poor.
B) That the criticism was about giving to some and not others, supporting allocation.
C) That the zakat verse is abrogated.
D) That the lam must indicate ownership.

Key Takeaway
The context of 9:58 and the hadith of Hunayn provide strong evidence that the lam in the zakat verse indicates allocation, not ownership.

Linguistic Analysis: Lam for Specification (Ikhtisas)
Linguistic analysis arguing lam is for specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the argument from Fath al-Qadir that the lam is for specification (ikhtisas) and evaluate its implications for the dispute.

Core Idea
The lam is not exclusively for ownership; it is for specification, making the Hanafi interpretation linguistically sound.

This lesson examines the linguistic argument that the lam is fundamentally for specification (ikhtisas), not ownership. Fath al-Qadir argues that assuming the lam is exclusively for ownership is itself a departure from the apparent meaning. This supports the Hanafi interpretation as the more straightforward reading.

Guided Path
1
Understand the default meaning of the lam
The lam in Arabic can indicate ownership, specification, or other relations. The question is which is primary.
The Shafi'is assume ownership is primary.
2
Study the Fath al-Qadir argument
Fath al-Qadir denies that the lam is apparently for ownership; rather it is for specification (ikhtisas), which includes ownership as one possibility.
Thus interpreting it as allocation is not a departure from the apparent.
3
Connect to Sadr al-Shariah's point about generality
Sadr al-Shariah argued that interpreting the verse as giving ownership to every poor person is unintelligible, so allocation is the only valid option.
This supports the idea that ownership cannot be the intended meaning.
4
Evaluate the implication
If the lam is for specification, then the Hanafi interpretation is actually closer to the apparent meaning than the Shafi'i interpretation.
The Shafi'i interpretation now requires additional evidence to prove ownership.
5
Reflect on the reversal of the burden of proof
The argument turns the tables: the Shafi'is must prove that ownership is intended, not the Hanafis for allocation.
This is a powerful linguistic argument.

قلت: لا يجوز عندهم ذلك، فليس ذلك اللمز باطلاً، لكن ورد في بعض الروايات من كتب الحديث أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أعطى أبا سفيان ومعاوية ويزيد بن أبي سفيان من غنائم حنين فقيل ما قيل And among them is their interpretation like the Malikis and Hanbalis? That is, the Hanafis' interpretation like the interpretation of the Malikis and Hanbalis of His saying: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor' (9:60) as indicating the allocation (of the funds) so that it is permissible to give to one category among those categories, despite the fact that the lam is apparently for ownership. Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the interpretation of the lam in the zakat verse (9:60). The Hanafis, along with Malikis and Hanbalis, interpret the lam as indicating allocation (sarf) of the funds, meaning the zakat is to be distributed to the eight categories, and it is permissible to give to one category only. Key Terms
الاختصاص (al-ikhtisas): Specification – the lam indicates that something is specifically for someone, but not necessarily as ownership.
التمليك (al-tamlik): Ownership – the lam indicates that the recipient owns the item.
