Interpretation of the Lam in the Zakah Verse: Ikhtisas vs Tamlik
Discusses the meaning of 'li' in the zakah verse, arguing for ikhtisas over tamlik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that 'al-lam' indicates ikhtisas (allocation) to verse 9:60, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on tamlik.

Core Idea
The lam in the zakah verse means allocation, not ownership — the Prophet and Companions confirmed this by practice.

This lesson unpacks a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the meaning of the preposition 'li' in the zakah verse (9:60). The Hanafi position—that 'li' indicates allocation to categories rather than transfer of ownership—is grounded in usul principles and supported by numerous prophetic practices. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to analyze linguistic markers in the revealed texts and appreciate how different usul frameworks yield divergent fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds the lam to indicate allocation (ikhtisas) to the eight categories, not individual ownership.
This is the core claim of the passage.
2
Identify the Shafi'i argument
Recognize the opposing view: the lam signifies tamlik (ownership), requiring distribution to individuals within each category.
Shafi'is argue the apparent meaning of 'li' in financial contexts is ownership.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Analyze the evidence cited: actions of the Prophet (PBUH) and Companions giving zakah to single categories, and the logical problem of tamlik li-ghayr mu'ayyan.
These are dalil naqli (transmitted proofs) and aqli (rational).
4
Understand the usul principle
Grasp the Hanafi usul that 'li' is haqiqah (literal) for ikhtisas; claiming tamlik is a claim of majaz that requires evidence, which is lacking.
This is the methodological foundation of the Hanafi position.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
See the practical consequence: Hanafi allows giving all zakah to one category as needed; Shafi'i requires at least three from each of eight categories.
This difference affects how zakah is distributed in real communities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الثاني
،
من كتب الحديث أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أعطى أبا سفيان ومعاوية ويزيد بن أبي سفيان من غنائم حنين فقيل ما قيل فأنزل الله تعالى هذه الآية، فاللمز حينئذ بسبب إعطاء البعض وتركهم، ودفع هذا اللمز لا يكون إلا ببيان المصارف لا ببيان الاستحقاق، وهذا وجه وجيه لكن ظاهر عبارة ابن الحاجب ينبو عنه فتدبر (أقول) في الجواب مطابقاً لما أفاد صدر الشريعة العموم) مناف للتمليك فإن تملك كل فقير كل صدقة غير معقول (لا) للمصرف فإن كل فقير يصلح مصرفاً فلا بد من (صرف) إما للعموم وإما للام وصرف العموم يستلزم التمليك لغير معين فإنه إذا انصرف اللفظ عن العموم فإما أن يراد الجنس ويكون المعنى جنس الصدقة مملوك لجنس الفقير فمع كونه خلاف مذهبهم من وجوب الإعطاء للثلاثة من كل صنف تمليك لغير معين أو يكون الجمعية مقصودة كما في النكارة، فمع كونه صرفاً للام عن الحقيقة تمليك أيضاً لغير معين (وهو) أي التمليك لغير المعين (لم يعهد) في الشرع فصرف اللام إلى المصرف هو الوجه لا غير ، فلا يكون تأويلاً بعيداً، وأجاب في «فتح القدير» بوجه آخر هو أن كون اللام ظاهراً في الملك وموضوعـاً لـه ممنوع وإنما اللام للاختصاص أعم من أن يكون على سبيل الملك أو غيره، فالحمل على خصوص الملك حمل على غير الظاهر من غير دليل فرجع المحذور قهقرى هذا (و) قال في التحرير لا ريب في فعل رسول الله وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلك بخلاف قول الشافعية وهو الصرف إلى ثلاثة من كل صنف حيث قسم الذهبة التي بعث بها معاذ من اليمن في المؤلفة فقط) كما نقل الشيخ ابن الهمام في فتح القدير عن أبي عبيدة في كتاب «الأموال» ثم أتاه مال آخر فجعله في صنف الغارمين وفي فتح القدير: قال لقبيصة بن مخارق حين أتاه وقد تحمل جعالة : أقم حتى تأتينا الصدقة فنأمر لك بها وفي حديث سلمة بن صخر البياضي أنه أمر له بصدقة قومه، وذكر في «فتح القدير آثاراً كثيرة عن كبار الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم أجمعين، وإذا ثبت عمل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وعمل أصحابه على هذا النمط علم أن المراد بيان المصرف فليس من التأويلات البعيدة في شيء فافهم
From books of hadith that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) gave Abu Sufyan, Muawiyah, and Yazid bin Abi Sufyan from the spoils of Hunain, so something was said, then Allah revealed this verse. The criticism then was due to giving some and leaving others, and repelling this criticism can only be by explaining the expenditure categories (masarif), not by explaining entitlement. This is a sound point, but the apparent expression of Ibn al-Hajib tends away from it, so reflect. (I say) In response, matching what Sadr al-Shariah stated: (general application) is incompatible with making property (tamlik), because every poor person owning every charity is unreasonable. (No) but for the expenditure, every poor person is suitable as an expenditure, so there must be (disbursement) either for the general or for the lam. And disbursement of the general entails tamlik to an unspecified person, because if the wording is diverted from generality, then either the genus is intended and the meaning is the genus of charity owned by the genus of the poor, then besides being contrary to their school of obligatory giving to three from each category, it is tamlik to an unspecified person; or the collectivity is intended as in [؟], then besides being a diversion of the lam from its reality, it is also tamlik to an unspecified person. (And it) i.e. tamlik to an unspecified person (is not known) in the law; therefore diverting the lam to the expenditure is the only proper way, so it is not a far-fetched interpretation. And in Fath al-Qadir, another answer was given: that the lam being apparent in ownership and placed for it is denied; rather the lam is for allocation, more general than being on the basis of ownership or other. So restricting it to ownership is interpreting it in a non-apparent meaning without evidence, so the objection is reversed. And in al-Tahrir it is said: there is no doubt in the action of the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) and his Companions in contradiction to the Shafi'is' statement of disbursement to three from each category, when he divided the gold sent with Mu'adh from Yemen among the mu'allafa alone, as transmitted by Shaykh Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir from Abu Ubayda in Kitab al-Amwal. Then another wealth came to him, so he gave it to the category of debtors. And in Fath al-Qadir: he said to Qubaysa bin Mukhariq when he came carrying a debt: stay until the charity comes to us, then we will order some for you. And in the hadith of Salama bin Sakhr al-Bayadi: that he ordered some of his people's charity for him. And many reports from great Companions are mentioned in Fath al-Qadir. And when the action of the Messenger of Allah and his Companions is established on this pattern, it is known that the intention is to explain the expenditure, so it is not among far-fetched interpretations, so understand.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh dispute regarding the interpretation of the preposition 'li' in the verse on zakah expenditures (Surah al-Tawbah 9:60). The Shafi'is argue that 'li' indicates tamlik (making the poor owners of the zakah), which would require distributing to at least three individuals from each of the eight categories. The author, commenting on Musallam al-Thubut, defends the Hanafi position that 'li' is for ikhtisas (allocation), meaning the verse only specifies the categories (masarif) entitled to receive zakah, not that each individual must be made owner. He supports this with evidence from the actions of the Prophet (PBUH) and the Companions, who distributed to single categories as needed, as recorded in works like Fath al-Qadir. The argument hinges on a usul principle: 'li' is primarily for allocation, and restricting it to ownership is an unwarranted specification without evidence. Key references include Fath al-Qadir and al-Tahrir, and the author cites instances from the Prophet's distribution of spoils and zakah to refute the Shafi'i view.

Key Terms
اللام (al-lam): The preposition 'li' in the zakah verse; the text argues it is for ikhtisas (allocation), not necessarily tamlik (ownership).
صرف (sarf): Disbursement or expenditure of zakah to the eligible categories (masarif).
تمليك لغير معين (tamlik li-ghayr mu'ayyan): Ownership to an unspecified person, which the author argues is not customary in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, what does the lam in verse 9:60 indicate?
A) Tamlik (ownership) to each poor individual
B) Allocation (ikhtisas) to the categories of recipients
C) Both ownership and allocation equally
D) General meaning with no specific indication

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul holds that the lam in the zakah verse indicates allocation to categories, not individual ownership, a position grounded in prophetic practice and linguistic principle.

Is a Word Equally Used for One and Two Meanings Mujmal?
Hanafi vs. majority dispute on definition of mujmal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on when a word is mujmal, apply the criterion of ghalaba (predominance) to resolve ambiguity, and evaluate the opposing majority argument.

Core Idea
A word is not mujmal if one meaning is more frequent, even if used for multiple meanings.

Does a word like 'dābba'—used for both donkey and horse—become ambiguous in legal texts? The Hanafis argue it does not, because predominant usage fixes the haqīqa. This lesson unpacks the dispute, focusing on the role of frequency and the distinction between lexical ambiguity and lack of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the contested issue: whether a word used equally for one meaning and for two meanings (e.g., dābba for donkey and horse) is considered mujmal (ambiguous) or not.
The Hanafis say no; the majority (including Ibn al-Hajib, Ibn al-Humam) say yes.
2
Understand the Hanafi definition of mujmal
The Hanafis define mujmal as a word whose multiple meanings are equally probable without any predominance. If one meaning is more frequent (ghalaba), the word is not mujmal even if used for another meaning via majāz.
Thus 'dābba' for donkey is haqīqa; for horse, majāz.
3
Analyze the Hanafi arguments
Three arguments: (1) Only ishtirāk leads to ijmal, and it is rare; (2) The word can be carried on majāz, and majāz is better than ishtirāk; (3) Haqā'iq for a single meaning are far more frequent than for two meanings.
The author uses inductive reasoning from linguistic practice.
4
Evaluate the majority counter-argument
The majority claim that if the word is used for both and neither is apparent, that is the essence of ijmal. The Hanafis respond: lack of appearance does not mean both are equally haqīqa; it only reflects ignorance of which is haqīqa.
Therefore, investigation of indicators is required, not blanket ijmal.
5
Apply the thamarah (practical consequence)
In a fiqh text, if 'dābba' appears without context, the Hanafi muftī rules it means donkey; the majority would consider it ambiguous and seek further clarification.
This affects how legal rulings are derived from such texts.

في الحقيقة ليس من الإجمال في شيء فافهم (و) لنا أيضاً (الحقائق لمعنى واحد (أغلب) فيكون في الواحد حقيقة وفي الاثنين مجازاً، كيف ووضع المفرد لم يوجد للاثنين، وهذا إنما يتم لو كان تحرير المسألة في استعمال بالتساوي المعنى الثاني، وإلا فالمظنة لا تعارض المئنة وترجيح إرادة المعنيين بكثرة (الفائدة فيهما، والاستدلال به على نفي الإجمال ليس فيه إثبات الوضع حتى يرد عليه أنه إثبات اللغة بالترجيح، وهو منهي عنه (كما ظن في المختصر) بل إثبات الإرادة بالترجيح ولا نهي عنه، لكنه (مدفوع بأن المظنة لا تعارض (المئنة وما ذكر يفيد مظنة إرادة المعنيين بمرجح تكثير الفائدة، وههنا غلبة وجود الحقائق بمعنى واحد، وإرادته من اللفظ المفرد موجودة غالباً فتدبر المجملون (قالوا) اللفظ المذكور يستعمل لهما وليس أحدهما ظاهراً وكونه لهما مع عدم ظهور أحدهما هو معنى المجمل وهذا يرشدك إلى أنهم أرادوا التساوي بالمعنى الأول، وحينئذ لا يتوجه قوله (أقول) عدم ظهور أحدهما (ممنوع، فإن عدم الظهور ههنا لعدم العلم بالحقيقة) لا لكون كل منهما حقيقة، فيلزم عدم الظهور فعليك بالنظر في الامارات فافهم.
Issue: When the usage of a word is equal for one meaning and two meanings, it is not mujmal, like "dābba" for the donkey, and it also applies to the horse. According to the majority, it is mujmal, and Ibn al-Hajib and Ibn al-Humam chose that. (It should not escape you that determining the point of dispute is problematic. For if by equality is meant equal in both usages, such that each of the one and two are immediately understood in the absence of a context, then ijmal is self-evident and cannot be denied. For its essence reduces to the shared term between one meaning and two meanings being mujmal, and no rational person would deny that. Indeed, then there is no benefit in restricting equality to a meaning or two meanings; rather, this ruling applies to equality whether between one meaning and another meaning, or one meaning and two meanings. But if by equality is meant equality in the usage itself, regardless of whether one of them is immediately understood or not, then probably no rational person would say it is mujmal. How? This is like saying: if a word is used for two meanings, even if one is immediately understood, is it mujmal or not? Then there is no benefit in specification on this [interpretation] either. So the dispute between the two groups is verbal. The one who says [it is] mujmal intended the first meaning of equality, as his proof indicates, while the one who denies it intended the second meaning, as his proofs indicate. For us, there are three probabilities: ishtirak, tawātu', and haqīqa and majāz. Ijmal only applies to the first, not the latter two, so its non-existence is more frequent. But this only holds if there is a common denominator between the one and two, which is not entirely apparent, even if it exists in the given example. For us also: this word is divided between majāz and ishtirak, and majāz is better, so it is carried on the majāz of one of the usages—either one or two—so there is no ijmal, because it is carried on the haqīqa in the absence of context and on the majāz with it. If you say: this only works if its being haqīqa in one of them is known; I say: then consider the indications when there is hesitation to know the haqīqa, and hesitation about the haqīqa is not part of ijmal in any way—understand. For us also: haqā'iq for a single meaning are more frequent, so for one [meaning] it is haqīqa and for two it is majāz. How? The singular is not placed for two. But this only works if the issue is about the usage of a word for one and two as two; but if it is about a word used for a meaning and two meanings such that there is a common denominator between them, then both are understood because they are particular to it, and that is more fitting. For the existence of a word used for two as a dual is hidden and there is no benefit in an issue whose subject is mostly doubtful of existence. The mentioned example also does not fit, so it is not complete—understand. Then these proofs return to the point that non-ijmal is more frequent, so it is preponderant. But this only works if by equality is meant the second meaning; otherwise probability does not oppose certainty. And giving preponderance to intending both meanings by frequency of benefit, and using that as proof to deny ijmal, does not involve establishing the lexical meaning by preponderance, which is prohibited (as thought in al-Mukhtaṣar); rather, it is establishing intention by preponderance, and that is not prohibited. However, it is refuted because probability does not oppose certainty. What has been mentioned gives a probability of intending both meanings by the preponderant factor of increasing benefit, but here the frequent existence of haqā'iq for a single meaning and intending it from the singular word exists frequently—so reflect. The proponents of ijmal said: the mentioned word is used for both and neither is apparent; its being for both with neither apparent is the meaning of mujmal. This guides you to the fact that they intended equality in the first sense. In that case, his statement that neither is apparent is not valid; indeed, lack of appearance here is due to lack of knowledge of the haqīqa, not because both are haqīqa, so lack of appearance follows. Therefore, you must consider the indications—understand.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi response to a usul dispute: whether a word equally used for one meaning and for two meanings (like 'dābba' which can mean donkey or horse) is considered mujmal (ambiguous). The Hanafi position, defended by the author, is that it is not mujmal, contrary to the majority (including Ibn al-Hajib and Ibn al-Humam). The author first clarifies the exact point of dispute, showing that the apparent disagreement is verbal. He then provides multiple arguments: (1) the three categories of word-meaning relationships (ishtirak, tawatu, haqiqa/majaz) – only ishtirak leads to ijmal, and ishtirak is less frequent; (2) the word is either shared or metaphorical, and metaphorical use is preferable therefore it carries the haqiqa meaning in absence of context; (3) haqaiq for a single meaning are more frequent, so the singular meaning is haqiqa and the dual is majaz. He refutes objections, emphasizing that frequency of usage determines non-ijmal, and that the proper analysis involves looking at indicators. The discussion shows the Hanafi reliance on ghalaba (predominance) and istiqra (induction) to resolve ambiguity.

Key Terms
مُجْمَل (mujmal): A word that is ambiguous due to equal probability of multiple meanings without a preferred interpretation.
الاشتراك (ishtirāk): A word used for multiple distinct meanings with equal frequency.
الغَلَبَة (ghalaba): Predominance or frequency of usage that determines the meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the key factor that prevents a word like 'dābba' from being mujmal?
A) The word is always used for only one meaning.
B) The word is more frequently used for one meaning (donkey), so that meaning is haqīqa and the other is majāz.
C) The word is a proper noun, not a common noun.
D) The word is only used metaphorically, so it is never ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses ghalaba (predominance of usage) to determine that a word is not mujmal even if it has multiple meanings, avoiding unnecessary ambiguity in legal texts.

Bayan in Hanafi Usul: Definition and Types of Clarification
Defines bayan and its first two subcategories: tafsir and taqrir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi definition of bayan, classify its types (verbal/non-verbal, mantuq/darurah), and differentiate between bayan tafsir and bayan taqrir with examples.

Core Idea
Bayan is the means by which Allah clarifies His rulings; Hanafis categorize it into verbal and non-verbal, and further into tafsir (explaining ambiguity) and taqrir (confirming clarity).

This lesson introduces the Hanafi classification of bayan (clarification). Understanding bayan is essential for deriving rulings from ambiguous or general texts. We will explore how Hanafi scholars define bayan, its two main divisions, and the first two types of conforming bayan: tafsir and taqrir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two senses of bayan
Bayan can refer to the act of clarification or to the means by which clarification is achieved. In usul, we focus on the latter: the means (Quran, Sunnah, etc.).
The passage states: 'It may be applied to the act of clarification itself, or to that by which clarification is achieved.'
2
Classify bayan into verbal and non-verbal
Hanafis include non-verbal means like the Prophet's actions as bayan. This is unique compared to some other schools.
The text says: 'Bayan in the second sense, according to the Hanafis, is either verbal or non-verbal, like action.'
3
Divide verbal bayan by explicit wording
Verbal bayan is either clarified by its explicit wording (mantuq) or not (darurah). The passage discusses whether implicative indicators (dal i̇ltizami) count as bayan darurah.
The majority holds that dal i̇ltizami is not bayan darurah, but Imam Fakhr al-Islam includes it.
4
Analyze conforming bayan: tafsir
When bayan conforms to the meaning and is mentioned to remove ambiguity, it is bayan tafsir. It clarifies mujmal (ambiguous) and mushtarak (homonym) terms.
Examples: 'Establish prayer' (mujmal) and 'the thief' (general clarified by conditions).
5
Analyze conforming bayan: taqrir
When bayan conforms to the meaning and is mentioned only to remove the possibility of change (e.g., emphasizing a general rule), it is bayan taqrir.
Taqrir does not introduce new information; it confirms the apparent meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث في البيان. قد يطلق على نفس هذا الإظهار وقد يطلق على ما به الإظهار (البيان) بالمعنى الثاني (عند الحنفية إما لفظي أو غيره كالفعل فإنه يتبين به المجمل أيضاً كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى ( والأول) يبين بمنطوقه أولا يبين بمنطوقه وهو بيان الضرورة) ظاهر هذا الكلام يرشد إلى أن الدال الالتزامي لا يسمى بيان الضرورة، وهو الأوفق بكلام الأكثر، قال الإمام فخر الإسلام وهذا نوع من البيان بما لم يوضع له، وهذا يشمل الدال التزاماً أيضاً بظاهره والأول) البيان بالمنطوق، إما موافق للمدلول وإنما ذكره دفعاً لاحتمال مجاز أو خصوص أو تعييناً لأحد محتمليه أو مخالف للمدلول (والأول) وهو البيان الموافق (أما مع الإجمال) أي إجمال ما هو بيان له لعله أراد به خفي المراد على مصطلح الشافعية، وإلا فبيان التفسير لا يختص ببيان المجمل (وهو) بيان تفسير) قال الإمام فخر الإسلام وأما بيان التفسير فبيان المجمل والمشترك، مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلَاةَ وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ﴾ [البقرة:43] ﴿وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ﴾ [المائدة:38] ونحو ذلك، ثم البيان، وعطف المشترك على المجمل من قبيل عطف الخاص على العام من وجه، فإن المشترك قد لا يكون مجملاً نحو أنى شئتم وثلاثة قروء، وقوله: ونحو ذلك، لعله معطوف على المجمل والمراد به سائر أقسام الخفاء لا على الأمثلة كما يوهم ظاهر العبارة، وذهب إليه الشراح، وإلا لكان ينبغي أن يقول: ونحوهما ونحو تينك (ومنه تفسير الكنايات أولاً) مع الإجمال وإنما ذكر لرفع احتمال التغير عن الظاهر (وهو) بيان تقرير كتأكيد الحقيقة والعام
Chapter Three on Bayan. It may be applied to the act of clarification itself, or to that by which clarification is achieved. Bayan in the second sense, according to the Hanafis, is either verbal or non-verbal, like action, for the mujmal is clarified by it as well, as will come. The first type is clarified by its explicit wording or not by its explicit wording, and it is the bayan of necessity. The apparent meaning of this statement indicates that the implicative indicator is not called bayan of necessity, and this is in agreement with the majority. Imam Fakhr al-Islam said: 'And this is a type of bayan by what was not assigned for it, and this includes the implicative indicator apparently as well.' The first is bayan by explicit wording, either conforming to the meaning (and it is mentioned to remove the possibility of metaphor or specification, or to specify one of the possibilities) or contrary to the meaning. The first, which is conforming bayan, is either with ambiguity (i.e., ambiguity of what it clarifies; perhaps he meant hidden meaning in Shafi'i terminology, otherwise tafsir bayan is not specific to clarifying mujmal) and it is bayan tafsir. Imam Fakhr al-Islam said: 'As for bayan tafsir, it is the clarification of mujmal and mushtarak, like His saying: Establish prayer and give zakat, and The thief, male and female, and the like.' Then bayan... joining mushtarak to mujmal is like joining specific to general in a way, for mushtarak may not be mujmal, such as 'however you wish' and 'three periods.' And his saying 'and the like' is probably connected to mujmal, meaning all types of hidden meanings not the examples, as the apparent expression suggests, and the commentators held this; otherwise he should have said 'and the like of them two' or 'the like of those two.' And from it is the interpretation of kinayat, first with ambiguity, and it is mentioned to remove the possibility of change from the apparent, and it is bayan taqrir, like affirming the reality and the general.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on bayan in Hanafi usul. It defines bayan in two senses: the act of clarification and the means of clarification. Hanafis divide bayan into verbal and non-verbal (e.g., actions of the Prophet). Verbal bayan then splits into that which is clarified by its explicit wording (manṭuq) and that which is not (bayan darurah). The text discusses a nuance: the implicative indicator (dal i̇ltizami) is usually not considered bayan darurah according to the majority, but Imam Fakhr al-Islam includes it. Then it details the first type: bayan by manṭuq, which can be either conforming (muwafiq) or contrary (mukhalif). Conforming bayan is subdivided: if it involves ambiguity (ijmal), it is bayan tafsir – the explanation of a mujmal or mushtarak term. Examples from the Quran are given: 'establish prayer and give zakat' clarifies the vague commands, and 'the thief, male and female' clarifies the general term. There is a discussion about whether mushtarak is always mujmal; the author notes it is not always, hence the phrase 'and the like' likely refers to other categories of hidden meanings. Finally, bayan taqrir is introduced as a confirming bayan that removes the possibility of change from the apparent meaning, like emphasizing a general statement.

Key Terms
البيان (al-bayan): Clarification; the act or means of making a legal ruling understood.
بيان التفسير (bayan al-tafsir): Explanation that clarifies a mujmal (ambiguous) or mushtarak (homonym) term.
بيان التقرير (bayan al-taqrir): Confirmation that removes the possibility of change from the apparent meaning, like emphasizing a general or real meaning.
بيان الضرورة (bayan al-darurah): Clarification that is not by explicit wording (manṭuq), e.g., through implication or context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does bayan tafsir (explanatory clarification) address according to this passage?
A) Only legal rulings that are general in scope.
B) Ambiguous (mujmal) and homonym (mushtarak) terms.
C) Only actions of the Prophet that need interpretation.
D) The implicative meanings derived from context.

Key Takeaway
Bayan tafsir resolves ambiguity (mujmal and mushtarak), while bayan taqrir confirms the apparent meaning and prevents arbitrary restriction.

Determining Bayan: Qawl vs Fi'l When They Agree
Determining which of Prophet's qawl or fi'l serves as bayan when they agree

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for identifying the bayan when the Prophet's statement and action agree in meaning, and apply the rule to hypothetical scenarios.

Core Idea
When the Prophet's qawl and fi'l agree, the earlier is bayan; if they differ, the statement is bayan because it is clearer.

In usul al-fiqh, both the Prophet's statements (qawl) and actions (fi'l) can serve as bayan (explanation) of a mujmal (ambiguous text). But when both exist and agree in meaning, which one is the actual bayan? This passage presents the Hanafi analysis, weighing chronological priority and clarity of expression. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the issue: qawl and fi'l as bayan
Understand that both the Prophet's statement and action can serve as explanations (bayan) of a mujmal. The problem is determining which one is the actual bayan when both convey the same meaning.
Bayan lifts ambiguity from the mujmal.
2
Apply the rule of chronological priority
If the timing of the qawl and fi'l is known, the earlier one is the bayan. This is because the first occurrence already clarifies the intended meaning.
If both occur simultaneously, further analysis is needed.
3
Handle the case of unknown chronology
If it is unknown which came first, then either could be the bayan without preference, since specifying one is arbitrary. However, some scholars argue that the weaker in indication (usually the action) is preferred to allow the stronger (statement) to serve as emphasis. This is refuted by induction from linguistic usage.
The passage uses the example 'the people all came' to show emphasis is weaker in independent contexts.
4
Resolve when qawl and fi'l differ in meaning
When the statement and action have different legal indications (e.g., one suggests one tawaf, the other suggests two), the chosen view is that the statement is the bayan absolutely, whether it came before or after. This is because the statement is more explicit and less likely to include extra elements (like recommended acts or concessions). The objection that the earlier action being bayan would require abrogation is dismissed as acceptable when evidence demands.
The passage cites the example of tawaf for Hajj and Umrah.

Source Text

مسألة
(القول والفعل إذا اتفقا في المفاد (وعلم المتقدم) منهما (فهو البيان) لأن التعريف حصل به (والا) علم المتقدم ( فأحدهما) البيان من غير ترجيح إذ الحكم على التعيين تحكم ولا حاجة إليه أيضاً (وقيل : المرجوح في الدلالة (مقدم لأن الراجح يؤخر للتأكيد) والمتقدم يكفي للتفهيم، فهو المراد وأجيب ذلك أي كون التأكيد راجحاً على المؤكد (في المفردات نحو : جاءني القوم كلهم دون المستقل فإنه يجوز فيه مرجوحة التأكيد (بالاستقراء، وإن اختلفا أي القول والفعل في المفاد (كما) روي أنه عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام (طاف طوافين) قد روى النسائي عن حماد بن عبد الرزاق الأنصاري عن إبراهيم محمد ابن الحنفية قال : طفت مع أبي وقد جمع الحج والعمرة، فطاف لهما طوافين، وسعى لهما سعيين، وحدثني أن علياً رضي الله عنه فعل ذلك، وحدثه أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم فعل ذلك . قال الشيخ ابن الهمام في فتح القدير: حماد هذا وإن ضعف لكن ذكره ابن حبان في «الثقات» ، وفي الحديث الطويل المروي لمسلم عن جابر إشارة إلى تكرر الطواف وأمر بواحد كما روى الترمذي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : من أحرم بالحج والعمرة أجزأه طواف واحد وسعي واحد منهما حتى يحل منهما» وقال : حديث صحيح غريب (فالمختار القول) للبيانية (مطلقاً) تقدم على الفعل أو تأخر (لأنه أظهر) وأدل في تعيين المراد) فإن الفعل ربما يشتمل على الزوائد من المندوبات (والفعل الزائد) إن كان ندب أو واجب مختص به عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام (والنقصان) إن كان في الفعل (تخفيف في حقه صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم (وقال أبو الحسين المتقدم) هو البيان أيّاً كان من القول أو الفعل (ورد) بلزوم النسخ عليه وهو خلاف الأصل ( (لو كان المتقدم الفعل فإنه إذا تقدم طوافان) وكان هذا الفعل بياناً للمجمل (وجب علينا طوافان، فإذا أمر بطواف واحد فقد نسخ أحدهما عنا فإن قلت له أن يلتزم النسخ لأن وجوب طوافين إنما يكون عند دليل التأسي وحينئذٍ دل الدليل على النسخ، قلت: ليس وجوب الطوافين بالفعل يحتاج إلى دليل التأسي، بل بالمجمل ، كذا في الحاشية»، ولو خصص قوله بما فيه دليل التأسي آل النزاع لفظياً .
،
اعلم أن الحق هذا القول واختاره الآمدي ولم يوجد أيضاً في كتبنا ما ينافيه، فإن المتقدم مفهم للمراد قطعاً فلا إجمال ،بعده ، وأما لزوم النسخ فلا بأس به عند اقتضاء الدليل، وأما اشتمال الفعل على المندوبات فلا نسلم ذلك إذا وقع بعد المجمل إلا إذا دل دليل صارف عن البيانية، على أن المجمل باق على إجماله وفي هذا القول والفعل سواء فتأمل .
Issue: (The statement and the action if they agree in meaning (and the earlier is known) then it is the explanation, because definition is obtained by it. (Otherwise, if the earlier is not known, then either of them is the explanation without preference, since specifying it is arbitrary and unnecessary. (And it is said: the weaker in indication is preferred, because the stronger is delayed for emphasis, and the earlier suffices for comprehension, so it is intended. And that was answered, i.e., that emphasis is stronger than the emphasized (in individual terms like 'the people all came' but not in independent [contexts]? because it is permissible for emphasis to be weaker (by induction. And if they differ, i.e., the statement and action in meaning (as it is narrated that he (peace be upon him and his family and companions) performed two tawafs). Al-Nasa'i narrated from Hammad ibn 'Abd al-Razzaq al-Ansari from Ibrahim Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyya: I performed tawaf with my father, and he had combined Hajj and Umrah, so he performed two tawafs for them and two sa'is for them, and he told me that 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) did that, and he told him that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) did that. Shaykh Ibn al-Humann said in Fath al-Qadir: This Hammad is weak but Ibn Hibban mentioned him in al-Thiqat, and in the long hadith narrated by Muslim from Jabir there is indication of multiple tawafs, and he commanded one, as al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both): The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'Whoever enters ihram for Hajj and Umrah, one tawaf and one sa'i suffice for both until he becomes halal from them.' He said: A saheeh ghareeb hadith. (So the chosen is the statement) for explanation (absolutely), whether it precedes or follows the action, (because it is more apparent and more indicative in specifying the intended meaning). Indeed, the action may include extras from recommended acts, (and the extra action) if it is recommended or an obligation specific to him (peace be upon him and his family and companions) (and the deficiency) if in the action (is a concession for him). (And Abu al-Husayn said: the earlier is the explanation, whichever of statement or action it be. (It was objected) by the necessity of abrogation, which is contrary to the original principle. (If the action is earlier, e.g., two tawafs preceded) and this action was an explanation of the mujmal, (then two tawafs would be obligatory upon us. So if he commanded one tawaf, then one of them has been abrogated for us. If you say: He may accept abrogation because the obligation of two tawafs only occurs due to the evidence of following, and then the evidence indicates abrogation. I say: The obligation of two tawafs by the action does not need evidence of following; rather it is due to the mujmal. As in the hashya. And if his statement is specified with what contains evidence of following, the dispute becomes verbal.)
Know that the truth is this statement, and al-Amidi chose it, and nothing contradictory is found in our books. The earlier certainly conveys the intended meaning, so there is no ambiguity after it. As for the necessity of abrogation, there is no harm when evidence requires it. As for the action including recommended acts, we do not concede that when it occurs after a mujmal unless there is evidence diverting from explanation, while the mujmal remains in its ambiguity. In this, both statement and action are equal. So reflect.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul principle of how the Prophet's statement (qawl) and action (fi'l) function as bayan (explanation) when they agree in meaning. The author presents multiple positions: if the earlier of the two is known, that one is the bayan. If not, either could be the bayan without preference. Another view says the weaker in indication (the action) is preferred because the stronger (statement) is delayed for emphasis. This is refuted by induction from examples like 'the people all came' where emphasis is weaker. When qawl and fi'l differ in meaning, the chosen view is that the statement is bayan absolutely because it is clearer. The objection that taking the earlier action as bayan would imply abrogation is addressed: abrogation is acceptable when evidence indicates. The author concludes that the correct view is that the earlier is bayan (statement or action), as chosen by al-Amidi and consistent with Hanafi books. The action may include recommended elements, so it is not a pure explanation unless proved otherwise.

Key Terms
البيان (al-bayan): الإيضاح للمجمل سواء كان بقول أو فعل
المجمل (al-mujmal): ما لا يفيد المراد بظاهره ويحتاج إلى بيان
القول (al-qawl): كلام النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الصادر بصفة التشريع
الفعل (al-fi'l): فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الصادر على وجه القدوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the chosen view when the Prophet's qawl and fi'l differ in meaning?
A) The action is the bayan because it is more emphatic.
B) The statement is the bayan absolutely because it is clearer.
C) Neither is bayan; both are subject to further evidence.
D) The earlier one is bayan, whichever it may be.

Key Takeaway
When the Prophet's qawl and fi'l agree in meaning, the earlier is the bayan; when they differ, the statement is the bayan because it is more explicit.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Equality of Bayan and Mubayyan in the Hanafi School
Discussion on whether the bayan must be stronger than the mubayyan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the required strength of a bayan relative to the mubayyan, identify the opposing view, and apply the Hanafi argument to a scenario.

Core Idea
The bayan (clarifier) does not need to be stronger than the mubayyan — equality suffices in both authenticity and meaning.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut, the author addresses a key usul dispute: must a clarificatory text (bayan) be stronger than the text it clarifies (mubayyan)? The Hanafi school, along with many others, holds that equality is sufficient, while Fakhr al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib argue for strength in meaning. This lesson breaks down the arguments, the evidence from the Quran, and the Hanafi rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafis allow equality in both thubut (authenticity) and dalala (indication). The bayan need not be stronger.
This is the relied-upon view.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Fakhr al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib require the bayan to be stronger in dalala, though they allow equality in thubut.
Their concern is arbitrariness (tahakkum).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Specification of a general by another general occurs frequently in the Shari'ah. For example, the verse 'Allah permitted trade and forbade usury' shows the prohibition of usury specifying the general permission of trade.
The two texts are equal in strength.
4
Evaluate the counter-argument
The objection of tahakkum is refuted because (1) applying both texts is better than discarding one, and (2) contextual clues (qara'in) indicate which is the mukhassis.
Thus no arbitrary preference.
5
Examine the cross-madhhab critique
The Hanafi response also points out inconsistencies in the opposing view, such as their allowance of specification by khabar wahid despite requiring strength in dalala.
This strengthens the Hanafi position.

تحرر
في الظاهر يجوز المساواة بينهما أي بين البيان والمبين عندنا وعند الأكثر من أغيارنا (ومنهم الإمام فخر الدين الرازي وابن الحاجب يجب أن يكون البيان أقوى دلالة وأما في الثبوت فلا تجب القوّة عندهم، فإنهم يجوّزون تخصيص عام الكتاب بخبر الواحد (و) قال (أبو الحسين يجوز الأدنى دلالة في التبيين، وهو خلاف المعقول (كما في المجمل) يجوز تبيينه بالأدنى اتفاقاً. ظاهر هذا يدل على أن يجوز في بيانه الأدنى منه دلالة، وهو فاسد، فإنه لا شيء أدنى من المجمل، فإنه لا يدل على المراد والبيان يدل ففيه نوع قوة منه، فالأصوب أن المسألة عامة في المساواة ثبوتاً أو دلالة، وينسب خلاف الأكثر إلى الأول وأبي الحسين في الثاني، ويدعي الإنفاق في المجمل في الأول لنا أقول: تخصيص العام بالعام وهو أخص) من المخصص به مطلقاً أو من وجه (واقع) البتة بالاستقراء الصحيح كيف لا وأكثر الشرع عمومات، وهما متساويان، أما عندنا فلأن العام قطعي الدلالة وأما عند غيرنا فلأنه ظني، فقد ثبت التخصيص بالمساوي، فإن قلت فيه تحكم بترجيح أحدهما على الآخر، قال: (وليس هذا تحكماً، لأن أعمالهما خير من إلغاء أحدهما عند المعارضة بخلاف الأدنى، إذ لا معارضة هناك بل يضمحل الأدنى، وأيضاً إن قرينة السباق والسياق أو غيرهما تدل على أن أحدهما مخصص دون العكس فلا تحكم، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَحَلَ اللهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبوا [البقرة: ٢٧٥] القطع بكون الثاني مخصصاً فما في التحرير) في الجواب أن المراد) لمشايخنا (المساواة في الثبوت) فيجوز تخصيص المتواتر بالمتواتر، والآحاد بالآحاد، (لا في حتى يلزم التحكم (مما لا حاجة إليه فإنه قد تم الكلام بدون هذا التكلف الذي ليس له أثر في كلامهم، كيف ويلزم التحكم أيضاً عند التساوي في الثبوت، وربما يورد على التحرير بأنهم يجوزون تخصيص المخصوص من الكتاب بالقياس مع كونه غير أقوى في الدلالة منه، وقد مر منا أنه بعد التخصيص يصير العام أضعف من القياس فتذكر الأكثرون (قالوا) لا بد من القوة، وإلا فإما بالمساوي أو المرجوح وبطلان الأول لأن في التساوي التحكم) إذ لا أحقية لأحدهما في البيانية (و) بطلان الثاني لأنه (في المرجوح) يلزم (إلغاء الراجح) لمعارضة المرجوح إياه، وهذا خلاف المعقول وقد ظهر لك جوابه يأتم وجه (أقول) هذا (منقوض بتخصيص العموم بالمفهوم المخالف لأن المنطوق أقوى منه فينبغي أن لا يجوز مع أنه يجوز عند قائليه (فتأمل) ولا يرد عليه أن المصنف قد منع تخصيصه للعام، ففي كلامه تعارض، لأن ما مر هو التحقيق، والذي قال ههنا مماشاة مع الخصم وإبداء الخلل في كلامه.
The first principle: the Book. Issue 57: It is clear that equality between them (i.e., between bayan and mubayyan) is permissible according to us and most of our opponents. (Among them, Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib require bayan to be stronger in indication, but in thubut they do not require strength, for they allow specification of a general (amm) verse of the Book by khabar wahid.) (And) Abu al-Husayn said: weaker in indication is permissible in clarifying, which is contrary to reason. (As in the mujmal: clarification by a weaker is permissible by consensus.) The apparent meaning is that it is permissible to clarify with something weaker in indication, but that is corrupt, because nothing is weaker than the mujmal, which does not indicate what is intended, while bayan does indicate, so it has some strength over it. The more correct view is that the issue is general: equality in thubut or indication. The dispute of the majority is attributed to the first, and Abu al-Husayn to the second, while consensus is claimed regarding the mujmal on the first. For us, I say: specification of a general by a general—which is more specific absolutely or in some respect—actually occurs by sound induction, because most of Shari'ah consists of generalities, and they are equal. According to us, because the general is definitive in indication; according to others, because it is probable. So specification by an equal is established. If you say: This is arbitrary preference of one over the other. He said: This is not arbitrary, because applying both is better than discarding one when they conflict, contrary to a weaker, which has no conflict but rather collapses. Also, qara'in of context and the like indicate that one is a mukhassis, not the other, so there is no arbitrariness. As in His saying: {Allah permitted trade and forbade usury} (2:275); it is certain that the second is a mukhassis. So in al-Tahrir, the answer is that our scholars intended equality in thubut, so that mutawatir can specify mutawatir, and ahad can specify ahad, not [in indication]—otherwise arbitrariness would follow. This is unnecessary because the speech is complete without this affectation. Moreover, arbitrariness would also follow from equality in thubut. It might be objected to al-Tahrir that they permit specification of something specified from the Book by qiyas even though it is not stronger in indication, and we have already mentioned that after specification, the general becomes weaker than qiyas. So the majority say: strength is necessary, otherwise either with equal or weaker. The first is invalid because equality leads to arbitrariness, since neither has more right to be clarificatory. The second is invalid because the weaker leads to discarding the stronger due to its opposition, which is irrational. The answer has already appeared. I say: This is refuted by specification of a general by a contradictory concept (mafhum mukhalafah), because the explicit (mantuq) is stronger, so it should not be allowed, yet it is allowed by its proponents. So reflect. It is not an objection that the author prohibited its specification of the general, for there is contradiction in his words. What preceded is the investigation, and what he said here is accommodating the opponent and showing the flaw in his words.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh discussion about the relationship between bayan (clarification) and mubayyan (the thing clarified). The question is whether the bayan must be stronger in evidence than the mubayyan. The Hanafi position, along with most scholars, holds that equality in both thubut (authenticity) and dalala (indication) is permissible. Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib require the bayan to be stronger in dalala, though they allow equality in thubut. Abu al-Husayn al-Basri even allows weaker dalala, but this is considered irrational. The author presents evidence that specification of a general by another general is common in the Shari'ah, for example, the verse 'Allah permitted trade and forbade usury'—the forbiddance of usury specifies the general permission of trade. The argument that equality leads to arbitrariness (tahakkum) is refuted by noting that applying both texts is better than ignoring one, and that contextual clues (qara'in) often indicate which is the mukhassis. The passage also critiques the view of those who insist on strength, showing that it leads to problems with specification by mafhum mukhalafah.

Key Terms
بيان (bayan): A text that clarifies a previously ambiguous text
مبين (mubayyan): The text being clarified
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term to exclude some of its individuals

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, can a general text (amm) be specified by another general text (amm) of equal strength?
A) No
B) Yes
C) Only if stronger
D) Only if weaker

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that a clarificatory text (bayan) can be equal in strength to the text it clarifies (mubayyan), as demonstrated by many scriptural examples.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Equality Between Mubayyin and Mubayyan in Strength
Ruling on equality between mubayyin and mubayyan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on equality between the clarifier and the clarified, and evaluate the objection of arbitrary preference (tahakkum) using the principle of giving effect to both texts.

Core Idea
The clarifier need not be stronger; equality is permissible, and contextual clues prevent arbitrary preference.

In usul al-fiqh, one of the key questions is the relationship between a text that clarifies (bayan) and the text being clarified (mubayyan). Must the clarifier be stronger in evidentiary weight? The Hanafi school argues that equality is sufficient, drawing on widespread practice in the Shari’ah. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the Hanafi proof from induction (istiqra) and the Quran, and the refutation of the charge of arbitrary preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Determine what exactly is contested: Hanafis permit equality in thubut and dalala; the majority (including Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib) require the clarifier to be stronger in dalala.
Equality in thubut (e.g., both mutawatir) is conceded by many opponents.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is based on induction (istiqra): specification of a general by another general occurs frequently in the Shari’ah. The Quranic verse 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' (2:275) exemplifies this.
The verse shows that a general permission (trade) is specified by a general prohibition (usury) – both are equal in strength.
3
Analyze the objection and response
The opposition argues that equality leads to arbitrary preference (tahakkum). The Hanafi response: giving effect to both texts is better than nullifying one, and contextual clues (qarina) resolve which is the specifier.
Contextual clues include the immediate context (siyaq) and broader textual evidence.
4
Consider the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis permit specifying a mutawatir by a mutawatir and an ahad by ahad, while opponents require the specifier to be stronger in dalala.
This affects how conflicting texts are reconciled in fatwa and interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
في الظاهر يجوز المساواة بينهما أي بين البيان والمبين عندنا وعند الأكثر من أغيارنا (ومنهم الإمام فخر الدين الرازي وابن الحاجب) يجب أن يكون البيان أقوى دلالة وأما في الثبوت فلا تجب القوّة عندهم، فإنهم يجوّزون تخصيص عام الكتاب بخبر الواحد (و) قال (أبو الحسين) يجوز الأدنى دلالة في التبيين، وهو خلاف المعقول (كما في المجمل) يجوز تبيينه بالأدنى اتفاقاً. ظاهر هذا يدل على أن يجوز في بيانه الأدنى منه دلالة، وهو فاسد، فإنه لا شيء أدنى من المجمل، فإنه لا يدل على المراد والبيان يدل ففيه نوع قوة منه، فالأصوب أن المسألة عامة في المساواة ثبوتاً أو دلالة، وينسب خلاف الأكثر إلى الأول وأبي الحسين في الثاني، ويدعي الإنفاق في المجمل في الأول لنا أقول: تخصيص العام بالعام وهو أخص من المخصص به مطلقاً أو من وجه واقع البتة بالاستقراء الصحيح كيف لا وأكثر الشرع عمومات، وهما متساويان، أما عندنا فلأن العام قطعي الدلالة وأما عند غيرنا فلأنه ظني، فقد ثبت التخصيص بالمساوي، فإن قلت فيه تحكم بترجيح أحدهما على الآخر، قال: (وليس هذا تحكماً، لأن أعمالهما خير من إلغاء أحدهما عند المعارضة بخلاف الأدنى، إذ لا معارضة هناك بل يضمحل الأدنى، وأيضاً إن قرينة السباق والسياق أو غيرهما تدل على أن أحدهما مخصص دون العكس فلا تحكم، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَحَلَ اللهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبوا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٥] القطع بكون الثاني مخصصاً فما في التحرير) في الجواب أن المراد لمشايخنا (المساواة في الثبوت) فيجوز تخصيص المتواتر بالمتواتر، والآحاد بالآحاد، (لا في حتى يلزم التحكم (مما لا حاجة إليه فإنه قد تم الكلام بدون هذا التكلف الذي ليس له أثر في كلامهم، كيف ويلزم التحكم أيضاً عند التساوي في الثبوت، وربما يورد على التحرير بأنهم يجوزون تخصيص المخصوص من الكتاب بالقياس مع كونه غير أقوى في الدلالة منه، وقد مر منا أنه بعد التخصيص يصير العام أضعف من القياس فتذكر الأكثرون (قالوا) لا بد من القوة، وإلا فإما بالمساوي أو المرجوح وبطلان الأول لأن في التساوي التحكم إذ لا أحقية لأحدهما في البيانية (و) بطلان الثاني لأنه (في المرجوح) يلزم (إلغاء الراجح) لمعارضة المرجوح إياه، وهذا خلاف المعقول وقد ظهر لك جوابه يأتم وجه (أقول) هذا (منقوض بتخصيص العموم بالمفهوم المخالف لأن المنطوق أقوى منه فينبغي أن لا يجوز مع أنه يجوز عند قائليه (فتأمل) ولا يرد عليه أن المصنف قد منع تخصيصه للعام، ففي كلامه تعارض، لأن ما مر هو التحقيق، والذي قال ههنا مماشاة مع الخصم وإبداء الخلل في كلامه.
Issue: In appearance, equality between them (i.e., between the clarifier and the clarified) is permitted according to us and according to most of our opponents (including Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib, who hold that the clarifier must be stronger in indication. As for in thubut, they do not require strength, for they permit specifying a general from the Book by a solitary report. (And) Abu al-Husayn said: the inferior in indication is permitted in clarification, which is contrary to reason. (As for the mujmal), clarifying it by the inferior is permitted by agreement. The apparent meaning of this indicates that it is permitted for its clarification to be inferior to it in indication, and this is corrupt, for there is nothing inferior to the mujmal, since it does not indicate the intended meaning, whereas the clarification does indicate, so it has a kind of strength over it. So the more correct view is that the issue is general regarding equality in thubut or indication, and the majority's disagreement is attributed to the first, and Abu al-Husayn's to the second, and consensus is claimed for the first regarding the mujmal. I say: Specification of a general by a general (which is more specific than what is specified by it absolutely or in some respect) is absolutely established by sound induction. Why not? Most of the Shari'a consists of general texts, and they are equal. According to us, because the general is definitive in indication; according to others, because it is presumptive. So specification by an equal is established. If you say: this involves arbitrary preference (tahakkum) of one over the other, he said: This is not arbitrary preference, because giving effect to both is better than nullifying one when they conflict, unlike the case of the inferior, where there is no conflict, but the inferior collapses. Also, contextual clues (qarinat al-siyaq wa al-siyyaq) or others indicate that one is the specifier and not the opposite, so no arbitrariness. As in His statement: 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' [2:275], where it is certain that the second is the specifier. So what is in al-Tahrir? In the answer: what is meant by our shuyukh is equality in thubut, so specifying mutawatir by mutawatir and ahad by ahad is permitted, not in indication, so that arbitrariness would be required. This is unnecessary, because the discussion is complete without this affectation, which has no trace in their statements. How? Arbitrariness would also occur when they are equal in thubut. And it may be objected to al-Tahrir that they permit specifying a specific part of the Book by analogical reasoning (qiyas) even though it is not stronger in indication than it. And it has passed from us that after specification, the general becomes weaker than qiyas. So the majority said: strength is necessary; otherwise, it is either by an equal or by an inferior. The first is invalid because in equality there is arbitrariness, since neither has priority in clarity; and the second is invalid because in the inferior, nullification of the stronger is required due to the inferior's contravening it, and this is contrary to reason. Their answer has appeared to you in due manner. I say: This is undermined by specifying a general by a conflicting implication (mafhum mukhalif), because the articulated expression (mantuq) is stronger than it, so it should not be permitted, yet it is permitted by its proponents. (Reflect.) And it is not refuted by the fact that the author has prohibited specifying the general by it, for in his statement there is contradiction, because what has passed is the verification, and what he said here is an accommodation with the opponent and showing the flaw in his statement.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the permissibility of equality between the mubayyin (clarifier) and the mubayyan (the clarified) in usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi school holds that the mubayyin can be equal in strength (in thubut or dalala) to the mubayyan. This is based on the widespread practice of takhsis (specification) of general texts by other general texts, as found through induction (istiqra). For example, the verse 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' shows that the general ruling on permissibility of trade is specified by the general prohibition of usury. The Hanafis argue that giving effect to both texts is better than nullifying one, and contextual clues (qarina) often indicate which text is the specifier, thus avoiding arbitrary preference (tahakkum). The passage also discusses the view of Abu al-Husayn al-Basri who permits the inferior in dalala, and the majority (Fakhr al-Razi, Ibn al-Hajib) who require the clarifier to be stronger. The Hanafis respond that the opponents' objection about tahakkum in equality is refuted by contextual clues and the principle that giving effect to both is preferable. The passage ends with a critical point: the Hanafi position is consistent even with permitting specification by a conflicting implication (mafhum mukhalif), showing that the clarifier need not be stronger.

Key Terms
البيان والمبين (al-bayan wa al-mubayyan): The clarifier (bayan) and the clarified (mubayyan). Bayan is the text that explains or specifies another text.
المساواة ثبوتاً أو دلالة (al-musawat thubutan aw dalalan): Equality in authority (thubut) or in indication (dalala). Thubut refers to the chain of transmission; dalala refers to the clarity of meaning.
تحكم (tahakkum): Arbitrary preference without justification. The opponents argue that choosing one of two equal texts as the specifier is arbitrary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is permissible regarding the relationship between the mubayyin (clarifier) and the mubayyan (the clarified)?
A) The mubayyin must always be stronger than the mubayyan in both thubut and dalala.
B) The mubayyin may be equal to the mubayyan in thubut and dalala.
C) The mubayyin must be weaker than the mubayyan.
D) The mubayyin must be stronger in thubut but can be weaker in dalala.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits equality between the clarifier and the clarified, relying on induction and contextual clues to avoid arbitrary preference.

Hanafi Refutation of Ease Verses Against Abrogation
Hanafi usul refutation of opponent's proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi use of 'al-lam li al-'ahd' to specify a general Quranic verse and apply this method to refute an opponent's argument from the same verse.

Core Idea
The lam in 'al-yusr' is for covenant, not generality — ease is contextual, not universal.

In this passage, the Hanafi school responds to an opponent's argument that Quranic verses promising ease and betterment invalidate abrogation that leads to heavier obligations. The opponent cites Surah al-Baqarah 2:185 and 2:106. The Hanafi reply demonstrates a sophisticated usul approach: firstly, by specifying the verse using 'al-lam li al-'ahd', and secondly, by reinterpreting the term 'khayr' as betterness in consequence rather than worldly ease. This lesson examines these two refutations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's argument
The opponent claims that the Quran promises ease (yusr) and better (khayr) in 2:185 and 2:106, thus abrogation that imposes heavier rulings contradicts these promises.
This is based on taking the verses as general and absolute.
2
Analyze the Hanafi response to 2:185
Explain the Hanafi claim that 'al-lam li al-'ahd' specifies the verse to the context of fasting in travel/illness. Note the support from Ibn Abbas.
The ease is specifically the permission to break fast, not a general principle.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to 2:106
Explain the Hanafi reinterpretation of 'khayr' as better in consequence (khayr 'āqibah), not easier in this world. The heavier ruling is better for the afterlife.
Abrogation occurs when the original command becomes evil; the new ruling, even if heavy, is better.
4
Synthesize the Hanafi method
Show how the Hanafi approach combines textual specification (takhsis) and interpretive redirection to defend the validity of abrogation that results in heavier rulings.
Both responses rely on contextual evidence and usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر أنه ليس في النقل من الأيسر إلى الأثقل يسر (قلنا : سياقهما أي الكريمتين (للمال) والآخرة (فالتخفيف تخفيف الحساب) في الأولى والعسر العقاب واليسر تكثير الثواب في الثانية، ولو سلم أن المراد التخفيف الدنيوي، وكذا العسر واليسر فلا نسلم أن هناك عموماً فإنه من البين أن ليس المعنى يريد الله جميع أنواع التخفيف واليسر، كيف حينئذ لا تكليف أصلاً ولا الوقوع في الشدائد بل لتخفيف أمر نسبي وكذا العسر واليسر، فلم يرد العسر الذي يؤدي إلى تلف النفس أو زيادة المرض وأراد اليسر والتخفيف، فأوجب ما لا يوجبهما في ظنه كما في الصوم، بل نقول : قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن كَانَ مَرِيضًا أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ يُرِيدُ اللهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْمُسْرَ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٥] فالظاهر أن اللام للعهد فاليسر يسر الإفطار في السفر والمرض، والعسر عسر الصوم فيهما، ويؤيده ما روى البيهقي وابن أبي حاتم وابن جرير وعن ابن عباس في قوله : يُرِيدُ اللَّهُ بِكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلَا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْعُسْرَ ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸٥] قال : اليسر الإفطار في السفر والعسر الصوم في السفر، وبما قررنا ظهر لك أن لا وجه لما في الحاشية) ، ولا يخفى ضعف هذا الإيراد وسقط توجيهه بأن اللام ليست عاهدة فهي للعموم فافهم ولو سلم العموم أيضاً (مخصوص بثقال التكاليف بالاتفاق) فيخص بالتكليف الناسخ أيضاً لدلالة الدليل والعقل قرينة التخصيص (أقول ولو سلم) أن الكريمتين غير مخصوصتين بثقال التكاليف ( فمعناه) أي معنى ذلك القول الكريم (يريد التخفيف واليسر مهما أمكن في نفس الأمر (ولما تغيرت المصلحة لا يمكن منه تعالى، لأنه قبيح يجب تنزيهه تعالى منه وتحقيقه أن نسبة الشرع إلى الأفعال نسبة الطب إلى الأبدان كما في المبادىء الإحكامية، فلا يحكم الشرع إلا بما فيه حسن أو قبح، فرعاية المصلحة واجبة بالنظر إلى الحكمة ولا يمكن بالنظر إلى الحكمة حكم إلا بما فيه إفضاء إلى الثواب وتخليص عن العقاب فلما تغير الفعل الأخف من الافضاء المذكور وصار الفعل الأثقل مفضياً مثل إفضائه في نفس الأمر لم يمكن الحكم بالأخف وتعيين الأثقل بالحكم فافهم (و) قالوا (ثالثاً) قال تعالى: مَا نَنسَخ مِنْ ءَايَةٍ أَوْ نُنسِهَا نَأْتِ بِخَيْرٍ مِنْهَا أَوْ مِثْلِهَا ﴾ [البقرة: ١٠٦] وظاهر أن الأيسر خير في حقه دون الأثقل (والجواب : أنه خير عاقبة لأن النسخ إنما يرد هو إذا صار المأمور المنسوخ قبيحاً، فالنهي عنه أو إيجاب ما هو حسن مقامه، ولو أثقل خير له في العاقبة، وهذه الخيرية هي المرادة في الآية فإن قلت قد روي عن ابن عباس حمله على الخيرية الدنيوية في المشقة وعدمها قلنا لو سلم صحته فتأويل الراوي لا يكون حجة لا سيما إذا قام الدليل على خلافه فتدبر أو المراد الخيرية (لفظاً) في الإعجاز والفصاحة والبلاغة وقد مر من قبل .
And it is apparent that there is no ease in transferring from the lighter to the heavier. We say: The context of the two noble verses (is about) wealth and the Hereafter; so the lightening is lightening of the account in the first, and the hardship is punishment, and the ease is multiplication of reward in the second. Even if it is granted that the intended meaning is worldly lightening, and likewise hardship and ease, we do not concede that there is generality, for it is clear that the meaning is not 'God wills all types of lightening and ease', otherwise there would be no obligation at all and no falling into hardships, but rather it is a relative lightening of a matter, and likewise hardship and ease. So He did not intend hardship that leads to destruction of the soul or increase of illness, and He intended ease and lightening, so He made obligatory what does not cause them in His opinion, as in fasting. Rather, we say: Allah Almighty said: 'And whoever is ill or on a journey, then a number of other days. Allah intends ease for you and does not intend hardship for you' [2:185]. So it is apparent that the lam is for covenant: so ease is the ease of breaking the fast in travel and illness, and hardship is the hardship of fasting in them. And this is supported by what al-Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Hatim, and Ibn Jarir narrated from Ibn Abbas regarding His statement: 'Allah intends ease for you and does not intend hardship for you' [2:185]; he said: ease is breaking the fast in travel, and hardship is fasting in travel. And by what we have established, it becomes clear to you that there is no basis for what is in the gloss. And the weakness of this objection is not hidden, and its justification that the lam is not for covenant but for generality falls flat. And if the generality is also conceded, (it is) specified by the heavy burdens of obligations by consensus; so it is also specified by the abrogating obligation due to the indication of the evidence and reason as a contextual indicator of specification. I say: and even if it is granted that the two noble verses are not specified to the heavy burdens of obligations, then its meaning—i.e., the meaning of that noble statement—(is that He intends) lightening and ease as much as possible in reality. And when the benefit changes, it is not possible from Him, Exalted, because it is vile and He must be exalted from it. And its verification is that the relation of the Law to actions is like the relation of medicine to bodies, as in the Usul al-Ahkam. So the Law does not rule except with what contains goodness or evil. So considering benefit is obligatory with regard to wisdom, and it is not possible with regard to wisdom to rule except with what leads to reward and deliverance from punishment. So when the lighter action changes from the mentioned leading, and the heavier action becomes leading like its leading in reality, it is not possible to rule with the lighter, and the heavier is determined by the ruling. So understand. And they said, thirdly: He, Exalted, said: 'We do not abrogate a verse or cause it to be forgotten but that We bring better than it or similar to it' [2:106]. And it is apparent that the easier is better for him, not the heavier. And the answer: it is better in consequence, because abrogation only occurs when the commanded abrogated action becomes evil, so it is prohibited or what is good is made obligatory in its place, even if heavier, it is better for him in consequence. And this betterness is what is intended in the verse. If you say: it has been narrated from Ibn Abbas that he interpreted it as worldly betterness in hardship and its absence, we say: even if its authenticity is granted, the interpretation of the narrator is not a proof, especially when evidence stands contrary to it, so ponder. Or the intended meaning is betterness in wording, in miraculousness, eloquence, and rhetoric, and it has already passed before.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi response to opponents' arguments that the Quranic verses promising ease and betterment invalidate abrogation that leads to heavier rulings. The text opens by stating the opponent's claim: it is not ease to move from light to heavy. The Hanafi reply: the two verses mentioned (2:185 and 2:106) are not about worldly ease but about the hereafter—ease of account and reward. Even if taken worldly, the ease is not absolute generality; the context shows relative ease. The verse 2:185 is specifically about fasting in travel/sickness, with the lam used for covenant (اللام للعهد), not generality. This is supported by Ibn Abbas' interpretation. Therefore, the general argument fails. Even if generality is assumed, it is specified by the heavy burdens of obligations by consensus. The second argument uses verse 2:106 (abrogation brings better). The Hanafi answer: 'better' here means better in consequence (خير عاقبة), not easier in this world, because abrogation occurs when the original act becomes evil, so the new ruling, even if heavier, is better for the person's afterlife. The interpretation of Ibn Abbas as worldly betterness is not authoritative when contradicted by evidence. Alternatively, 'better' refers to linguistic excellence.

Key Terms
اللام للعهد (al-lam li al-'ahd): The definite article used to refer to a previously known specific referent, not for generality.
عام ('amm): A term that covers all individuals of its category without restriction.
مخصوص (makhsūs): A general term that has been specified to exclude some individuals.
خير عاقبة (khayr 'āqibah): Better in consequence, especially in the afterlife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, what is the function of the lam in the verse 'يريد الله بكم اليسر' (2:185)?
A) It indicates generality (الاستغراق).
B) It is for covenant (العهد), specifying the verse.
C) It is for emphasis.
D) It is extra (زائدة).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends abrogation of easier rulings by interpreting the ease verses as context-specific, not general.

Hanafis and Mafhum al-Mukhalafah: Why Raising It Is Not Naskh
Clarifying Hanafi position on abrogation of implied opposite meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis do not consider abrogation (naskh) of mafhum al-mukhalafah as valid naskh, and apply this to avoid misattributions.

Core Idea
Hanafis reject mafhum al-mukhalafah as proof, so raising it cannot be naskh.

This passage addresses a common misconception: that Hanafis accept mafhum al-mukhalafah and thus its abrogation would be naskh. The author clarifies that Hanafis do not recognize mafhum al-mukhalafah as a source of rulings, so raising it via another text is not naskh. The discussion involves a critique of Ibn al-Hajib's attribution and a justification using Mirzâ Jân's argument about the benefit of description.

Guided Path
1
Identify mafhum al-mukhalafah
Understand the concept: an implied opposing ruling derived from a descriptive qualifier. For example, 'in pasturing livestock zakat is due' implies that non-pasturing livestock has no zakat.
This is the opposite meaning (mukhalafah) of the explicit text.
2
State the Hanafi position on mafhum
Recall that Hanafis generally do not accept mafhum al-mukhalafah as a binding proof. Descriptive conditions do not necessarily restrict the ruling to that description.
This is a fundamental usul principle for Hanafis.
3
Explain why raising mafhum is not naskh for Hanafis
Since mafhum al-mukhalafah is not a valid ruling in the Hanafi school, abrogating it by another text is meaningless. Naskh only applies to established rulings.
Therefore, attributing such abrogation to Hanafis is incorrect.
4
Analyze the critique of Ibn al-Hajib
The passage states that Ibn al-Hajib's attribution of this naskh view to Hanafis is a mistake (sahw). Understand the author's reasoning.
The exception (illa) mentioned is only hypothetical: if Hanafis accepted mafhum, then raising it would be naskh, but they do not.
5
Evaluate Mirzâ Jân's argument and the response
Mirzâ Jân argues that if mafhum were abrogated, the description would be useless. The response: benefit at the time of speaking is sufficient; later abrogation does not make the earlier speech vain.
This defends the Hanafi position against the charge of superfluity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما رفع مفهوم المخالفة كفي المعلوفة زكاة بعد القول (في السائمة) زكاة، فالأول يرفع مفهوم الثاني (فنسبته) أي نسبة كونه نسخاً إلى الحنفية سهو من ابن الحاجب) لأنهم لا يقولون بمفهوم المخالفة حتى يكون رفعه نسخاً (إلا) تقريراً بأن يقال : لو كان المفهوم عندهم ثابتاً كما إذا دلت القرينة كان رفعه نسخاً. وأنت تعلم أن ذكره ههنا غير مناسب، قال میرزاجان لو صح نسخ مفهوم قولنا في الغنم السائمة زكاة بمنطوق في المعلوفة زكاة لم يبق لذكر الصفة فائدة، بل يكون لغواً، والقائلون بالمفهوم إنما وقعوا في القول به لئلا يكون ذكر الصفة لغواً، وجوابه أنه لا يلزم بقاء الفائدة دائماً، بل القدر الضروري لزوم الفائدة حين التكلم لئلا يلغو التكلم وهم إنما وقعوا في القول به لئلا يكون التكلم بها من غير فائدة، وهذا لا يوجب بقاء تلك الفائدة، وهل هذا إلا كما قيد بالصفة لخوف سامع آخر، وإذا زال خوفه لم تبق تلك الفائدة فافهم
As for raising the opposite meaning (mafhum al-mukhalafah), like after saying 'in pasturing livestock there is zakat', saying 'in fed livestock there is zakat' – the first raises the opposite meaning of the second. So attributing that it is naskh to the Hanafis is an oversight by Ibn al-Hajib, because they do not affirm the opposite meaning such that raising it would be naskh, except as a conditional statement: if the implied meaning were established for them, as when a qarina (contextual evidence) indicates, then raising it would be naskh. You know that mentioning it here is inappropriate. Mirzâ Jân said: If abrogation of the opposite meaning of our statement 'in pasturing sheep there is zakat' by the explicit statement 'in fed livestock there is zakat' were valid, then there would be no benefit in mentioning the description; indeed it would be superfluous. Those who affirm the opposite meaning only fell into saying it so that mentioning the description would not be superfluous. The answer is that persistence of benefit is not always necessary; rather the essential amount is that there is benefit at the time of speaking so that speech is not vain. They only fell into saying it so that speaking with it would not be without benefit, and this does not require persistence of that benefit. Is this not like a description added due to fear of another listener, and when that fear is gone, that benefit remains no longer? So understand.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage clarifies that Hanafis do not consider raising mafhum al-mukhalafah (inferred opposite meaning) as naskh because they do not accept mafhum al-mukhalafah as a valid source of rulings. Ibn al-Hajib erroneously attributed to Hanafis the view that such raising is naskh. The author explains that even if Hanafis hypothetically accepted mafhum, its raising could be naskh, but in practice they do not. Mirzâ Jân adds that if mafhum were abrogated by an explicit statement, the original description would be useless, contradicting the purpose of the text which is to avoid vain speech. The answer given is that benefit at the time of speech suffices; later abrogation does not make the earlier speech vain.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhūm al-mukhālafa): An implied ruling that is opposite to an explicit one, e.g., if the explicit says 'in pasturing livestock zakat is due', the opposite meaning might be that non-pasturing livestock has no zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is attributing naskh regarding mafhum al-mukhalafah to Hanafis considered an oversight by Ibn al-Hajib?
A) Because Hanafis use mafhum al-mukhalafah as a strong proof.
B) Because Hanafis do not recognize mafhum al-mukhalafah as a valid ruling.
C) Because Hanafis consider all mafhum as abrogated from the start.
D) Because Hanafis believe mafhum cannot be raised.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis do not accept mafhum al-mukhalafah, so abrogation of such an implied meaning is not recognized in their usul.
