Ziyada as Naskh or Takhsis? The Hanafi Position
Arguing that an increase in obligation is naskh, not takhsis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to argue why the Hanafi school classifies an increase in an obligation as naskh (abrogation) rather than takhsis (specification), and apply the principle that mutlaq has no generality.

Core Idea
An increase in obligation is naskh, not takhsis, because mutlaq has no generality.

A key usul dispute revolves around whether adding a new requirement to an existing obligation (e.g., adding a limb to wash in wudu) is an act of specification (takhsis) or abrogation (naskh). The Hanafi school argues that since the original command is mutlaq (absolute) and mutlaq lacks generality, it cannot be specified; therefore, the later text must be abrogating the earlier ruling. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this position and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
State the dispute: is an increase in obligation naskh or takhsis? Understand the two positions.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
Why does the Hanafi school argue that mutlaq cannot be specified? Because mutlaq indicates only the essence, not specific individuals; takhsis requires a general statement.
3
Analyze the opposing view
Some scholars claim that increase is takhsis because it is lighter (ahwan) than naskh. They argue it merely restricts the original, not abolishes it.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the later text is temporally separate and cannot serve as a specifying factor for a mutlaq text. The principle 'daf' (repulsion) is easier than 'raf'' (removal) but here it is actual removal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If it is naskh, the original ruling is completely replaced; if takhsis, the original remains for cases not covered. This affects how we view the legal continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قد عرفت أن الزيادة مغيرة للحكم المطلق فما في) شرح (المختصر أن زيادة غسل عضو في الوضوء أو ركن في الصلاة ليس بنسخ ساقط لأن تحقق الامتثال بالأول المطلق عن غسل هذا العضو المفروض الآن أو الركن المفروض الآن لم يبق كما عرفت (بل) الامتثال حينئذ (بالكل) فقط لا غير (فتدبر) منكرو كون الزيادة نسخاً (قالوا الزيادة (تخصيص) للمزيد عليه من الأصل (لأنه أهون) من النسخ لكونه ،إبطالاً، وهذا بيان قلنا : المطلق لا يدل إلا على الماهية من حيث هي * أي على أمر صالح لأن يوجد في كل فرد سواء كان ماهية مطلقة، كالغسل المفهوم في بالوضوء أو الفرد المبهم كرقبة فلا ينافي ما مر في فصل المطلق والمقيد والتخصيص فرع الدلالة على المشخصات لفظاً كما مر) يعني أن التخصيص إنما يكون إذا كان هناك دلالة على المشخصات المعينه والمطلق إنما يدل على القدر المشترك، ولا دلالة للعام على الخاص بإحدى الدلالات وليس ههنا قرينة صارفة عن القدر المشترك إلى المشخصات، إذ غير النص الدال على الزيادة مفروض الانتفاء، وهذا النص متراخ عنه معدوم في زمان التكلم فلا دلالة له على المشخصات، ولم يرد به أن التخصيص، إنما يكون في العام وهو فرع الدلالة على العموم، ولا عموم في المطلق لدلالته على الماهية حتى يرد عليه أنه لم يرد المستدل بالتخصيص قصر العام بل القصر المطلق على طريق الدفع والحاصل أن الدفع أهون من الرفع فتدبر
And since you have known that the increase changes the absolute ruling, what is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that adding a limb in wudu or a pillar in prayer is not abrogation is invalid, because the realization of compliance with the first absolute ruling that did not include washing this limb now prescribed or the pillar now prescribed has not remained, as you have known. Rather, compliance at that time is only with the whole, not otherwise, so reflect. The deniers that the increase is abrogation said: The increase is specification (takhsis) of the original increased-upon, because it is lighter than abrogation since it is nullification. This is an explanation. We said: The absolute does not indicate except the essence as such, i.e., upon something suitable to exist in each individual, whether it be an absolute essence like the understood washing in wudu or the vague individual like a slave. So it does not contradict what passed in the chapter on absolute and restricted. And specification is a branch of indication of the specified individuals by wording, as passed. That is, specification only occurs if there is an indication of the specific individuals, and the absolute only indicates the common denominator, and the general does not indicate the specific by any of the indications. And here there is no context diverting from the common denominator to the specific individuals, since the text indicating the increase is presumed absent, and this text is remote from it, non-existent at the time of speech, so it has no indication of the specific individuals. And it is not intended that specification is only in the general, and it is a branch of indication of generality, and there is no generality in the absolute because it indicates the essence, such that it would be objected that the proponent of specification did not intend restriction of the general, but rather absolute restriction by way of repulsion. And the gist is that repulsion is easier than removal, so reflect.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul_dispute) on whether adding a new requirement to an existing obligation (e.g., adding a limb to wash in wudu or a pillar to prayer) constitutes abrogation (naskh) or specification (takhsis). The author argues that it is not takhsis but naskh. The argument: An absolute (mutlaq) command only indicates the essence, not specific individuals. Takhsis can only apply to a general (amm) statement which has generality, but a mutlaq has no generality. Therefore, the later text that adds a requirement cannot be specifying the previous text; it must be abrogating it and establishing a new ruling. The author refutes the claim that the increase is 'lighter' and thus preferred as takhsis. He shows that the later text is temporally separate and cannot be a specifying factor for a text that did not imply those specifics. The author concludes that 'دفع' (repulsion) is easier than 'رفع' (removal), but here it is actually removal (naskh). This is a key principle in Hanafi usul distinguishing between naskh and takhsis.

Key Terms
مُطْلَق (mutlaq): A term that indicates an essence without any restriction or qualification.
تَخْصِيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term to exclude some of its individuals.
نَسْخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later divine text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the claim that an increase (ziyada) in a ritual act is takhsis (specification)?
A) Because the original command was abrogated entirely.
B) Because takhsis requires a general (amm) statement, but the mutlaq has no generality.
C) Because the increase is considered a completely new obligation.
D) Because the increase is only a recommendation, not a requirement.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that an increase in obligation is naskh, not takhsis, because the original mutlaq command has no generality to be specified.

Contract Phrases: Informative or Performative? The Hanafi Perspective
Hanafi defense of contract formulas as informative against Shafi'i performative view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that contract formulas are informative (ikhbār) and apply the concept of the mental contract (al-‘aqd al-qalbī) to refute the four main Shafi'i objections.

Core Idea
Contract formulas report about a mental contract that Shariah considers real — they are informative, not performative.

A fundamental question in uṣūl al-fiqh is whether the words used in contracts (e.g., 'I sold', 'I divorced') directly create the legal effect (performative/inshā') or merely report about an underlying internal commitment (informative/ikhbār). The Hanafi school, following the method of the verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn), holds the latter view. This lesson examines the Shafi'i objections and the Hanafi responses, emphasizing the unique concept of al-‘aqd al-qalbī (the mental contract), which the Shariah treats as the real cause of legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What exactly is debated? Is the utterance 'I sold' a performative that creates the sale, or an informative report about a pre-existing mental reality?
This distinction is foundational in Hanafi uṣūl and affects many contract rulings.
2
State the Hanafi position and its key concept
The Hanafi view is that these utterances are reports about a mental contract (al-‘aqd al-qalbī) that the Shariah considers existent and as the true cause (sabab) of the legal effect.
The mental contract is not necessarily conscious; it is a legal construct.
3
Examine the first two Shafi'i objections and Hanafi responses
(1) No external referent: Hanafi replies the mental contract is the referent. (2) No truth value: Hanafi shows truth/falsity is possible based on the existence or absence of the mental contract.
The Shariah's consideration makes the report true when the speaker is honest.
4
Examine the third and fourth objections and responses
(3) Past tense cannot accept suspension: Hanafi demonstrates that suspension (taʿlīq) modifies the temporal reference, valid in both views. (4) No difference between informing and performing: Hanafi distinguishes by the presence or absence of a new cause (iqtidā’).
The key is the repetition of the causal nexus.
5
Apply the dispute to a concrete case
The case of a man saying 'I divorced you' to his wife in ʿiddah. In the Hanafi view, intention is asked: if performative intent, a new divorce occurs; if informative, no. This is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf).
This illustrates why the usul dispute matters in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثاني/ السُّنَّة العقد عبارات شراح الأصول للإمام فخر الإسلام توهمه لكنه لا يخفى على من له قلب سليم ما فيه من الكلفة، فإن هذه الصيغ كانت مستعملة في الجاهلية، ولم يكن المستعملون يعرفون الشرع قالوا : (أولاً) لو كانت هذه الألفاظ إخبارات لكان لها خارج تكون حكايات ، فافهم . ، أن ، عنه ولا خارج لها، بل البيع مثلاً يقع ببعت وكذا أخواته، فليس هناك بيع سابق عليها حتى يكون خارجاً محكياً عنه (و) واللامطابقة هذا محصول ما في الحاشية»، ولعل مقصوده هذه الإخبارات صادقة بالنظر إلى الأمر الخارجي، وهو أن المتكلم أعرف بحاله، ومعلوم أنه لا يقصد عند استعمال هذه الصيغ الكذب، وأما بالنظر إلى حقيقتها شرح الشرح» بأنه إخبار عن وقوع تعليق الطلاق مثلاً في الذهن فلا ينافي كونه ماضياً (وهو ليس بشيء لأن الماضي إنما يدل على وقوع مصدره) في الزمان الماضي والتعليق يقتضي وقوع مصدره عند وجود الشرط لا غير وأما عنه أصلاً أولاً، ومرة إخبار عن التطليق المحكي بالحكاية أولاً وعلى الأول يقع طلاق آخر بوجود الموجب مرة ثانية، وعلى الثاني لا يقع لعدم تكرار الموجب، وقد يجاب بأن الفرق بين ما إذا قصد إيقاع الطلاق وبين فلا يحتاج إلى اعتبار وقوع آخر وهذا بناء على ما مر نقله عن البعض في تحقيق الإخبارية مع ما عليه فتذكر. قال شارح الشارح : أن القطع بالفرق المذكور إنما هو في الحكاية عن الخارج، وأما في الحكاية عما في الذهن فدقيق تحقيقه أن الإنشاء يدل على حدوث البيع بهذا
The second principle: the Sunnah. The contract: The expressions of the commentators of usul led Imam Fakhr al-Islam to suppose [something], but it is not hidden from one with a sound heart what strain is in it. For these formulas were used in the pre-Islamic era, and the users did not know the Shariah, let alone this consideration; rather, the general Muslims use these formulas and do not know this precision, nor do they intend lying when using them—i.e., reporting something not in reality. Then considering non-existent as existent by the Shariah is something that the mind abhors. So the truth is what the author stated, following the verifiers: that these are reports about the internal [mental] [contract] which the Shariah considered a cause. So understand that the formula is placed for information, so it remains upon that, because being performative is only established by transmission, and transmission is not established. It may be said: The performative meaning is the first to come to mind, and that is evidence of transmission. The answer: The necessary point is that contracts [occur] when these words are uttered; as for the performative meaning being the first to come to mind, there is no proof for it; rather, the linguistic meaning is valid, so one should not depart from it, because the original is the original. The Shafi'is said: First: If these words were informative, they would have an external reality that they report, but they have no external reality. Rather, for example, sale occurs by 'I sold' and its likes, and there is no prior sale to be the reported external. Second: If they were informative, they would be subject to truth and falsehood, but they are not subject to truth and falsehood, for conscience judges as wrong anyone who allows that. The answer: We do not accept that they have no external reality; they have an external reality in speech, which is the mental contract that necessitates the occurrence of the sale, and by it the sale actually occurs. They match it, so they are true without doubt, and they can fail to match as previously explained. He only mentioned matching because it is known that what can match can also fail to match. Not as in Sharh al-Sharh that this report is definitely true and cannot be false because its referent exists absolutely, as if one reports that there is an image in his mind—this is not sound, for reporting about the mind and about external reality are the same in possibility of matching and non-matching. This is the gist of what is in the Hashiyah. Perhaps his intent is that these reports are true with regard to the external matter, i.e., the speaker knows his own state best, and it is known that he does not intend lying when using these formulas; but with regard to their reality, they are possible both ways. So reflect. It may be answered that being informative does not require the actual existence of the referent; what is necessary is the intention to report about an external matter, and its absence is denied. But it is not false because the Shariah considered it as already existent before using these formulas, so they are true for that reason; otherwise they would be false, so their possibility of both is established. This answer is based on what we previously transmitted regarding the analysis of being informative along with its implications. It is possible to interpret the words of Sharh al-Sharh accordingly: that their truth is certain due to the Lawgiver considering the non-existent referent as existent and considering the formulas true, and the possibility of falsehood with regard to the speech itself is not denied. So reflect. Third: If it were a report, it would be past tense, because of its form. If it were past, it would not accept suspension (ta'liq) on what is future and prevented from existence, but that is false because it does accept suspension by consensus. This is refuted by the case of a performative, because if it were a performative, it would be a performative of the contract occurring now, so suspension on a future and prevented matter would not be valid. If they say: The condition changes it from being a performative now to a performative at the occurrence of the condition. We say: Likewise in the case of it being informative, the condition changes it from a past report to a report of its occurrence in the future at the occurrence of the condition. If they say it is for the performative of the conditional ruling? We say: On the assumption of being informative, it is for reporting about bindingness and suspension on what is in reality. In short, whatever your answer is, it is our answer. I say: The qualification changes it as in all reports and performatives. Do you not see that 'the day exists' indicates present occurrence; when suspended by a condition that only exists after it, it then indicates occurrence and changes from what it indicated alone. Similarly: 'You are divorced' in the performative view as is the opponent's madhhab is a divorce now and a performative of it; after suspension it is not so but is a performative of a divorce that occurs at the occurrence of the condition. So likewise in the case of being informative: it is a report about a divorce that will occur in the future when the condition exists. So we do not accept that it was past and suspension is invalid; rather, it is valid and changes from past to future, shedding the past ruling and having a ruling of bindingness between it and the condition. Then, since the meaning that necessitates is a requirement of the report, its suspension entails the suspension of the report. Indeed, if the meaning existed now, the report about the conditional ruling would be false. Rather, it only requires the existence of the necessitating meaning when the condition exists, not otherwise. That is why we said: suspension prevents causality, as previously. It is clear that the report requires the existence of bindingness between the paths and entering the house, for example; and bindingness only exists by the Shariah's consideration of the causality of the mental conditional contract for it. This much is necessary and certain. As for whether it is a cause for the occurrence of divorce when the condition exists, the dispute remains. It is mentioned along with its pros and cons, so we will not repeat it. In Sharh al-Sharh it is answered: It is a report about the occurrence of the suspension of divorce in the mind, so it does not contradict being past. This is nothing, because the past tense merely indicates the occurrence of its verbal noun in the past time; suspension requires the occurrence of its verbal noun when the condition exists only; as for the existence of its suspension in the past, it is far from what we are discussing because it is not the meaning of the formula 'I divorced', which is very clear. Fourth: If the mentioned formulas were informative, there would be no difference between a previously occurred divorce and a performative one because it is a report in any case. This lack of difference is false. Therefore, if one says to a revocably divorced woman in her waiting period 'I divorced you,' he is asked about his intention: if he intends performative, another divorce occurs; if he intends informing, it does not occur. I say: The entailment is denied; rather, the difference is that sometimes it is a report about what has occurred by a necessitation and thereby divorce occurs; other times it is not, but is a report about a real divorce not by necessitation. Otherwise, it would appear in expression: sometimes it is a report about a divorce that occurred by a self-performative that was not reported at all; other times it is a report about the divorce that was reported earlier. In the first case, another divorce occurs due to the repetition of the cause; in the second, it does not occur due to the non-repetition. It may be answered that the difference between intending to effect a divorce and intending to report about a previous divorce is that in the former he intends to report about a non-existent divorce that he reports will occur, so the Shariah considers it as occurring for the truth of this speech, so another divorce occurs; in the latter, he intends about a real, existent divorce, so he is truthful in reporting and does not need the consideration of another occurrence. This is based on what was previously transmitted from some regarding the analysis of being informative with its implications. So remember. The commentator of al-Sharh said: Certainty about the mentioned distinction is only in reporting about external reality; as for reporting about what is in the mind, its precise analysis is that the performative indicates the occurrence of the sale by this
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute on whether contract formulas (e.g., 'I sold', 'I divorced') are informative (إخبار) or performative (إنشاء). The Hanafi position, as articulated by the author following the verifiers (muhaqqiqun), is that these words are informative: they report about a mental contract (العقد القلبي) that the Shariah considers as a cause. The Shafi'i school argues they are performative, creating the legal effect directly. The passage responds to four Shafi'i arguments: (1) lack of external referent, (2) impossibility of truth/falsehood, (3) past tense not allowing suspension, and (4) no difference between informing and performing. The Hanafi response consistently invokes the concept of ذهني (mental) contract as the external referent, and that Shariah's consideration gives it reality. The author shows how suspension (تعليق) can modify both informative and performative sentences. A key point: the Hanafi view does not require the speaker to be aware of the mental contract; it is a legal construct. The passage ends with a quote from Sharh al-Sharh distinguishing reporting about external vs. mental reality.

Key Terms
إخبار (ikhbār): An utterance that reports about something else (external or mental).
إنشاء (inshā’): An utterance that creates or effects a legal consequence directly, not reporting about a pre-existing reality.
العقد القلبي (al-‘aqd al-qalbī): The mental contract or inner commitment that the Shariah considers as the real cause of the legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the function of the phrase 'I sold' (بعت) in a sale contract?
A) It creates the sale directly as a performative utterance.
B) It is an informative report about a pre-existing mental contract.
C) It is both informative and performative simultaneously.
D) It has no legal effect unless witnessed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school views contract formulas as informative reports about an internal mental contract, which explains their ability to be true/false and to accept suspension.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Authority of Mashhur Hadith to Restrict Quranic Texts
Usul rule on the authority of mashhur hadith to restrict Quranic texts, with a critique of an opposing view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a mashhur hadith can restrict a mutlaq or specify an 'amm Quranic verse, but cannot completely abrogate the mutlaq or all individuals of the 'amm.

Core Idea
Mashhur hadith can restrict but never fully abrogate a definitive Quranic text.

This passage from the commentary on Musallam al-Thubut clarifies the precise role of mashhur hadith in relation to the Quran. While the Quran is definitively established (qat'i al-thubut), its indication of absoluteness (mutlaq) or generality ('amm) is only definitive in a general sense. Mashhur hadith shares that general definitiveness, enabling it to restrict or specify, but not to entirely overturn a clear Quranic ruling. The author also critiques an opposing view that would grant mashhur greater authority.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish levels of certainty
Identify the two dimensions of a text: thubut (certainty of transmission) and dalala (certainty of meaning). Quranic mutlaq/'amm has qat'i thubut but its indication of absoluteness/generality is only qat'i in a general sense (qat'i bi al-ma'na al-amm). Mashhur hadith has zanni thubut but its indication can be qat'i in the general sense.
Thubut: mutawatir = qat'i; mashhur = zanni (though strong). Dalala: mutlaq/ 'amm indication is qat'i until restricted, but the absoluteness itself is only qat'i in a general sense.
2
Identify the intermediate status of mashhur
Mashhur is a barzakh (isthmus) between mutawatir and ahad. It partakes of both: its thubut is stronger than ahad but weaker than mutawatir. Therefore, it can perform taqyid/takhsis but not complete naskh of a qat'i text.
The author says: 'al-mashhur barzakh bayn al-mutawatir wa al-ahad'.
3
Apply the rule: restriction allowed, complete abrogation forbidden
Apply to an example: the flogging verse (al-Nur: 2) is mutlaq applying to all adulterers. The mashhur hadith of stoning Ma'iz restricts it to unmarried offenders. However, the mashhur hadith cannot abrogate the entire verse or all its individuals, because that would replace a qat'iyyat with a zanniyyat.
The author notes that the stoning example may not be pure mashhur because stoning is also mutawatir in meaning, but the principle stands.
4
Evaluate the opposing argument and its refutation
Some argue that because many narrators reach tawatur from the Companion, and because of the hadith praising the early generations, mashhur should be equivalent to the Quran's absoluteness. Refutation: tawatur from the Companion does not guarantee tawatur from the Prophet; the praise of generations indicates abundance of upright people, not infallibility of each narrator; possibility of error remains.
The author says: 'Wa fihi nazar zahir...' and concludes the truth is what he taught previously.

Source Text

الأصل الثاني/ السنة
الأعم، ثم مطلق الكتاب وإن كان ثبوته مقطوعاً بالمعنى الأخص لكونه متواتراً إلا أن دلالته على الإطلاق مقطوعة بالمعنى الأعم، فيكون الإطلاق حكم الله تعالى وحكم الخبر المشهور حكمه تعالى متساويان في المقطوعية العامة فيجوز إبطاله به فيجوز التقييد في الابتداء أو نسخ الإطلاق، وكذا يجوز تخصيص عام الكتاب ونسخ بعض أفراده به لهذا، لكن لا يجوز نسخ المطلق رأساً ولا نسخ جميع أفراد العام رأساً بالخبر المشهور، إذ يلزم منه إبطال المقطوع بالمعنى الأخص بالمقطوع بالمعنى الأعم هذا ما عند هذا العبد، ولعل الله يحدث بعد ذلك أمراً.
والمشهور في إبانة هذا المطلب أن تقييد المطلق بيان من وجه وإبطال من وجه، وكذا الخبر المشهور برزخ بين المتواتر والآحاد فتوفر عليه شبههما فجوز التقييد به دون الإبطال بالكلية، ولا يخفى عليك أنه لو كان بياناً فبيان تغيير فهو إبطال له من كل وجه، فلا صحة لهذا إلا بالإرجاع إلى ما قلنا وقال بعضهم في إبانة هذا المطلب: إن رواية هذا الجم الغفير الذين بلغوا مبلغ التواتر وقد انضم إليه شهادة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم بالصدق بقوله: «خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم ثم يفشو الكذب» توجب للثبوت قوية بينة، فيبلغ مبلغ قوة إطلاق الكتاب فيجوز إبطاله بالتقييد وفيه نظر ظاهر، فإن بلوغ الرواة عن الصحابي حد التواتر إنما يوجب ثبوته عنه قطعاً، ولا يلزم منه قوة الثبوت عنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وشهادة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم للقرون الثلاثة إنما هي بكثرة العدول فيهم، ثم فشوا الكذب بعدهم، وهو لا يوجب قطعية عدالة كل راو وإما احتمال النسيان والسهو فقائم كما كان، فتأمل والحق لا يجاوز عما أقرأناك سابقاً (كآية الجلد) قوله تعالى: ﴿الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ﴾ [النور: ٢] قيدت عدم الإحصان برجم ماعز وهو خبر مشهور تلقته الأمة بالقبول في «فتح القدير» أخرج أحمد وإسحاق بن راهويه وابن أبي شيبة عن خليفة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه: أتى ماعز بن مالك النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم وأنا عنده فاعترف مرة، فرده ثم جاء فاعترف عنده الثانية، فرده، ثم جاء فاعترف عنده الثالثة فرده، فقلت له: إن اعترفت الرابعة رجمك، قال: فاعترف الرابعة فقالوا: لا نعلم إلا خيراً، فأمر به فرجم، ثم في هذا التمثيل نظر، فإن ثبوت الرجم متواتر المعنى كما صرح به في «فتح القدير»، وقد ثبت الرجم عن الحيوانات كما نقل عن القردة معجزة للنبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، فليس من الباب في شيء، وكثير والمشهور في التمثيل تقييد قوله تعالى: ﴿حَتَّى تَنكِحَ [؟]﴾ [البقرة: ۲۳٠] بحديث العسيلة، وتقييد آية الوضوء بخبر المسح على الخف، والأول صحيح، والثاني منظور فيه لما سيجيء أن خبر المسح متواتر المعنى فافهم
Second principle: Sunnah. The general [of the Quran] and then the absolute of the Book, even though its proof is definitive in the specific sense because it is mutawatir, yet its indication of absoluteness is definitive in the general sense. So the absolute ruling of Allah and the ruling of the mashhur report are equal in general definitiveness, thus it is permissible to invalidate it [the absolute] by it, so restriction is permissible initially or abrogation of the absolute. Likewise, it is permissible to specify the general of the Book and abrogate some of its individuals by it for this reason. But it is not permissible to abrogate the absolute entirely nor to abrogate all individuals of the general entirely by a mashhur report, because that would entail invalidating what is definitive in the specific sense by what is definitive in the general sense. This is my view, and perhaps Allah will bring about something after that. The well-known explanation of this point is that restricting the absolute is clarification in one aspect and invalidation in another. Likewise, the mashhur report is an isthmus between mutawatir and ahad, so it partakes of both, thus restriction is allowed through it but not total invalidation. It is not hidden from you that if it were clarification, then it would be a clarifying change, so it is invalidation from every aspect. This is not valid unless referred back to what we said. Some have said in explaining this point: The narration of this great multitude who have reached the level of tawatur and to which is added the testimony of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) to their truthfulness by his saying, 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them, then falsehood will spread,' necessitates a strong evidentiary force for the report, so it reaches the strength of the absoluteness of the Book; thus it is permissible to invalidate it by restriction. But there is an apparent problem: The narrators' reaching the level of tawatur from the Companion only necessitates definitive proof from him, and it does not necessitate strong proof from the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and Companions). And the testimony of the Messenger of Allah for the three generations is only about the abundance of upright people among them, then falsehood spread after them, and it does not necessitate the definitive uprightness of every narrator; the possibility of forgetfulness and error remains as before. So reflect, and the truth does not go beyond what we taught you previously. Like the verse of flogging: Allah says, 'The adulteress and adulterer, flog each of them one hundred lashes.' This was restricted by the condition of not being muhsan, by the stoning of Ma'iz, which is a mashhur report accepted by the Ummah. Ahmad, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from the Caliph of the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq: 'Ma'iz ibn Malik came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) while I was with him and confessed once, and he turned him away. Then he came and confessed a second time, and he turned him away. Then he came and confessed a third time, and he turned him away. I said to him: If you confess a fourth time, he will stone you. He said: So he confessed a fourth time, and they said: We know nothing but good. So he ordered him to be stoned.' Then there is a problem with this example: The stoning ruling is mutawatir in meaning as stated in Fath al-Qadir, and stoning has been established from animals as reported from monkeys as a miracle of the Prophet (peace be upon him), so it is not from this topic at all. Many famous examples include restricting His saying, 'until she marries another husband' by the hadith of 'asilah, and restricting the verse of wudu by the report of wiping over khuffs. The first is correct, and the second is subject to discussion because the report of wiping over khuffs is mutawatir in meaning, as will come. So understand.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of a key usul rule regarding the hierarchy of textual evidence. The author (likely the commentator) explains that while the Quran is definitively established (qat'i al-thubut) due to tawatur, its indication (dalala) regarding absoluteness is only definitive in a general sense. The mashhur hadith shares this general definitiveness, so it can be used to restrict (taqyid) a mutlaq verse or specify (takhsis) a general ('amm) verse. However, it cannot completely abrogate (naskh) the mutlaq or all individuals of the 'amm, as that would require a higher level of certainty. The author then critiques an alternative view that argues for stronger authority of mashhur based on the hadith about the best generations, showing its flaw: the testimony to the truthfulness of the generations does not guarantee the infallibility of every narrator. The example of the flogging verse and the stoning of Ma'iz is given to illustrate the restriction of the absolute (the flogging verse is absolute in its application to all adulterers, but the mashhur hadith of stoning restricts it to married offenders), but the author notes this example is weak because the stoning ruling is itself mutawatir in meaning. Other examples like the 'asilah hadith and the wiping over khuffs are mentioned. The passage reinforces the rule that mashhur occupies an intermediate position between mutawatir and ahad.

Key Terms
المشهور (al-mashhur): The well-known report: a hadith narrated in the second generation by three or more narrators, surpassing ahad but not reaching tawatur.
المطلق (al-mutlaq): An absolute or unqualified expression in the Quran, indicating the genus without restriction.
العام (al-'amm): A general term that includes all individuals within its scope, like 'every' or 'all'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The mashhur hadith has no effect on the mutlaq verse.
D) The mashhur hadith can only specify an 'amm verse, not a mutlaq.

Key Takeaway
A mashhur hadith can restrict the absolute or specify the general of the Quran, but it cannot completely abrogate the mutlaq or all individuals of the 'amm.

The Proof from Surah al-Hujurat 49:6 Using Mafhum al-Mukhalafah
Analyzing a Quranic verse to derive a usul principle via inferred meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the type of mafhum (mafhum al-sifah) used in the argument from Surah al-Hujurat 49:6 and evaluate why the Hanafi school does not accept this as qat'i evidence.

Core Idea
The verse about the fasiq implies by its attribute that a just person's report is accepted, but this inferred meaning is weak and disputed in Hanafi usul.

This passage examines a key proof for khabar al-wahid from Surah al-Hujurat 49:6. The verse commands investigation when a fasiq brings news. By mafhum al-mukhalafah, it is inferred that when a just person brings news, acceptance is required. However, the passage highlights the Hanafi position that such inferred meanings are weak and not sufficient for certain knowledge. It also clarifies that the correct inference is from the attribute (mafhum al-sifah), not the condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative phrase
Focus on the phrase 'fasiq' and the command 'tabayyanu'. The attribute 'fasiq' triggers the inferred meaning.
The verse: 'If a fasiq comes to you with news, then investigate.'
2
Classify the type of mafhum
Determine if the inference is from the condition (mafhum al-shart) or the attribute (mafhum al-sifah). The passage states it is correctly mafhum al-sifah.
3
Apply Hanafi usul principle
Recall that Hanafis generally reject mafhum al-mukhalafah as independent evidence; it is considered zanni and weak.
This limits the force of the argument.
4
Evaluate epistemic weight
Even if accepted, the inference is only conjectural (zanni), not qat'i, so it cannot serve as a definitive proof in usul al-fiqh.
5
Consider the counter-response
The author suggests attaching consensus (ijma) to strengthen the argument, as done previously with other verses.
This is a common Hanafi strategy to bolster weak proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدل بقوله تعالى ﴿إِن جَاءَكُمْ فَاسِقٌ بِنَبَاءِ فتبينوا الحجرات : ٦] فإنه يدل على أنه : إن جاءكم عادل فاقبلوا قوله (وهذا) الاستدلال (بناء على مفهوم المخالفة فلا يستطيع الحنفي المنكر إياه أن يستدل بها (و) أيضاً لو سلم (فهو ظاهر ظني ظناً ضعيفاً، فلا يصلح حجة فيما يقصد فيه القطع ولك أن تدفع بما سبق من ضم الإجماع إليه، واعترض أيضاً بأن مفهوم شرطه هو أنه إذا لم يجىء فاسق بنبأ فلا تبينوا، وهو أعم من قبول خبر العدل وعدم إخبار واحد وأجيب بأن ثبوت المفهوم لئلا تنتفي الفائدة، وفي هذا المفهوم لا فائدة أصلاً، فإنه معلوم من قبل، والحق أن الاستدلال ليس بمفهوم الشرط، بل بمفهوم الصفة، فإن الفاسق صفة ومفهومه : إن جاء غير فاسق وهو العادل فاقبلوا، فافهم
And he argued by the saying of Allah Most High: 'If a fasiq comes to you with news, then investigate' (al-Hujurat 49:6). For it indicates that if a just person comes to you, then accept his words. This inference is based on the concept of opposition (mafhum al-mukhalafah). So the Hanafi who rejects it cannot argue with it. Also, even if it is granted, it is an apparent conjecture, a weak conjecture, so it is not suitable as proof in what is intended to be definitive. But you can repel [this] by what preceded, by attaching consensus to it. It is also objected that the condition's inferred meaning is: if a fasiq does not come with news, then do not investigate; and this is more general than accepting the report of a just person and not reporting a single person. It was answered that establishing the inferred meaning is so that benefit is not lost, and in this inferred meaning there is no benefit at all, for it is known from before. The truth is that the inference is not based on the condition's inferred meaning, but on the attribute's inferred meaning, for 'fasiq' is an attribute, and its inferred meaning is: if one who is not fasiq, i.e., the just person, comes, then accept. So understand.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents the proof from Surah al-Hujurat 49:6 for khabar al-wahid. The verse commands investigation when a fasiq (sinful person) brings news. By mafhum al-mukhalafah (opposite implication), it is understood that if a just person brings news, investigation is not required; rather, acceptance is obligatory. This is a classic argument. However, the passage immediately notes that Hanafis who reject mafhum al-mukhalafah cannot use this argument. Even if accepted, the inference is merely conjectural (zanni), and a weak conjecture at that, so it does not produce the certainty required in usul. To strengthen it, one can again resort to the combined argument with consensus, as was done with the previous verse. Another objection is raised: the inferred meaning of the condition is that if no fasiq comes, do not investigate; this is broader and does not specifically mandate acceptance of the just person's report. The response is that the true inference is from the attribute (mafhum al-sifah): 'fasiq' is a descriptor, so its opposite implies that the non-fasiq (the just person) is treated opposite, i.e., his report is accepted without investigation. Thus, the argument is based on mafhum al-sifah, not mafhum al-shart. The passage ends with 'so understand', indicating careful reflection. In Hanafi usul, mafhum al-mukhalafah is not generally accepted as strong evidence, so relying solely on this verse is problematic unless supported by other proofs.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafah): The inferred opposite meaning: if a condition or attribute is mentioned, its opposite ruling is inferred when that condition/attribute is absent.
مفهوم الصفة (mafhum al-sifah): Inferred meaning from an attribute: the attribute implies a ruling for its opposite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the specific type of inferred meaning used in the argument from Surah al-Hujurat 49:6 according to the passage?
A) Mafhum al-shart (condition's inferred meaning)
B) Mafhum al-sifah (attribute's inferred meaning)
C) Mafhum al-ghayah (limit's inferred meaning)
D) Mafhum al-adad (number's inferred meaning)

Key Takeaway
The argument from Surah al-Hujurat 49:6 for khabar al-wahid is based on mafhum al-sifah, which is considered weak (zanni) by Hanafis, requiring additional evidence like consensus for certainty.

Definition of Sahabi: Hanafi Usul vs. Muhaddithin
Comparison and analysis of the definition of sahabi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi usul definition of a sahabi, contrast it with the muhaddithin definition, and apply the Hanafi criteria to evaluate the status of narrators like al-Ash'ath ibn Qays.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of sahabi requires long companionship and following; mere brief meeting does not grant automatic 'adalah.

In this lesson, we explore the critical definition of a 'companion' (sahabi) and how it differs between usul scholars (Hanafis) and hadith scholars. This distinction affects whether a narrator is automatically considered trustworthy ('adil) or needs additional verification. We will analyze the key cases of Hassan ibn Thabit, Jarir al-Bajali, and al-Ash'ath ibn Qays to see the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate in the passage the definitions given for 'sahabi' by the majority of usul scholars and by the majority of hadith scholars. Note the conditions (shurut) in each.
Usul scholars: Muslim with long companionship (ṭālat ṣuḥbatuhu) and following (muttabiʿan). Hadith scholars: whoever met him as a Muslim and died in Islam.
2
Examine the excluded cases
The passage mentions Hassan ibn Thabit and Jarir al-Bajali as not fitting the usuli definition but being companions by consensus. Understand why they are excluded under the strict definition.
Hassan did not go on a military expedition; Jarir embraced Islam only 40 days before the Prophet's death.
3
Analyze the case of al-Ash'ath ibn Qays
Understand how apostasy (riddah) affects sahabiyyah according to Hanafis. Al-Ash'ath apostatized after the Prophet's death, then returned to Islam. Why do Hanafis require tazkiyah for him?
Apostasy nullifies all deeds including companionship, so his earlier meeting is invalidated; he is not considered a sahabi automatically.
4
Understand the linguistic argument
The Hanafi position relies on the 'urf (customary) understanding of 'companion' as a constant associate. Identify the Arabic phrase that expresses this and see how it is used to exclude brief visitors.
المتبادر من الصحابي وأصحاب الحديث عرفاً ليس إلا الملازم المتبع المحب
5
Recognize the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Determine how the definition affects the acceptance of narrations. For Hanafis, those who do not meet the strict definition require tazkiyah; for muhaddithin, all who met the Prophet are 'udul by default.
The consequence: automatic 'adalah vs. need for verification.

Issue: The companion (sahabi) according to the majority of usul scholars is: a Muslim whose companionship with the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family and companions) was long, following him. The correct view is that length is not specified; and it is said: six months, and it is said: a year or a military expedition. On this basis, Hassan ibn Thabit and Jarir ibn Abdullah al-Bajali are excluded, even though they are companions by consensus; for Hassan did not participate in a military expedition with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions), and Jarir embraced Islam forty days before his death. According to the majority of hadith scholars, the companion is whoever met him as a Muslim and died in Islam. And death upon Islam is known by not manifesting disbelief; by the inner necessity of faith and the testimony that the companion's death was only upon faith (even if apostasy intervened, whether Islam after apostasy occurred during his lifetime (peace be upon him) or after his death, like al-Ash'ath ibn Qays: he embraced Islam in the year 10 Hijri, apostatized after the death of the Messenger of Allah, was captured during the caliphate of the greatest Siddiq, and was speaking in chains; then he embraced Islam, and he and Jarir attended a funeral; al-Ash'ath gave precedence to Jarir and said: 'I apostatized but you did not.' This is stated in al-Isti'ab according to the soundest of their school, contrary to what some hadith researchers say. And what emboldened him to rule as most sound is that most biographers of the Companions count the mentioned al-Ash'ath. But the truth is the latter school: for apostasy nullifies all deeds by decisive text, and companionship is among the best deeds, so apostasy nullifies it; so the companionship that occurred before returning to Islam is not companionship at all, like the companionship of a disbeliever during his disbelief. And their mentioning him in the biographies of Companions may be because his narration was accepted, and the intended purpose is to know the condition of narrators, and his narration is like that of the Companions without an intermediary; therefore they rightly mentioned him among them. But there must be tazkiyah (purification) for this man, and apparent 'adalah is not sufficient due to him not being a true companion. Ibn al-Hajib chose this. And it is not hidden that modifying all in this sense is problematic and the mentioned evidence does not establish it. Do you not see the saying of the Commander of the Faithful 'Umar regarding Fatima bint Qays: 'We do not know whether she told the truth or lied'? And what is preserved in Sahih Muslim is: 'We do not know whether she forgot.' And this amount does not negate 'adalah; so understand. (And it is said) the companion is one in whom long companionship and narration are combined, and this is far from language and custom, for they do not imply narration; and it is close in terms of modification, for the narrators among the Companions are all 'udul in our view. The immediate understanding from the word 'companion' and the custom of hadith scholars is only the constant companion, the follower, the lover. (Therefore negation of the visitor is sound by agreement, because he is not constant. If you say: the validity of negation in the more specific sense is conceded, but negation of the absolute companion is not allowed; he said: and carrying the negation to the more specific from the real meaning is contrary to the apparent from custom. The majority of hadith scholars said: firstly, companionship includes both little and much of it, like ziyarah includes both; so the companion is everyone who met even a little. (And) they said: (secondly: if.)
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a mas'ala (issue) defining the term 'sahabi' (companion). It contrasts the definition held by the majority of usul scholars (jumhur al-usuliyyin) with that of the majority of hadith scholars (jumhur al-muhaddithin). According to the usul scholars (and this is the Hanafi position), a sahabi is a Muslim who had a long companionship with the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) and followed him; the exact length is not fixed but is generally more than a brief meeting. This excludes people like Hassan ibn Thabit and Jarir al-Bajali who are still considered companions by consensus but not usuli definition. The hadith scholars define a sahabi as anyone who met the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) as a Muslim and died in Islam, even if there was apostasy in between (like al-Ash'ath ibn Qays). The passage delves into the case of al-Ash'ath ibn Qays, who apostatized after the Prophet's death, and discusses whether he regains the status of sahabi upon returning to Islam. The author argues that apostasy nullifies all deeds including companionship; thus his earlier companionship is invalidated, and he cannot be considered a true sahabi without tazkiyah (purification) for his 'adalah. The commentary then presents a third opinion: that a sahabi must have both long companionship and be a narrator. The author favors the Hanafi usul definition (long companionship) as the default understanding in language and custom, and notes that the hadith scholars' definition is too broad. The passage ends with an objection that the Hanafi restriction to 'constant companion' is against the apparent custom.

Key Terms
الصحابي (al-sahabi): This passage defines 'sahabi' according to usuliyyin (Hanafi) as one with long companionship and following; according to muhaddithin as one who met the Prophet as Muslim and died in Islam.
الردة (al-riddah): Apostasy from Islam; it nullifies all previous deeds including the status of sahabiyyah.
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): A formal declaration of a narrator's 'adalah; necessary for those who are not proven 'udul automatically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Al-Ash'ath ibn Qays, who apostatized after the Prophet's death but later returned to Islam.
D) A person who accompanied the Prophet for many years and followed him continuously.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of sahabi requires long companionship and following; brief meetings or apostasy disqualify, necessitating tazkiyah for narrator acceptance.

Reconciling Conflicting Texts: Hanafi Methods
Enumeration of reconciliation methods for conflicting nusus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four methods of reconciling conflicting texts (amm-amm, mutlaq-mutlaq, khass-khass, amm-khass) according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
When texts conflict, prefer reconciliation over discarding — apply diversification, restriction, subdivision, or specification.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, encountering seemingly contradictory texts does not automatically lead to abrogation or suspension. The jurist seeks to give effect to both texts through specific reconciliation techniques. This lesson explains the four main methods: tanwi' for general-general, taqyid for absolute-absolute, tab'id for specific-specific, and takhsis for general-specific, along with the underlying principle that acting on both proofs is superior to neglecting one.

Guided Path
1
Classify the conflict type
First, identify whether the conflict is between two general texts (amm-amm), two absolute texts (mutlaq-mutlaq), two specific texts (khass-khass), or a general and a specific (amm-khass). This determines the reconciliation method.
This classification is crucial; applying the wrong method may lead to incorrect reconciliation.
2
Apply the reconciliation method
For amm-amm: use tanwi' (diversification) by assigning each general ruling to a different subset of individuals. For mutlaq-mutlaq: use taqyid (restriction) by adding different qualifying conditions to each. For khass-khass: use tab'id (subdivision) by interpreting each for a different case or metaphorically. For amm-khass: use takhsis (specification) by limiting the general to matters outside the specific's scope.
All methods aim to give effect to both texts simultaneously.
3
Justify with the principle
The underlying justification is the principle: إعمال الدليلين أولى من إهمال أحدهما (acting on both evidences is better than discarding one). This principle overrides the need for chronological knowledge.
This principle is especially important for the amm-khass case where Shafi'is require contemporaneity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الجمع في العامين المتعارضين بالتنويع بأن يخص حكم أحدهما بالبعض والآخر بالبعض الآخر وفي المطلقين بالتقييد في كل منهما بقيد مغاير للآخر وفي الخاصتين بالتبعيض بأن يحمل أحدهما على حال والآخر على حال أو بحمل أحدهما على المجاز وإبقاء الآخر على الحقيقة وفي العام والخاص بتخصيص العام والعمل به فيما وراء الخاص والعمل بالخاص احتمال الغلط لا بأن يقطع بأن المراد بالعام ما وراء الخاص كتخصيص الشافعية وعلى مع هذا لا يرد عليهم أن التخصيص فرع المقارنة ولا علم في التعارض بالمقارنة إن قيل كما قال الشيخ الهداد الأعمال بالدليلين أولى من الإهمال بأحدهما فيقدم الجمع الذي فيه إعمال
Then in reconciling conflicting general texts (general-general), it is by al-tanwi' (diversification) i.e., specifying the ruling of one to some individuals and the other to other individuals. In conflicting absolute texts (mutlaq-mutlaq), by al-taqyid (restriction) in each with a different restriction from the other. In conflicting specific texts (khass-khass), by al-tab'id (subdivision) i.e., interpreting one for one case and the other for another case, or by interpreting one metaphorically and retaining the other as literal. In general and specific (amm and khass), by specifying the general and acting upon it in matters outside the specific, and acting upon the specific — with the possibility of error — not by asserting definitively that the intended meaning of the general is what is outside the specific, like the specification of the Shafi'is. And despite this, they are not rebutted that specification is contingent upon contemporaneity, and in conflict there is no knowledge of contemporaneity, if it is said as Sheikh al-Haddad said: acting upon both evidences is better than discarding one, so reconciliation that gives effect is preferred.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of rules for reconciling conflicting nass when both cannot be abrogated or ignored. The Hanafi method is: For two general texts (amm-amm), use tanwi' (diversification) by apportioning each ruling to different subsets of individuals. For two absolute texts (mutlaq-mutlaq), use taqyid (restriction) by adding different qualifying conditions to each. For two specific texts (khass-khass), use tab'id (subdivision) by applying each to different circumstances, or interpret one metaphorically and the other literally. For a general and a specific text (amm and khass), the general is specified by the specific, meaning the general applies to cases outside the scope of the specific, and the specific is acted upon in its own scope. This is done as a reconciliation method, not as a definitive assertion that the general's intended meaning excludes the specific, which is the Shafi'i view of takhsis (specification). The text notes a potential objection: takhsis requires that both texts be contemporaneous in revelation, but in conflict we don't know the timing. However, the principle that acting on both is better than discarding one overrides, so we prefer the reconciliation method.

Key Terms
التنويع (al-tanwī'): Diversification: applying each conflicting general text to a different subset of individuals.
التقييد (al-taqyīd): Restriction: adding a qualifying condition to each absolute (mutlaq) text to resolve conflict.
التبعيض (al-tab'īḍ): Subdivision: interpreting each specific text for different cases or circumstances.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Specification: limiting the scope of a general text by a specific text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which method is used to reconcile two conflicting absolute texts (mutlaq-mutlaq)?
A) al-tanwi' (diversification)
B) al-taqyid (restriction)
C) al-tab'id (subdivision)
D) al-takhsis (specification)

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul prioritizes reconciliation of conflicting texts through specific methods to give effect to both, based on the principle that acting on both proofs is better than discarding one.

Methods of Jam' (Reconciliation) in Conflicting Evidences
Discussing methods of jam' (reconciliation) between conflicting texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four main methods of jam' (reconciliation) for conflicting texts: tanwi', taqyid, tab'id, and takhsis.

Core Idea
Reconciliation preserves both texts; the method depends on whether the texts are general, absolute, particular, or mixed.

In this passage, the author outlines systematic ways to reconcile apparently conflicting evidences without discarding any. These methods are fundamental in Hanafi usul for harmonizing primary sources. Understanding these tools is the first step before considering preponderance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of conflicting texts
Determine whether the texts are both general (amm), both absolute (mutlaq), both particular (khass), or one general and one particular. The method of jam' depends on this classification.
For two general texts, use tanwi'; for two absolute, use taqyid; for two particular, use tab'id; for general and particular, use takhsis.
2
Apply tanwi' for two general texts
Tanwi' means diversification: apply each general text to a different subset of individuals or situations. For example, a general command to honor scholars and a general command to honor the poor can be reconciled by applying each to different contexts.
3
Apply taqyid for two absolute texts
Taqyid means restriction: add a qualifying condition to each absolute text to differentiate their scopes. For example, one text says 'free a slave' and another says 'feed the poor'; they can be reconciled by restricting one to cases of expiation and the other to voluntary charity.
4
Apply tab'id or takhsis for particular texts or mixed
For two particular texts, use tab'id (partial application): apply one to one situation and the other to another, or take one figuratively. For a general and a particular, specify the general (takhsis) so it applies beyond the particular, and the particular stands as an exception.
The particular is acted upon with possibility of error; the general is applied to all other cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرجح

يحمل أحدهما على حال والآخر على حال أو بحمل أحدهما على المجاز) وإبقاء الآخر على الحقيقة وفي العام والخاص بتخصيص العام والعمل (به) فيما وراء الخاص، والعمل بالخاص احتمال الغلط (لا) بأن يقطع بأن المراد المدينة، فأمرهم أن يأتوا إبل الصدقة ليشربوا من أبوالها وألبانها وفعلوا فصحوا فارتدوا وقتلوا رعاتها واستاقوا الإبل، فبعث في آثارهم فأتي بهم فقطع أيديهم وأرجلهم من خلاف وسمل أعينهم ثم لم يحسمهم حتى ماتوا (المرجح التحريم) فإنه مقدم على الإباحة (مع إمكان حمل العام ما لا يؤكل لحمه كما حمل الإمام محمد فحكم بإباحة بول ما يؤكل ( أو ) مع إمكان حمل العام على ما (لا) يكون (للتداوي) كما حمل الإمام أبو يوسف فحلل التداوي بأبوال الإبل بل المحرم مطلقاً في رواية وقوله أرفق بالناس، ولتقديم الراجح شواهد كثيرة لا تحصى. ولنورد ههنا أمثلة للتعارض (تمرينا) للمتعلم للتخلص عنها فمنها ما بين قراءة النصب والجر في قوله تعالى: ﴿يَتأَيُّهَا الذين امنوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ وَامْسَحُوا بِرُءُوسِكُمْ وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَينِ ﴾ [المائدة: ٦] (المقتضيين أحدهما (للمسح فإنه إذا كان مجروراً كان معطوفاً على الرؤوس داخلاً تحت المسح (و) الآخر (للغسل) كما إذا كان منصوباً، فإنه معطوف حينئذ على الأيدي داخل تحت الغسل، وجمع بحمل الجر على الجوار وكون المجرور معطوفاً على المعطوف عليه حال النصب ولم يرتض به المص وقال : (وحمل الجر على الجوار معارض بالنصب على المحل فإنه يمكن أن يكون معطوفاً على الرؤوس حملاً على المحل، فإنه مفعول محلاً فلا أولوية لجعل الجر للجوار، لكن ينبغي أن لا يصغي إليه، فإن من جعل الجر للجوار قال : إن غسل الرجل ثابت قطعاً بالتوارث، فلا بد من ارتكاب خلاف الظاهر في قراءة الجر، فحمل على الجوار وحينئذ لا توجه لما ذكر (أقول لك ترجيح الغسل على المسح بأن الرجل محل التلوث، فبالغسل أجدر كاليد دون الرأس) فإنه لا احتمال للتلوث فيه، وفيه شائبة من الخفاء، فإن الكلام في إزالة النجاسة الحكمية وأنها المسح أو الغسل ولا دخل فيه للتلوث، إلا أن يقال الظاهر وقوع الشرع بإزالة النجاسة الحكمية مطابقاً لما يحكم به الطبع من إزالة النجاسة الحقيقية، وأن محل التلوث أحرى وأليق بأن يعتبر نجساً حكماً، ولا تزول هذه النجاسة إلا بما تزول به الحقيقية في الحكم فافهم وتأمل (وأيضاً: الوضوء كالغسل في تطهير (البدن كله فإن الحدث حل تمام البدن كالجنابة والوضوء يطهره كالغسل فينبغي أن يجب غسل كل البدن في الوضوء، كما في الغسل، لكن كان فيه حرج عظيم فأقيم غسل الأطراف مقام غسل (الكل) فيكون الرجل من المغسولات، لكن كان ينبغي أن يجب غسل الرأس أيضاً فدفعه بقوله : واكتفى في الرأس بالمسح دفعاً للحرج) إذ في غسل
Preponderator (murajjih). And know also that whoever does not hold the authority of the sayings of the Companions should act upon them when two texts conflict, for it is known that one of them is abrogated by the other, and the Companion's practice agrees with one of them because it is established. So it is apparent that the Companion only acted upon what is established, not what is abrogated. So understand. (Then: reconciliation (jam') in two conflicting general texts (ammayn) is by diversification (tanwi'), such that the ruling of one is specified to some [individuals] and the other to others. And in two absolute (mutlaqayn) texts, by restriction (taqyid) in each with a condition different from the other. And in two particular texts (khasatayn), by partial application (tab'id) such that one is applied to one situation and the other to another, or by taking one as metaphorical (majaz) and keeping the other as literal (haqiqa). And in a general and a particular, by specifying the general and acting upon it beyond the particular, and acting upon the particular [is] with possibility of error. (No) not by cutting off that the intended meaning of the general is what is beyond the particular, (like the specification of the Shafi'is). And with this, it is not objected against them that specification is a branch of [knowledge of] contemporaneity (muqarana) and we have no knowledge of contemporaneity in conflict. (If it is said) as said by Shaykh al-Haddad: (Acting upon) both proofs is better than ignoring one, so reconciliation (jam') is preferred over preponderance (tarjih) which involves ignoring the preponderated (marjuh). And he took this as his madhhab. (We say: Preferring the preponderant (rajih) over the preponderated is the rational [position], and upon this consensus has been formed. So the priority of acting [upon both] is only when the ignored is not preponderated. The secret is that the preponderated in the presence of the preponderant is not a proof, so ignoring it is not ignoring a proof. (And for this) i.e., for preferring the preponderant, Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) gave precedence to his saying (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'Guard yourselves from urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it' (narrated by Hakim and declared sahih) over the drinking of the 'Uranis of camels' urine. Al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Anas that some people from 'Urana or 'Ukl came to Medina and became ill, so the Prophet ordered them to go to the camels of sadaqa and drink from their urine and milk. They did so and recovered, then apostatized, killed the herdsmen, and drove away the camels. He sent after them; they were brought, and he cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides and gouged out their eyes, then did not cauterize them until they died. (The preponderator is prohibition), for it is given precedence over permissibility, (with possibility of restricting the general to what is not eaten for its meat, as Imam Muhammad restricted it and ruled for permissibility of urine of what is eaten [animals]); (or) with possibility of restricting the general to what not (for treatment), as Imam Abu Yusuf restricted it and declared treatment with camels' urine permissible, rather it is absolutely prohibited in one narration, and his saying is more convenient for people. And for preferring the preponderant there are numerous evidences beyond count. And let us present here examples of conflict (as training) for the student to extricate themselves. Among them is what is between the nasb and jar readings in His saying, may He be exalted: {O you who believe, when you rise to prayer, wash your faces and your hands to the elbows, and wipe your heads and your feet to the ankles} [al-Ma'ida 5:6], (which require one (for wiping) because when it is majrur it is conjoined to the heads and falls under wiping, (and) the other (for washing) as when it is mansub, for it is then conjoined to the hands and falls under washing. And reconciliation is attempted by taking jar as [grammatical] adjacency (al-jarr li al-jawar) and that the majrur is conjoined to [the heads] in the state of nasb. But the author (Muslim al-Thubut) did not approve this and said: 'Taking jar as adjacency is opposed by the nasb on the basis of [grammatical] position (al-nasb 'ala al-mahal), for it is possible to be conjoined to the heads as a locative object. So there is no priority for making jar due to adjacency.' But one should not pay heed to this, because those who take jar as adjacency say that the washing of the foot is established definitively by transmission (tawatur), so it is necessary to adopt a departure from the apparent meaning in the jar reading, so it is taken as adjacency. In that case, what is mentioned has no [force]. (I say to you: preferring washing over wiping because the foot is a place of filth, so it is more deserving of washing, like the hand, unlike the head), for there is no likelihood of filth in it. But there is a shade of subtlety, for the discussion is about removing ritual impurity (najasa hukmiyya) and whether it is wiping or washing, and filth has no relevance; except that it may be said that the apparent practice of the Shari'a in removing ritual impurity is in accordance with what nature decrees for removing actual impurity, and that a place of filth is more deserving and appropriate to be considered ritually impure, and this impurity is not removed except by what removes the actual impurity in the ruling. So understand and reflect. (Also: wudu is like ghusl in purifying (the whole body), for minor impurity permeates the entire body like major impurity (janaba), and wudu purifies it like ghusl, so it should be obligatory to wash the whole body in wudu, like in ghusl. But that would be a great hardship, so washing the limbs was set in place of washing (the whole). Thus the foot is among the washed parts. But it should also require washing the head, but he repelled that by saying: 'And He sufficed with wiping the head to remove hardship') for in washing [the head] there is hardship.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a continuation discussing the methods of resolving conflict between evidences. It begins by noting that even those who reject the authority of Companion sayings should still use them to resolve text conflict because they indicate which text is abrogated. Then it lists methods of jam' (reconciliation): for two general texts, diversify (tanwi'); for two absolute texts, restrict each; for two particular texts, apply partially or take one figuratively; for general and particular, specify the general. Then it addresses the principle of whether reconciliation (jam') or preponderance (tarjih) takes precedence. The text refutes the view that jam' is always preferred, arguing that when one evidence is clearly preponderant (rajih), the other is not a proof, so ignoring it is not ignoring proof. It gives the example of Imam Abu Hanifa preferring the hadith 'Guard yourselves from urine' over the permissibility implied by the hadith of the 'Uranis drinking camel urine, because the former is more preponderant (prohibitory). Then it presents a detailed example from the Qur'an (al-Ma'ida 5:6) regarding the reading of 'arjulakum' (feet) as nasb (washing) or jar (wiping). Various approaches to reconciliation are discussed, and the text leans towards washing as preponderant because the foot is a place of filth and wudu is analogous to ghusl in purifying the whole body, with the exception of the head. This is a typical Hanafi usul exposition.

Key Terms
المرجح (al-murajjih): A preponderant evidence that tips the scale in favor of one conflicting evidence over another.
الجمع (al-jam'): Reconciliation of apparently conflicting evidences by interpreting them in a way that both can be applied.
التنويع (al-tanwi'): Diversification: applying each of two conflicting general texts to different subsets of individuals or situations.
التقييد (al-taqyid): Restriction: adding a qualifying condition to each absolute text to differentiate their scopes.
التبعيض (al-tab'id): Partial application: assigning each of two particular texts to different situations, or taking one metaphorically.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Specification: limiting the scope of a general text to exclude what is covered by a particular text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which method of jam' should be used for two conflicting absolute (mutlaq) texts?
A) Tanwi' (diversification)
B) Taqyid (restriction)
C) Tab'id (partial application)
D) Takhsis (specification)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usuli has four distinct tools for jam'; applying the correct one depends on the linguistic type of the conflicting texts.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Tarjih vs Jam': The Hanafi Position on Preponderance
Defending tarjih over jam' and illustrating with the urine hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument for preferring tarjih over jam' when one evidence is preponderant, and apply it to the example of the urine hadiths.

Core Idea
When one evidence is preponderant, the weaker is not a proof, so preferring strength over reconciliation is rational.

This passage defends the Hanafi stance that tarjih (preponderance) takes precedence over jam' (reconciliation) when the conflict cannot be resolved or when one evidence is clearly stronger. The argument is illustrated with two hadiths: one prohibiting contact with urine and another permitting camel urine for treatment. The Hanafi view, following Imam Abu Hanifa, gives precedence to the prohibitory hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting evidences
Locate the two hadiths: (1) 'Guard yourselves from urine...' (prohibitory) and (2) the story of the 'Uranis drinking camel urine (permissive). Note that both are ahad hadiths (zanni al-thubut).
The text also mentions different interpretations by Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf to reconcile, but the core is the preference for prohibition.
2
Determine if one evidence is preponderant (rajih)
Examine factors: the prohibitory hadith is general and prohibitory, while the permissive hadith is specific to a particular incident (treatment). The prohibitory hadith is deemed stronger by the Hanafi school.
Factors include generality vs specificity, and the principle that a prohibition takes precedence over permission when both are possible.
3
Apply the principle: the preponderated is not a proof
Once the prohibitory hadith is deemed rajih, the other hadith (marjuh) loses its probative value in the presence of the stronger evidence. Thus, ignoring it is not ignoring a proof.
This is the key response to Shaykh al-Haddad's objection that jam' is always better.
4
State the resulting ruling
The ruling is that urine in general is impure and contact with it is prohibited. The permissive hadith is either abrogated or restricted to the specific case of treatment with camel urine (and even that is debated among the Sahibayn).
Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that the prohibitory hadith takes precedence, making urine impure.

مرجح
واعلم أيضاً أن من لا يقول بحجية أقوال الصحابة ينبغي أن يعمل بها عند تعارض النصين، فإن من المعلوم أن أحدهما منسوخ بالآخر، وعمل الصحابي موافقاً لأحدهما لكونه ثابتاً، فإن الظاهر أن الصحابي إنما عمل بما هو ثابت دون ما هو منسوخ فافهم (ثم الجمع في العامين المتعارضين (بالتنويع) بأن يخص حكم أحدهما بالبعض والآخر بالبعض الآخر (وفي المطلقين بالتقييد) في كل منهما بقيد مغاير للآخر (وفي الخاصتين بالتبعيض بأن يحمل أحدهما على حال والآخر على حال أو بحمل أحدهما على المجاز) وإبقاء الآخر على الحقيقة وفي العام والخاص بتخصيص العام والعمل (به) فيما وراء الخاص، والعمل بالخاص احتمال الغلط (لا) بأن يقطع بأن المراد بالعام ما وراء الخاص (كتخصيص الشافعية) وعلى مع هذا لا يرد عليهم أن التخصيص فرع المقارنة ولا علم في التعارض بالمقارنة (إن قيل) كما قال الشيخ الهداد (الأعمال) بالدليلين أولى من الإهمال بأحدهما فيقدم الجمع) الذي فيه إعمال الدليلين (على الترجيح الذي فيه إهمال بالمرجوح واتخذ هو تقديم الجمع على الترجيح مذهباً (قلنا : تقديم الراجح على المرجوح هو المعقول) وعليه انعقد الإجماع، فأولوية الاعمال إنما هو إذا لم يكن المهمل مرجوحاً، والسر فيه أن المرجوح عند مقابلة الراجح ليس دليلاً، فليس في إهماله إهمال دليل ( ولهذا ) أي لتقديم الراجح (قدم) الإمام أبو حنيفة) رحمه الله قوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «استنزهوا من البول فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه» رواه الحاكم وصححه على شرب العرنيين أبوال الإبل روى البخاري ومسلم عن أنس قال: قدم النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم نفر من عرينة أو عكل فاجتووا المدينة، فأمرهم أن يأتوا إبل الصدقة ليشربوا من أبوالها وألبانها وفعلوا فصحوا فارتدوا وقتلوا رعاتها واستاقوا الإبل، فبعث في آثارهم فأتي بهم فقطع أيديهم وأرجلهم من خلاف وسمل أعينهم ثم لم يحسمهم حتى ماتوا (المرجح التحريم) فإنه مقدم على الإباحة (مع إمكان حمل العام ما لا يؤكل لحمه كما حمل الإمام محمد فحكم بإباحة بول ما يؤكل ( أو ) مع إمكان حمل العام على ما (لا) يكون (للتداوي) كما حمل الإمام أبو يوسف فحلل التداوي بأبوال الإبل بل المحرم مطلقاً في رواية وقوله أرفق بالناس، ولتقديم الراجح شواهد كثيرة لا تحصى. ولنورد ههنا أمثلة للتعارض (تمرينا) للمتعلم للتخلص عنها فمنها ما بين قراءة النصب والجر في قوله تعالى: ﴿يَتأَيُّهَا الذين امنوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ إِلَى الْمَرَافِقِ وَامْسَحُوا بِرُءُوسِكُمْ وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَينِ ﴾ [المائدة: ٦] (المقتضيين أحدهما (للمسح فإنه إذا كان مجروراً كان معطوفاً على الرؤوس داخلاً تحت المسح (و) الآخر (للغسل) كما إذا كان منصوباً، فإنه معطوف حينئذ على الأيدي داخل تحت الغسل، وجمع بحمل الجر على الجوار وكون المجرور معطوفاً على المعطوف عليه حال النصب ولم يرتض به المص وقال : (وحمل الجر على الجوار معارض بالنصب على المحل فإنه يمكن أن يكون معطوفاً على الرؤوس حملاً على المحل، فإنه مفعول محلاً فلا أولوية لجعل الجر للجوار، لكن ينبغي أن لا يصغي إليه، فإن من جعل الجر للجوار قال : إن غسل الرجل ثابت قطعاً بالتوارث، فلا بد من ارتكاب خلاف الظاهر في قراءة الجر، فحمل على الجوار وحينئذ لا توجه لما ذكر (أقول لك ترجيح الغسل على المسح بأن الرجل محل التلوث، فبالغسل أجدر كاليد دون الرأس) فإنه لا احتمال للتلوث فيه، وفيه شائبة من الخفاء، فإن الكلام في إزالة النجاسة الحكمية وأنها المسح أو الغسل ولا دخل فيه للتلوث، إلا أن يقال الظاهر وقوع الشرع بإزالة النجاسة الحكمية مطابقاً لما يحكم به الطبع من إزالة النجاسة الحقيقية، وأن محل التلوث أحرى وأليق بأن يعتبر نجساً حكماً، ولا تزول هذه النجاسة إلا بما تزول به الحقيقية
