Preponderator (murajjih). And know also that whoever does not hold the authority of the sayings of the Companions should act upon them when two texts conflict, for it is known that one of them is abrogated by the other, and the Companion's practice agrees with one of them because it is established. So it is apparent that the Companion only acted upon what is established, not what is abrogated. So understand. (Then: reconciliation (jam') in two conflicting general texts (ammayn) is by diversification (tanwi'), such that the ruling of one is specified to some [individuals] and the other to others. And in two absolute (mutlaqayn) texts, by restriction (taqyid) in each with a condition different from the other. And in two particular texts (khasatayn), by partial application (tab'id) such that one is applied to one situation and the other to another, or by taking one as metaphorical (majaz) and keeping the other as literal (haqiqa). And in a general and a particular, by specifying the general and acting upon it beyond the particular, and acting upon the particular [is] with possibility of error. (No) not by cutting off that the intended meaning of the general is what is beyond the particular, (like the specification of the Shafi'is). And with this, it is not objected against them that specification is a branch of [knowledge of] contemporaneity (muqarana) and we have no knowledge of contemporaneity in conflict. (If it is said) as said by Shaykh al-Haddad: (Acting upon) both proofs is better than ignoring one, so reconciliation (jam') is preferred over preponderance (tarjih) which involves ignoring the preponderated (marjuh). And he took this as his madhhab. (We say: Preferring the preponderant (rajih) over the preponderated is the rational [position], and upon this consensus has been formed. So the priority of acting [upon both] is only when the ignored is not preponderated. The secret is that the preponderated in the presence of the preponderant is not a proof, so ignoring it is not ignoring a proof. (And for this) i.e., for preferring the preponderant, Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) gave precedence to his saying (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'Guard yourselves from urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it' (narrated by Hakim and declared sahih) over the drinking of the 'Uranis of camels' urine. Al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Anas that some people from 'Urana or 'Ukl came to Medina and became ill, so the Prophet ordered them to go to the camels of sadaqa and drink from their urine and milk. They did so and recovered, then apostatized, killed the herdsmen, and drove away the camels. He sent after them; they were brought, and he cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides and gouged out their eyes, then did not cauterize them until they died. (The preponderator is prohibition), for it is given precedence over permissibility, (with possibility of restricting the general to what is not eaten for its meat, as Imam Muhammad restricted it and ruled for permissibility of urine of what is eaten [animals]); (or) with possibility of restricting the general to what not (for treatment), as Imam Abu Yusuf restricted it and declared treatment with camels' urine permissible, rather it is absolutely prohibited in one narration, and his saying is more convenient for people. And for preferring the preponderant there are numerous evidences beyond count. And let us present here examples of conflict (as training) for the student to extricate themselves. Among them is what is between the nasb and jar readings in His saying, may He be exalted: {O you who believe, when you rise to prayer, wash your faces and your hands to the elbows, and wipe your heads and your feet to the ankles} [al-Ma'ida 5:6], (which require one (for wiping) because when it is majrur it is conjoined to the heads and falls under wiping, (and) the other (for washing) as when it is mansub, for it is then conjoined to the hands and falls under washing. And reconciliation is attempted by taking jar as [grammatical] adjacency (al-jarr li al-jawar) and that the majrur is conjoined to [the heads] in the state of nasb. But the author (Muslim al-Thubut) did not approve this and said: 'Taking jar as adjacency is opposed by the nasb on the basis of [grammatical] position (al-nasb 'ala al-mahal), for it is possible to be conjoined to the heads as a locative object. So there is no priority for making jar due to adjacency.' But one should not pay heed to this, because those who take jar as adjacency say that the washing of the foot is established definitively by transmission (tawatur), so it is necessary to adopt a departure from the apparent meaning in the jar reading, so it is taken as adjacency. In that case, what is mentioned has no [force]. (I say to you: preferring washing over wiping because the foot is a place of filth, so it is more deserving of washing, like the hand, unlike the head), for there is no likelihood of filth in it. But there is a shade of subtlety, for the discussion is about removing ritual impurity (najasa hukmiyya) and whether it is wiping or washing, and filth has no relevance; except that it may be said that the apparent practice of the Shari'a in removing ritual impurity is in accordance with what nature decrees for removing actual impurity, and that a place of filth is more deserving and appropriate to be considered ritually impure, and this impurity is not removed except by what removes the actual impurity in the ruling. So understand and reflect. (Also: wudu is like ghusl in purifying (the whole body), for minor impurity permeates the entire body like major impurity (janaba), and wudu purifies it like ghusl, so it should be obligatory to wash the whole body in wudu, like in ghusl. But that would be a great hardship, so washing the limbs was set in place of washing (the whole). Thus the foot is among the washed parts. But it should also require washing the head, but he repelled that by saying: 'And He sufficed with wiping the head to remove hardship') for in washing [the head] there is hardship.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a continuation discussing the methods of resolving conflict between evidences. It begins by noting that even those who reject the authority of Companion sayings should still use them to resolve text conflict because they indicate which text is abrogated. Then it lists methods of jam' (reconciliation): for two general texts, diversify (tanwi'); for two absolute texts, restrict each; for two particular texts, apply partially or take one figuratively; for general and particular, specify the general. Then it addresses the principle of whether reconciliation (jam') or preponderance (tarjih) takes precedence. The text refutes the view that jam' is always preferred, arguing that when one evidence is clearly preponderant (rajih), the other is not a proof, so ignoring it is not ignoring proof. It gives the example of Imam Abu Hanifa preferring the hadith 'Guard yourselves from urine' over the permissibility implied by the hadith of the 'Uranis drinking camel urine, because the former is more preponderant (prohibitory). Then it presents a detailed example from the Qur'an (al-Ma'ida 5:6) regarding the reading of 'arjulakum' (feet) as nasb (washing) or jar (wiping). Various approaches to reconciliation are discussed, and the text leans towards washing as preponderant because the foot is a place of filth and wudu is analogous to ghusl in purifying the whole body, with the exception of the head. This is a typical Hanafi usul exposition.

Key Terms
المرجح (al-murajjih): A preponderant evidence that tips the scale in favor of one conflicting evidence over another.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant evidence that is stronger and to be followed.
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The weaker evidence that is overridden by the preponderant.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars, cited here to support the preference of rajih over marjuh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core secret (al-sirr) given in the text for why the preponderated evidence can be ignored?
A) It is weak in transmission.
B) It has been abrogated.
C) It is not a proof when faced with a preponderant evidence.
D) It contradicts the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that when one evidence is clearly preponderant, the other loses its probative value, making tarjih the necessary approach.

Case Study: Washing vs Wiping the Feet – Applying Usul Principles
Applying jam' and tarjih to the Qur'anic example of washing vs wiping the feet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the conflicting readings of 'arjulakum' and evaluate the arguments for washing and wiping, identifying the usul principles at play.

Core Idea
The Qur'anic reading allowed both washing and wiping; the preponderant evidence and analogy to ghusl tip the scale toward washing.

This passage applies the jam' and tarjih tools to a concrete Qur'anic example: the verse of wudu (al-Ma'ida 5:6) where the word 'arjulakum' (your feet) can be read in nasb (accusative) implying washing, or jar (genitive) implying wiping. The author discusses attempts at reconciliation (jarr li al-jawar) and then offers arguments for why washing is preponderant, including natural reasoning and analogy (qiyas) to ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two readings and their legal implications
The verse has two qira'at: 'arjulakum' (nasb) and 'arjulikum' (jar). The nasb reading makes 'feet' conjoined to 'hands' (washed), so feet must be washed. The jar reading makes 'feet' conjoined to 'heads' (wiped), so feet are wiped. Both readings are mutawatir? The text suggests the jar reading is also transmitted.
The author notes that the nasb reading indicates washing, jar indicates wiping.
2
Examine the attempted reconciliation: jarr li al-jawar
Some scholars attempt to reconcile by claiming the jar is due to grammatical adjacency (jarr li al-jawar), meaning the feet are actually washed but the genitive case is because of the adjacent word 'heads'. The author rejects this as weak, noting that it is opposed by nasb 'ala al-mahal (accusative due to position).
3
Evaluate the argument for washing based on nature
The author argues that the foot is a place of filth (mahall al-talawuth), so washing is more appropriate, like the hand, unlike the head which is not typically filthy. This is a form of istishan or rational preference.
This argument is presented as a reason for giving preponderance to the washing reading.
4
Apply qiyas: analogy between wudu and ghusl
The author draws an analogy: minor impurity (hadath) permeates the whole body like major impurity (janaba), so wudu should require washing the whole body like ghusl. But hardship (haraj) led to washing only the limbs. Thus, the foot is among the washed parts by default, except the head where wiping suffices due to hardship.
This qiyas strengthens the argument that washing the feet is the original ruling.

وكون المجرور معطوفاً على المعطوف عليه حال النصب ولم يرتض به المص وقال : (وحمل الجر على الجوار معارض بالنصب على المحل فإنه يمكن أن يكون معطوفاً على الرؤوس حملاً على المحل، فإنه مفعول محلاً فلا أولوية في الحكم فافهم وتأمل (وأيضاً: الوضوء كالغسل في تطهير (البدن كله فإن الحدث حل تمام البدن كالجنابة والوضوء يطهره كالغسل فينبغي أن يجب غسل كل البدن في الوضوء، كما في الغسل، لكن كان فيه حرج عظيم فأقيم غسل الأطراف مقام غسل (الكل) فيكون الرجل من المغسولات، لكن كان ينبغي أن يجب غسل الرأس أيضاً فدفعه بقوله : واكتفى في الرأس بالمسح دفعاً للحرج) إذ في غسل
Preponderator (murajjih). And know also that whoever does not hold the authority of the sayings of the Companions should act upon them when two texts conflict, for it is known that one of them is abrogated by the other, and the Companion's practice agrees with one of them because it is established. So it is apparent that the Companion only acted upon what is established, not what is abrogated. So understand. (Then: reconciliation (jam') in two conflicting general texts (ammayn) is by diversification (tanwi'), such that the ruling of one is specified to some [individuals] and the other to others. And in two absolute (mutlaqayn) texts, by restriction (taqyid) in each with a condition different from the other. And in two particular texts (khasatayn), by partial application (tab'id) such that one is applied to one situation and the other to another, or by taking one as metaphorical (majaz) and keeping the other as literal (haqiqa). And in a general and a particular, by specifying the general and acting upon it beyond the particular, and acting upon the particular [is] with possibility of error. (No) not by cutting off that the intended meaning of the general is what is beyond the particular, (like the specification of the Shafi'is). And with this, it is not objected against them that specification is a branch of [knowledge of] contemporaneity (muqarana) and we have no knowledge of contemporaneity in conflict. (If it is said) as said by Shaykh al-Haddad: (Acting upon) both proofs is better than ignoring one, so reconciliation (jam') is preferred over preponderance (tarjih) which involves ignoring the preponderated (marjuh). And he took this as his madhhab. (We say: Preferring the preponderant (rajih) over the preponderated is the rational [position], and upon this consensus has been formed. So the priority of acting [upon both] is only when the ignored is not preponderated. The secret is that the preponderated in the presence of the preponderant is not a proof, so ignoring it is not ignoring a proof. (And for this) i.e., for preferring the preponderant, Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) gave precedence to his saying (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'Guard yourselves from urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it' (narrated by Hakim and declared sahih) over the drinking of the 'Uranis of camels' urine. Al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Anas that some people from 'Urana or 'Ukl came to Medina and became ill, so the Prophet ordered them to go to the camels of sadaqa and drink from their urine and milk. They did so and recovered, then apostatized, killed the herdsmen, and drove away the camels. He sent after them; they were brought, and he cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides and gouged out their eyes, then did not cauterize them until they died. (The preponderator is prohibition), for it is given precedence over permissibility, (with possibility of restricting the general to what is not eaten for its meat, as Imam Muhammad restricted it and ruled for permissibility of urine of what is eaten [animals]); (or) with possibility of restricting the general to what not (for treatment), as Imam Abu Yusuf restricted it and declared treatment with camels' urine permissible, rather it is absolutely prohibited in one narration, and his saying is more convenient for people. And for preferring the preponderant there are numerous evidences beyond count. And let us present here examples of conflict (as training) for the student to extricate themselves. Among them is what is between the nasb and jar readings in His saying, may He be exalted: {O you who believe, when you rise to prayer, wash your faces and your hands to the elbows, and wipe your heads and your feet to the ankles} [al-Ma'ida 5:6], (which require one (for wiping) because when it is majrur it is conjoined to the heads and falls under wiping, (and) the other (for washing) as when it is mansub, for it is then conjoined to the hands and falls under washing. And reconciliation is attempted by taking jar as [grammatical] adjacency (al-jarr li al-jawar) and that the majrur is conjoined to [the heads] in the state of nasb. But the author (Muslim al-Thubut) did not approve this and said: 'Taking jar as adjacency is opposed by the nasb on the basis of [grammatical] position (al-nasb 'ala al-mahal), for it is possible to be conjoined to the heads as a locative object. So there is no priority for making jar due to adjacency.' But one should not pay heed to this, because those who take jar as adjacency say that the washing of the foot is established definitively by transmission (tawatur), so it is necessary to adopt a departure from the apparent meaning in the jar reading, so it is taken as adjacency. In that case, what is mentioned has no [force]. (I say to you: preferring washing over wiping because the foot is a place of filth, so it is more deserving of washing, like the hand, unlike the head), for there is no likelihood of filth in it. But there is a shade of subtlety, for the discussion is about removing ritual impurity (najasa hukmiyya) and whether it is wiping or washing, and filth has no relevance; except that it may be said that the apparent practice of the Shari'a in removing ritual impurity is in accordance with what nature decrees for removing actual impurity, and that a place of filth is more deserving and appropriate to be considered ritually impure, and this impurity is not removed except by what removes the actual impurity in the ruling. So understand and reflect. (Also: wudu is like ghusl in purifying (the whole body), for minor impurity permeates the entire body like major impurity (janaba), and wudu purifies it like ghusl, so it should be obligatory to wash the whole body in wudu, like in ghusl. But that would be a great hardship, so washing the limbs was set in place of washing (the whole). Thus the foot is among the washed parts. But it should also require washing the head, but he repelled that by saying: 'And He sufficed with wiping the head to remove hardship') for in washing [the head] there is hardship.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a continuation discussing the methods of resolving conflict between evidences. It begins by noting that even those who reject the authority of Companion sayings should still use them to resolve text conflict because they indicate which text is abrogated. Then it lists methods of jam' (reconciliation): for two general texts, diversify (tanwi'); for two absolute texts, restrict each; for two particular texts, apply partially or take one figuratively; for general and particular, specify the general. Then it addresses the principle of whether reconciliation (jam') or preponderance (tarjih) takes precedence. The text refutes the view that jam' is always preferred, arguing that when one evidence is clearly preponderant (rajih), the other is not a proof, so ignoring it is not ignoring proof. It gives the example of Imam Abu Hanifa preferring the hadith 'Guard yourselves from urine' over the permissibility implied by the hadith of the 'Uranis drinking camel urine, because the former is more preponderant (prohibitory). Then it presents a detailed example from the Qur'an (al-Ma'ida 5:6) regarding the reading of 'arjulakum' (feet) as nasb (washing) or jar (wiping). Various approaches to reconciliation are discussed, and the text leans towards washing as preponderant because the foot is a place of filth and wudu is analogous to ghusl in purifying the whole body, with the exception of the head. This is a typical Hanafi usul exposition.

Key Terms
الجر بالجوار (al-jarr li al-jawar): Grammatical adjacency: a word takes the genitive case because of an adjacent genitive word, not because of its own syntactic role.
النصب على المحل (al-nasb 'ala al-mahal): Accusative case based on the position/function of the word in the sentence, disregarding the literal case ending.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a common effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which qira'a of 'arjulakum' does the Hanafi school consider preponderant for the ruling of wudu?
A) The jar reading because it is more common.
B) The nasb reading because it implies washing and is supported by qiyas.
C) Both readings are equally valid and a choice can be made.
D) Neither, because the matter is settled by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling to wash the feet in wudu is derived by preponderance (tarjih) of the nasb reading and strengthened by qiyas to ghusl.

The Hanafi Interpretation of 'طهرن' in Quran 2:222
Analyzing Quran 2:222 to derive ruling on intercourse after menses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of mutlaq and muqayyad to the Quranic verse on menstruation and derive the ruling on permissibility of intercourse after cessation of blood.

Core Idea
The Hanafi reading of 'tathahharna' as cessation of blood, not ghusl, allows intercourse before ghusl.

This lesson unpacks a classic Hanafi defense of the ruling that a woman becomes permissible for intercourse as soon as her menstrual blood stops, before performing ghusl. The debate centers on the meaning of the verb in Quran 2:222 and the usul principle of absolute (mutlaq) vs. restricted (muqayyad) terms. By analyzing the flow of the verse and the nature of the 'harm' mentioned, the author establishes why the Hanafi position is linguistically and legally sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two linguistic forms
Examine the two words in the verse: 'yathurna' (with takhif) and 'yatathahharna' (with tashdid). The Hanafis treat them as synonymous, while the Shafi'is distinguish them.
2
Apply the mutlaq-muqayyad principle
Understand the Hanafi usul rule: when an absolute and a restricted term occur in the same ruling, the absolute is carried on the restricted. Here, the absolute 'yathurna' is interpreted by the restricted 'yatathahharna'.
Hanafi: the restricted shows the meaning (cessation of blood). Shafi'i: the restricted shows a separate requirement (ghusl).
3
Analyze the concept of 'adha' (harm)
The verse says: 'It is harm, so keep away...' The author argues that the harm is the physical blood itself (type 1 impurity), not the legal state of janabah (type 2). Type 1 is removed by cessation; type 2 remains but does not prohibit intercourse by consensus.
Type 1: prevents acts requiring purity and permits those that don't (like fasting). Type 2: only prevents acts requiring purity (like prayer).
4
Resolve the dispute using linguistic principles
The author addresses the Shafi'i objection that 'tathahharna' is literal for ghusl and metaphorical for cessation. He argues that the form 'tafa'ala' can mean 'do the action intensely' and that cessation of blood is a complete purification, so the metaphor is valid, supported by context.
Also cites lexicons showing 'tahura' can mean both cessation and ghusl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثاني السنة الاغتسال ويكون يطهرن بالتخفيف بمعنى يطهرن فتكون الحرمة إلى الاغتسال (كما عليه الشافعية بل هذا ،أولى كيف ويطهرن بالتشديد بمنزلة المقيد من يطهرن بالتخفيف، فإن الاغتسال لا يكون إلا بعد الانقطاع الذي هو الطهارة وقد تقدم أن المطلق والمقيد إذا وردا في حكم واحد وجب حمل المطلق على المقيد، مع أنه قيل طهره مشترك جاء بمعنى اغتسل أيضاً، قال في «القاموس» : طهرت : انقطع دمها واغتسلت من الحيض وغيره (قلنا: سوق الكلام أن لا مانع من الوطء إلا) (الأذى قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَيَسْتَلُونَكَ عَنِ الْمَحِيضِ قُلْ هُوَ أَذًى فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۲] وقد ارتفع الأذى حقيقة) بالانقطاع (وحكماً) حيث وجبت العبادات (ولا) توقف بعد المقتضى) وهو النكاح الصحيح ههنا (وعدم المانع) وهو الأذى فيما نحن فيه (فتدبر) وقد يناقش بأنه ليس المراد الأذى النجاسة المرئية، فإن النجاسة في الفرج موجودة على كل حال، بل المراد الأذى الحكمي، وهو موجود إلى الاغتسال فيوجب الحرمة إليه، ولك أن تجيب عنه بأنه : هب أن الأذى ليس مطلق النجاسة المرئية التي يتنفر عنها الجبلة الإنسانية، وهو الدم أو القذر الذي يكون في الأدبار، فالمانع هذه النجاسة، وقد ارتفعت، سلمنا أنه ليس المراد النجاسة المرئية بل الحكمية، لكن هي نوعان : نوع يمنع أهلية ما يشترط فيه الطهارة وأداء ما لا يشترط فيه كالصوم نوع آخر يمنع أداء ما يشترط فيه فقط، كالجنابة، فالمراد بالأذى هو النوع الأول، فإن النوع الثاني لا يوجب حرمة الوطء بالإجماع، وإلا فيحرم وطء الجنب، فكيف لا يراد النوع الأول ويجوز أداء الصوم مع النوع الثاني حتى يصح صوم قطعاً الحائض بعد الانقطاع قبل الغسل، وكذا الجنب، ولا يزيد الوقاع على الصوم في اشترا الطهر عن الأذى، فالمانع هو النوع الأول، وهو لا يكون إلا عند الحيض ويرتفع بالانقطاع، فلا معنى لحرمة الوطء قبل الاغتسال فإن قلت : قد بينت سابقاً أنه لا يصح التخلص المذكور سابقاً، والآن بينت أن تخلص الشافعية أيضاً لا يتم فبأي وجه يتخلص؟ قلت: الأظهر أن يتخلص بأن تحمل قراءة التشديد على التخفيف وهذا غير عزيز ولا بعد فيه فإن تفعل يجيء بمعنى فعل كثيراً لكن إذا انقطع قبل العشرة فاحتمال الدرّ باق فإن الدم قد يدر وقد لا في المدة فمقتضى الاحتياط أن يؤخر إلى أن يظن الانقطاع ، لكنه إذا مر وقت الاغتسال والتحريمة فقد وجبت الصلاة، فاعتبرت طاهرة شرعاً عن الأذى الحكمي الحيضي المانع عن وجوبها، عن حل الوقاع فيحل الوطء ولا يؤخر فإن قلت كيف يحمل الأطهر على انقطاع الدم لأنه مجاز كما نقل عن الكشاف التطهر حقيقة في الاغتسال مجاز في الانقطاع، ولا ينفع مجيء تفعل بمعنى فعل، فإن الكلام في خصوص هذه المادة، قلت: لا نسلم حقيقة فيه، بل هو للمبالغة في الطهارة وهي تتحقق في الاغتسال فإنه نوع من المبالغة، وإذا حمل على الانقطاع أريد به الانقطاع الكامل. نعم، قد كثر استعماله في الاغتسال ولا يلزم من كثرة الاستعمال في فرد منه كونه حقيقة فيه فقط ، مع أنه قال في «القاموس» إنه جاء بمعنى تنزه أيضاً، واللغة لا تتعرض للمعنى المجازي، ولو سلم أنه مجاز في الانقطاع فلا بعد في الحمل عليه لدليل دل كما بينا هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم هذا المقام ولعله من نفائس هذا الكتاب فاحفظه
The second principle: the Sunnah. Ghusl (full bath). And it (the word تَطَهَّرْنَ) appears with tashdid (doubled consonant) meaning yatathahharna (they purify themselves), so the prohibition extends until ghusl — as the Shafi'is hold. Rather, this is even more appropriate? How? Because تَطَهَّرْنَ with tashdid is like a muqayyad (restricted) of yatathahharna with takhif (lightened), for ghusl only occurs after cessation which is purity. It has already been stated that when an absolute and a restricted [term] occur in one ruling, it is necessary to carry the absolute upon the restricted. Additionally, it is said that طُهْر is a homonym, coming also in the meaning of ghusl. Al-Qamus says: طَهَرَتْ: her blood ceased and she performed ghusl from menses and otherwise. We said: The flow of speech indicates that there is no impediment to intercourse except the harm. Allah said: {They ask you about menstruation. Say: It is harm, so keep away from women during menstruation} [2:222]. And the harm has been removed — literally, by cessation, and juristically, since acts of worship become obligatory. And there is no delay after the effective cause (which is valid marriage here) and the absence of the impediment (which is the harm in our case). So ponder. It may be objected that what is meant by harm is not visible impurity, for impurity in the private part exists in any case, but rather the legal harm, which exists until ghusl, thus it necessitates prohibition until then. You may answer: Assume harm is not absolute visible impurity that human nature shrinks from, i.e., blood or filth in the anus; the impediment is this impurity, and it is removed. We accept that it is not visible impurity but legal harm, but it is of two types: a type that prevents eligibility for acts requiring purity and also permits acts like fasting; another type that only prevents acts requiring purity, like janabah. So what is meant by harm is the first type, for the second type does not cause prohibition of intercourse by consensus; otherwise intercourse with a junub would be prohibited. So why would the first type not be intended? It is permissible to perform fasting with the second type, such that the fast of a menstruating woman after cessation before ghusl is valid, and similarly the junub. And intercourse does not exceed fasting in requirement of purity from harm. So the impediment is the first type, which only exists at menstruation and is removed by cessation. Thus there is no meaning to prohibit intercourse before ghusl. If you say: I have already shown previously that the mentioned resolution is not sound, and now you have shown that the Shafi'i resolution also is not complete, by what means is it resolved? I say: The most apparent is to resolve by reading the tashdid as takhif, and this is not uncommon nor far-fetched, for تَفْعَل may come in the meaning of فَعَل often. But if [the blood] stops before ten days, the possibility of continuation remains, for blood may continue or not within the period, so caution dictates delaying until one thinks it has stopped. However, when the time for ghusl and the forbiddenness have passed, prayer has become obligatory, so she is considered legally pure from the menstrual legal harm that prevented its obligation, and from the permissibility of intercourse, so intercourse is permissible and is not delayed. If you say: How can you carry تَطَهَّر on cessation of blood? That is metaphorical, as transmitted from al-Kashshaf: التَّطَهَّر is literal in ghusl, metaphorical in cessation. And the coming of تَفْعَل in the meaning of فَعَل is of no benefit, for the discussion is about this specific material. I say: We do not accept it as literal there; rather it is for exaggeration in purity, which is realized in ghusl as a kind of exaggeration. If carried on cessation, complete cessation is intended. Yes, it is frequently used for ghusl, but frequency of use for one instance does not necessitate it being literal only. Moreover, al-Qamus states that it also came in the meaning of 'being purified', and lexicography does not address metaphorical meaning. Even if we accept it is metaphorical for cessation, there is no objection to carrying it upon it due to evidence as we have shown. This is how this topic should be understood, and perhaps it is among the precious gems of this book, so memorize it.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of the Quranic verse on menstruation (2:222) and a defense of the Hanafi position that a woman becomes permissible for intercourse as soon as her menstrual blood ceases, even before she performs ghusl. The author engages in a discussion with the Shafi'i school, which holds that intercourse is prohibited until after ghusl. The key linguistic point is the meaning of the verb تَطَهَّرْنَ (with tashdid) in the verse: the Hanafis argue that it can be interpreted as equivalent to يَطْهُرْنَ (with takhif), meaning 'they become pure' (i.e., cessation of blood), while the Shafi'is take it literally as 'they perform ghusl.' The author employs the usul principle that an absolute term (mutlaq) when paired with a restricted term (muqayyad) must be carried on the latter, but he also shows that the context of the verse indicates that the impediment to intercourse is the 'harm' (adha) of blood, which is removed by cessation. He further distinguishes between two types of legal impurity: one that prevents acts requiring purity (like prayer) and one that merely prevents those acts but does not prohibit intercourse (like janabah). Menstrual impurity is of the first type, which is removed by cessation. The commentary follows the author's step-by-step reasoning, addressing objections and resolving the linguistic debate by noting that تَفْعَل can be used for repetition but also for the basic meaning, and that the lexicographers do not restrict the word to ghusl. The final ruling: a woman whose menses stops before ten days must wait until she is certain it has stopped, but if the time for prayer enters, she is considered pure and intercourse is permitted.

Key Terms
طهرن (tathahharna): In this passage, the word is debated: Hanafi interprets it as 'become pure (by cessation of blood)', Shafi'i as 'perform ghusl'.
أذى (adha): Harm; in the verse, the blood itself. The text distinguishes between two types: one that prevents acts requiring purity (like menstruation) and one that does not (like janabah).
مطلق ومقيد (mutlaq wa muqayyad): Absolute and restricted terms; the principle that when both occur in the same ruling, the absolute must be interpreted in light of the restricted. Here, 'yathurna' (mutlaq) is restricted by 'yatathahharna' (muqayyad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the meaning of 'hatta yatathahharna' in Quran 2:222?
A) Until they perform ghusl
B) Until they become pure (i.e., their blood stops)
C) Until they have completed ten days
D) Until they have made intention for purity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of 'tathahharna' as cessation of blood, based on the usul principle of mutlaq and muqayyad, demonstrates how linguistic analysis and context combine to derive a ruling.

Resolving Verse Contradiction: Ghampus and Kaffarah
Resolving conflict between two verses on oath accountability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of resolving apparent contradiction (takhrij al-matan) between two Quranic verses by distinguishing between eschatological and this-worldly accountability, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The apparent contradiction is resolved: one verse addresses afterlife punishment, the other this-worldly expiation.

This passage presents a classic usul challenge: two Quranic verses appear to give opposite rulings on false oaths (ghamus). The Hanafi masters resolve this by distinguishing between types of accountability — ukhrawi (eschatological) and dunyawi (this-worldly expiation). This method preserves the integrity of both texts. We will walk through the verses, the Shafi'i dispute, and the Hanafi reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Verses
Locate the two verses: al-Baqarah 2:225 (accountability for 'earned' oaths) and al-Ma'idah 5:89 (accountability for 'contracted' oaths). Note the apparent conflict over ghampus.
Ghampus is a false oath about the past, knowingly false.
2
Understand the Hanafi Resolution
The Hanafi resolution: the first verse refers to eschatological accountability (punishment in the Hereafter), while the second verse refers to this-worldly accountability (kaffarah). Ghampus is not 'contracted' so no kaffarah.
The context 'earned by hearts' indicates afterlife; legal custom (urf) defines 'contract' for future oaths.
3
Trace the Shafi'i Position
The Shafi'is argue that 'contract' includes the heart's determination, so ghampus is contracted and requires kaffarah. They also cite general principles of oath-breaking.
They interpret both verses as referring to this-worldly accountability.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Rebuttal
The Hanafi rebuttal: 'contract' is a legal term for future oaths; carrying it on heart's determination is a legal metaphor not to be taken literally. The Shafi'i view leads to absurd consequences (trivializing major sin).
The proof includes Quranic usage of 'uqud' (contracts) for future commitments.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The text strongly favors the Hanafi position, arguing it avoids contradiction and upholds the gravity of false oaths. The mufta bihi is that ghampus requires no kaffarah.
This is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

ومنها ما بين آيتي اللغو في اليمين تفيد إحداهما وهي قوله تعالى في البقرة: ﴿لَّا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللهُ بِالغْوِ فِي أَيْمَنِكُمْ وَلَكِن يُؤَاخِذُكُم بِمَا كَسَبَتْ قُلُوبُكُمْ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٢٥] (المؤاخذة بالغموس) وهو الحلف على الماضي مع العلم بالكذب لأنها مكسوبة فدخلت فيما كسبت قلوبكم (و) الآية (الأخرى) وهي قوله تعالى في سورة المائدة: ﴿وَلَا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللهُ بِاللغْوِ فِي أَيْمَنِكُمْ وَلَكِن يُؤَاخِذُكُم بِمَا عَقَدتُم الْأَيْمَنَ ﴾ [المائدة : ۸۹] تفيد (عدمها) في الغموس (إذ ليست معقودة) وهي اليمين على المستقبل بأنه يفعل كذا أو لا يفعل قال الإمام مالك : هذا التفسير أحسن شيء سمعت في الباب (والمفهوم من لا يؤاخذكم بكذا) و(لكن) يؤاخذكم بكذا) عدم الواسطة) والحصر في المذكورين فخرجت مرة عن اللغو) حيث دخلت في مقابلها وهي المكسوبة كما في الآية الأولى، وثبت به المؤاخذة فيها ودخلت فيه مرة (أخرى) وانتفى المؤاخذة فيها وذلك لشيوع استعماله فيما لا يقصد وهذا المعنى صار مقابلاً للمكسوب (وفيما لا يفيد) وبهذا الاعتبار صار مقابلاً للمعقود : فحمل في الموضعين على ما يصح به المقابلة فالتعارض في الآيتين باعتبار أن الأولى تثبت المؤاخذة في الغموس والأخرى تنفيها فيها (والتخلص) عند مشايخنا (بأن) المؤاخذة (الثابتة) في الغموس (هي الأخروية للإضافة إلى كسب القلب وهي القرينة على كونها أخروية (و) المؤاخذة (المنفية) فيها هي الدنيوية وهي الكفارة فلا كفارة فيها عندنا، وهذا التخلص من قبل الحكم، لا يقال : روى البخاري عن أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله عنها نزلت : ولَا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللهُ بِاللَّغْوِ فِي أَيْمَنِكُمْ ﴾ [المائدة : ۸۹] في قول الرجل لا والله وبلى والله، وفي رواية أبي داود : قالت عائشة رضي الله عنها : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: هو قول الرجل في يمينه كلا والله بلى والله لأنا نقول هذا التفسير والنزول مسلم، لكن من أين علم أن المراد في آية المائدة، بل يجوز أن يراد آية البقرة والشافعية يحملونهما) أي المؤاخذتين المذكورتين في الآيتين على الدنيوية) ويدرجون الغموس في المعقودة (لأنها من المعقودة بعقد القلب وعزمه عليه والعقد العزم فيكون ما عقدتم الإيمان بمعنى ما كسبت قلوبكم، فتجب الكفارة في الغموس عندهم ودفعه بأن العقد مجاز (في) عقد (القلب) وعزمه، فإن العقد في الأصل عقد الحبل وشد بعضه مع بعض وهو لا يتحقق إلا في المنعقدة، لأن ربط الجزاء بالشرط لإيجاب الصدق فيه دون الغموس ( يدفع) بأنه أعم لغة) من عقد القلب، فلا يكون مجازاً فيه، فإنه في اللغة ربط شيء بشيء فكيف لا ولم يتأيد كونه عقد القلب من أهل اللغة (وأجيب بأنه في عرف الشرع لما له حكم في المستقبل كما نقلنا عن الإمام مالك (قال تعالى: ﴿أَوْفُوا بِالْعُقُودِ ﴾ [المائدة: ١] فتدبر فالحمل على عقد القلب مجاز شرعي فلا يحمل عليه، ثم إن فيما ذهب إليه الشافعية تسوية المنعقدة ،المباحة، بل قد يكون بعض اليمين المنعقدة واجباً أيضاً والغموس الذي هو من أكبر الكبائر وأفسق الفسوق في الساتر، ولم يعهد هذا في الشريعة أصلاً، وكيف يعهد ولو وعد الشارع بستر هذه الكبيرة بالكفارة لكان المدعي الكاذب بمساغ في حلفه الكاذب، فيحلف كاذباً ويأخذ المال بالباطل ثم يكفر، وهل هذا إلا فتح الباب الظلم، وبما قررنا ظهر لك عدم اتجاه ما قيل في دفع التعارض أن المراد في الآيتين
And among them [the examples] is what is between the two verses concerning laghw in oaths. One of them - and it is His saying in al-Baqarah: {Allah will not impose blame upon you for what is meaningless in your oaths, but He will impose blame upon you for what your hearts have earned} [2:225] - indicates accountability for the false oath (al-ghamus), which is swearing about the past knowingly false, because it is earned, thus it enters 'what your hearts have earned.' The other verse - and it is His saying in al-Ma'idah: {Allah will not impose blame upon you for what is meaningless in your oaths, but He will impose blame upon you for what you have contracted in oaths} [5:89] - indicates no accountability for the false oath because it is not contracted. The contracted oath is about the future: that he will do such and such or not. Imam Malik said: This interpretation is the best thing I have heard on the topic. And what is understood from 'He will not impose blame upon you for such and such' and 'but He will impose blame upon you for such and such' is the absence of an intermediary and restriction to the two mentioned categories. Thus [the false oath] once exits from laghw - where it enters its opposite, i.e., earned, as in the first verse, through which accountability is established - and another time it enters [the category] and accountability is negated. This is because of the common usage of [laghw] for what is not intended; this meaning became opposite of 'earned.' And in what does not benefit, in this regard it became opposite of 'contracted.' So it is carried in each context on what makes the contrast appropriate. Thus there is a contradiction between the two verses, in that the first establishes accountability for ghampus and the second negates it. The resolution according to our Mashayikh (Hanafi scholars) is that the accountability established for ghampus is eschatological (ukhrawi), due to its attribution to 'earned by the heart' which is a context indicating it is ukhrawi, and the accountability negated is this-worldly (dunyawi), i.e., the expiation (kaffarah). So there is no kaffarah for ghampus with us. This is a resolution from the perspective of the ruling. It should not be said: Bukhari narrated from Umm al-Mu'minin A'isha al-Siddiqah (may Allah be pleased with her) that the verse {Allah will not impose blame...} [5:89] was revealed concerning a man's saying 'No, by Allah' and 'Yes, by Allah.' And in Abu Dawud's narration, A'isha (RA) said: The Messenger of Allah (SAW) said: 'It is a man's saying in his oath: No, by Allah; Yes, by Allah.' We say: This interpretation and revelation are accepted, but how is it known that it is meant in the verse of al-Ma'idah? It is possible it refers to the verse of al-Baqarah. The Shafi'is carry both - i.e., the two accountabilities mentioned in the two verses - on the this-worldly [accountability] and include ghampus among the contracted oaths, because it is [said to be] contracted by the contract of the heart and its determination, and 'contract' means determination, so 'what you have contracted in oaths' becomes synonymous with 'what your hearts have earned.' Thus kaffarah is obligatory for ghampus according to them. This is countered by saying that 'contract' is metaphorical for the contract of the heart and its determination, for 'contract' originally means tying a rope and joining its parts, which is only realized in a future oath because linking the consequence to the condition necessitates truthfulness in it, unlike ghampus. This counter is in turn refuted by saying that [contract] is linguistically more general than contract of the heart, so it is not metaphorical for it, because in language it means tying something to something. How could it not be? And it has not been affirmed by linguists that it is contract of the heart. And it is answered that in the legal custom (shar'), it has a ruling concerning the future, as we transmitted from Imam Malik. Allah says: {Fulfill the contracts} [5:1]. So ponder. Thus carrying it on the contract of the heart is a legal metaphor, so it should not be carried upon it. Moreover, the Shafi'is' position equates the contracted oath (which is permissible, and some may even be obligatory) with ghampus, which is among the major sins and most wicked of transgressions regarding concealment. This has never been witnessed in the Shari'ah at all. How could it be? If the Lawgiver promised to conceal this major sin through kaffarah, then a false claimant would have a way to utter a false oath, swearing falsely and taking property wrongfully, then expiating. Is this not opening the door to oppression? And with what we have established, it becomes clear to you that what is said in resolving the contradiction - that the intended meaning in the two verses is...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage addresses a classic usul problem: two Quranic verses on oaths appear contradictory. The first verse (al-Baqarah 2:225) imposes accountability for 'what your hearts have earned,' which includes false oaths (ghampus - deliberate lies about the past). The second verse (al-Ma'idah 5:89) states that there is no blame for laghw (unintentional oaths) and only blame for 'contracted' oaths (future oaths). The contradiction: ghampus is held accountable in the first verse but not in the second. The Hanafi resolution, attributed to the Mashayikh, is to distinguish between eschatological accountability (punishment in the Hereafter) and this-worldly accountability (kaffarah). The first verse refers to the afterlife, so ghampus is sinful and deserves punishment; the second verse refers to this-worldly expiation, so ghampus does not require kaffarah. The passage then discusses the Shafi'i view that ghampus does incur kaffarah, arguing that 'contract' (عقد) includes the heart's determination, thus ghampus is contracted. The Hanafi response is that 'contract' in the legal sense is metaphorical for future oaths, and the Shafi'i interpretation would lead to legal absurdities: equating a minor oath with a major sin, allowing a false swearer to pay kaffarah as a license to cheat. The commentary follows the author's step-by-step analysis of the verses, the dispute with Shafi'is, and the final Hanafi position that there is no kaffarah for a deliberate false oath, only punishment in the afterlife.

Key Terms
الغموس (al-ghamus): An oath in which a person swears falsely about the past, knowing they are lying. It is a major sin.
اللغو (al-laghw): An oath made without intention, often by habit (e.g., saying 'No, by Allah' without intent). It carries no accountability.
عقد اليمين (aqd al-yamin): A contracted oath binding oneself to do or not do something in the future. It is contrasted with ghampus.
المؤاخذة الأخروية (al-mu'akhadhah al-ukhrawiyyah): Accountability in the Hereafter; punishment for sin after death.
المؤاخذة الدنيوية (al-mu'akhadhah al-dunyawiyyah): Accountability in this world; includes legal penalties and expiations like kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi resolution of the contradiction between al-Baqarah 2:225 and al-Ma'idah 5:89, why does ghampus (a deliberate false oath about the past) NOT require expiation (kaffarah)?
A) Because it is not a contracted oath in the legal sense, and the accountability in al-Baqarah refers to afterlife punishment.
B) Because ghampus is considered laghw (unintentional) and thus forgiven.
C) Because the Quranic verses are abrogated by later revelation.
D) Because the Shafi'i school has a different interpretation, but Hanafi still requires kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction between the two oath verses is resolved by the Hanafi distinction between eschatological and this-worldly accountability, ruling that ghampus does not incur kaffarah.

12 min
Tarjih: Preponderance Factors in Conflicting Texts
Listing and explaining factors of textual preponderance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the Hanafi factors of tarjih (preponderance) when two textual evidences conflict, giving reasons for each factor.

Core Idea
Preponderance is given by textual features, probability, and practice — not by arbitrary preference.

When two texts conflict, a Hanafi usuli does not abandon either; instead, he seeks preponderance (tarjih) through specific factors. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut enumerates these factors, ranging from internal textual clues like mentioning a cause, to external ones like the practice of the Caliphs. Understanding these factors is essential for any serious student of Hanafi usul, as they guide juristic preference in real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict and available clues
First, confirm that two texts genuinely conflict and cannot be reconciled. Then, examine whether one text mentions an explicit cause (illah) or reason (sabab) for its ruling.
This is the most basic factor: a ruling mentioned with its cause is stronger.
2
Apply the takhsis vs. ta'wil rule
If one text can be specified (takhsis) by another and the other can be interpreted (ta'wil), the Hanafi rule gives preponderance to specification because it is more frequent.
Frequency of occurrence in Sharia makes specification more probable.
3
Check agreement with qiyas
A text that agrees with analogical reasoning (qiyas) is given preponderance over one that opposes it. This is because most rulings are based on effective causes, so agreement with qiyas makes the text's meaning more probable.
Not because qiyas adds strength, but because the majority of rulings follow this pattern.
4
Consider negation vs. affirmation in fame-related issues
In matters where the norm is widespread fame, a text that negates the ruling is preferred over one that affirms it, if the affirming text is not famous. Example: hadith on wudu from touching the penis (negation) over the contradictory affirmation.
If the affirming text were famous, the rule might differ.
5
Evaluate external practice evidence
The practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs is a strong preponderance factor, as they would not have acted contrary to a valid ruling. The practice of the people of Medina is also considered, but with reservation.
The author hints at dispute regarding Medinan practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وموجب الطلاق والعتاق يترجح على نافيهما لأن موجبهما في قوة المحرم و يترجح الحكم المعلل أي الحكم المذكور مع العلة على غيره أي الحكم الذي لم يذكر لأن ذكر العلة ينادي على الأهمية وما ذكر معه السبب يترجح على نقيضه لأن ذكر السبب قرينة الأهمية و الترجيح في المتن قد يكون بالأغلبية كالتخصيص يترجح على التأويل يعني إذا تعارض نصان وتعارض وجوه جمعهما كتخصيص أحدهما وتأويل الآخر يترجح التخصيص على التأويل لكثرة التخصيص بالنسبة إلى التأويل كما تقدم أنه يجمع بتخصيص عند معارضة الخاص وموافقة القياس تترجح على المخالفة يعني إذا تعارض نصان وأحدهما موافق للقياس والآخر مخالف له، فالموافق مرجح على المذهب الأصح لا لأن الموافق يترجح بانضمام القياس إليه، كيف والقياس حجة لو انفرد بنفسه وما يكون حجة بانفراده لا يقع به الترجيح، بل لأن الغالب في الأحكام ما يكون معللاً، ويقاس عليه غيره، والظن تابع للأغلب، فالظن بثبوته أقوى وما لم ينكر الأصل روايته إنكار سكوت على ما أنكر ذلك لا يرى سقوط الحديث به وإنما قيدنا الإنكار بإنكار السكوت، لأنه إذا أنكر الإنكار عند من إنكار التكذيب سقط الخبر عن الحجية إجماعاً فلا اعتداد به حتى يعارض الصحيح منه ويطلب الترجيح والنفي يترجح على الإثبات فيما الغالب فيه الشهرة لو كان ولم يشتهر كحديث انتقاض الوضوء بمس الذكر على حديث الانتقاض به وحديث مس رجل أم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة في الصلاة على حديث انتقاضه بمس النساء الظاهر إسقاط هذا الكلام، فإن الإثبات فيما الغالب فيه الشهرة مع عدم الاشتهار مردود ولا يعمل به لو انفرد عن المعارض عندنا، فلا يصلح معارضاً لحديث النفي، فلا يطلب الترجيح و الترجيح في المتن قد يكون بعمل الخلفاء الراشدين، فإن الظاهر من عملهم بقاء ذلك الحكم، لأنهم أجل من أن يخفى عليهم الحكم الثابت الواجب العمل وقيل و يقع الترجيح بعمل أهل المدينة فإنهم أعرف بالأحكام لكون المدينة المطهرة مهبطاً للوحي ومنقية للخبث كما ينقي الكير خبث الحديد، وفيه ما فيه
The cause of divorce and manumission is given preponderance over its negation because its cause is in the strength of the prohibited. And the ruled-upon mentioned with the cause is given preponderance over other than it, i.e., the ruling not mentioned, because mentioning the cause indicates importance. And what is mentioned with the reason is given preponderance over its opposite because mentioning the reason is an indication of importance. And preponderance in the text may be by majority, such as specification (takhsis) which is given preponderance over interpretation (ta'wil). That is, if two texts conflict and the ways of reconciling them conflict, like specifying one and interpreting the other, specification is given preponderance over interpretation due to the frequency of specification relative to interpretation, as previously mentioned that reconciliation is done by specification when the specific conflicts with the general. And agreement with analogical reasoning (qiyas) is given preponderance over opposition. That is, if two texts conflict and one agrees with qiyas and the other opposes it, the agreeing one is given preponderance according to the most sound madhhab. Not because the agreeing one is preferred by the addition of qiyas to it—how so, when qiyas is a proof by itself, and what is a proof alone does not effect preponderance—but because most rulings are based on effective causes and analogized to others, and probability follows the majority, so the probability of its establishment is stronger. And as long as the origin is not denied, its narration with denial of silence does not cause the hadith to fall, according to what is denied. We only restrict denial to denial by silence because if one denies by denial of accusation, the report falls from authority by consensus, so it is not considered until it opposes the authentic one and preponderance is sought. And negation is given preponderance over affirmation in matters where fame is predominant, if it is not famous, like the hadith of the nullification of wudu by touching the penis over the hadith of nullification by it, and the hadith of touching the foot of the Mother of the Believers Aisha in prayer over the hadith of nullification by touching women; the apparent import of this statement is dropped. For affirmation in matters where fame is predominant, while lacking fame, is rejected and not acted upon if it stands alone against opposition according to us, so it is not valid as an opponent to the hadith of negation, so preponderance is not sought. And preponderance in the text may be by the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, for the apparent implication of their practice is the continuance of that ruling, because they are too great to have the established ruling, which necessitates action, hidden from them. And it is said that preponderance is made by the practice of the people of Medina, for they are more knowledgeable of rulings because Medina, the purified, is the descent of revelation and purifies impurity as the bellows purify the dross of iron—but there is something in that.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage expands on factors that give preponderance (tarjih) to one textual evidence over another. The author first states that a ruling mentioned with its cause (علة) is stronger than one without, because mentioning the cause signals importance. Similarly, mentioning the reason (سبب) strengthens the ruling. Then, he discusses preponderance in the matn (text): specificity (takhsis) is preferred over interpretation (ta'wil) when reconciling conflicting texts, because takhsis is more common. Next, a text that agrees with qiyas (analogical reasoning) is given preponderance over one that opposes it. This is not because qiyas adds strength, but because most Sharia rulings are based on causes and analogies, so probability leans toward the text that fits the pattern. The author then addresses a nuance: if the original narrator does not deny the hadith but remains silent, that silence does not nullify the hadith. However, if the denial is explicit (تكذيب), the report loses authority. He also discusses the rule that negation (نفي) overrides affirmation (إثبات) in matters where the norm is widespread fame, if the affirmation is not famous. Examples are given: the hadith on wudu nullification by touching the penis (negation of nullification) is preferred over a contradictory hadith, because the negation is more famous. Finally, the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and, with some reservation, the practice of the people of Medina are cited as factors of preponderance.

Key Terms
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Specification of a general text by a specific text
التأويل (al-ta'wil): Allegorical interpretation to reconcile conflicting texts
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a text that agrees with qiyas (analogical reasoning) have preponderance over a text that opposes it?
A) Because qiyas is a stronger proof than textual evidence
B) Because the majority of rulings are based on causes and can be analogized, making probability stronger
C) Because the text agreeing with qiyas is always from the Qur'an
D) Because the opposing text has a weaker chain of transmission

Key Takeaway
Tarjih in Hanafi usul relies on a hierarchy of factors: cause/reason mention, takhsis over ta'wil, qiyas agreement, negation over affirmation in fame issues, and practice of the Caliphs — each grounded in probability and frequency.

The Eighth Objection: Can Zahir Prove a Qat'i Matter?
Refuting an objection that zahir cannot prove qat'i ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the qat'i nature of zahir and identify the difference between cutting off probability from evidence and cutting off absolute probability.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, zahir is qat'i unless subject to ta'wil, but it only cuts off probability from evidence, not absolute probability.

This passage addresses the eighth objection to the verse 'سبيل المؤمنين' as proof for ijma. The objector claims the verse is merely zahir and cannot establish a qat'i matter. The Hanafi response refines the concept of qat'i: zahir is qat'i in our school, but its qat'i is limited compared to ijma. This lesson unpacks the layers of probability and the authority of zahir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector argues that the verse (Quran 4:115) is only 'zahir' and lacks definitive contextual indicators (qara'in qati'a), so it cannot prove a definitive matter like ijma.
The verse in question: 'وَمَن يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِن بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَىٰ وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ'
2
Understand the Hanafi definition of zahir as qat'i
The Hanafi response states that 'zahir' is considered qat'i (definitive) according to their usul, unless it has been subject to ta'wil (interpretation). Its authority is self-evident, not dependent on ijma.
Zahir is qat'i because it cuts off probability that arises from evidence, but it still allows absolute probability in theory.
3
Distinguish types of probability
There is a subtle but crucial difference: zahir cuts off probability arising from evidence, while ijma cuts off probability absolutely. Therefore, zahir cannot serve as a proof for the qat'i nature of ijma itself, but it can establish qat'i rulings in other contexts.
This distinction prevents a circular argument.
4
Analyze the second objection and refutation
Another objection claims that if the verse were proof, it would negate ijma because the believers' way is to rely on non-ijma proofs. The response clarifies that 'other' here means contradictory, not merely different; once ijma exists, relying on it is consistent.
The verse actually supports ijma by making it part of the believers' way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عن الثامن : فالظاهر أنه قوي وإن لم تكن الكريمة محفوفة بقرائن حالية قاطعة للاحتمالات، وأجيب بان الظاهر قطعي عندنا وإنما يكون ظنياً لو كان مؤوّلا، وليس حجيته ثابتة بالإجماع بل حجية القواطع جلية في نفسها وضرورة دينية، وإذا كان قطعياً فيثبت به الأمر القطعي، وبعد فيه خفاء ظاهر فإن الظاهر قطعي عندنا بمعنى أنه لا يحتمل خلافه احتمالاً ناشئاً عن دليل، وإن كان فيه مطلق الاحتمال والإجماع قطعي، بمعنى أنه يقطع الاحتمال مطلقاً، فالظاهر لا يقع مثبتاً لهذا القطعي فافهم ثم أورد على الدليل بأنه لو تم لدل على عدم حجية الإجماع فإن سبيل المؤمنين المجتمعين إنما تمسكوا بما سوى الإجماع على الحكم المجمع عليه، فالاستدلال بإجماعهم غير سبيل المؤمنين، وضعفه ظاهر فإن الغير ما ينافي سبيلهم ولو كان المراد مطلق المغايرة فسبيلهم التمسك بما سوى الإجماع عند عدمه والتمسك به بعد لا يكون غير سبيلهم هذا غاية الكلام في تحقيق هذا الوجه
As for the eighth [objection]: It appears that it is strong even if the noble verse is not surrounded by contextual indicators that cut off probabilities. It was answered that 'zahir' is definitive (qat'i) according to us; it would only be speculative (zanni) if it were interpreted (mu'awwal). Its authority is not established by ijma, rather the authority of definitive proofs is clear in themselves and a religious necessity. And if it is definitive, it establishes a definitive matter. But after that, there is apparent obscurity: 'zahir' is definitive according to us in the sense that it does not admit a contrary probability arising from evidence, although it admits absolute probability, while ijma is definitive in the sense that it cuts off probability absolutely. So 'zahir' cannot be a proof for this definitive matter. Understand! Then an objection was raised against the proof: if it were valid, it would prove the non-authority of ijma, because the way of the assembled believers is that they adhere to what is other than ijma concerning the ruled-upon matter. So deducing proof from their consensus is not their way. Its weakness is apparent: 'other' is what contradicts their way. If what is meant is absolute difference, their way is adherence to what is other than ijma when it is absent, and adherence to it after is not different from their way. This is the sum of the discourse in verifying this aspect.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an objection and response concerning the first proof for the authority of ijma (the verse 'سبيل المؤمنين'). The eighth objection argues that the verse is only 'zahir' (apparent) and not surrounded by definitive contextual indicators, so it cannot prove a definitive matter like ijma. The Hanafi response distinguishes: 'zahir' is considered qat'i (definitive) in our school unless it is subject to ta'wil (interpretation). However, the authority of 'zahir' is not itself based on ijma; rather, definitive proofs are self-evident and a religious necessity. If 'zahir' is qat'i, it can establish a qat'i ruling. Yet there is a subtlety: 'zahir' cuts off probability that arises from evidence, but it still allows absolute probability in theory, whereas ijma cuts off probability absolutely. So 'zahir' cannot be the proof for the qat'i nature of ijma itself. The objector further argues that if the verse were proof, it would negate ijma because the 'way of the believers' is to rely on other proofs, not on ijma. The response clarifies that 'other' here means contradictory, not merely different; the believers' way is to rely on other proofs when ijma is absent, but relying on ijma after its existence is not contradictory. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
الظاهر (al-zahir): The apparent meaning that is qat'i (definitive) in the absence of ta'wil; it cuts off probability arising from evidence but not absolute probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, in Hanafi usul, when is 'zahir' considered to cut off probability arising from evidence?
A) When it is surrounded by definitive contextual indicators
B) When it is not subject to ta'wil (interpretation)
C) Only when it is confirmed by ijma
D) When it is transmitted through tawatur

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between cutting off probability from evidence and cutting off absolute probability is crucial for understanding the epistemic weight of texts and the role of ijma.

The Ruling of Khuzayma's Testimony: A Case of Ikhtisas Not Subject to Qiyas
Discusses the specificity of Khuzayma's testimony as a karama not subject to qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats Khuzayma's testimony as an ikhtisas (specific ruling) that cannot be extended by qiyas, and evaluate the counterarguments.

Core Idea
A karama-based ruling is an exception from general qiyas; its rationality does not justify analogical extension.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut explores a key usul principle: when a ruling is established as a miracle (karama) for a specific individual, it cannot be extended to others through qiyas, even if the rationale seems understandable. The example of Khuzayma ibn Thabit, whose single testimony was accepted by the Prophet ﷺ as sufficient, illustrates this principle. We will examine the textual basis, the arguments for specificity, and the responses to objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its textual basis
Locate the hadith 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him, it is sufficient for him' and note that this is an explicit text (nass) establishing a specific ruling for Khuzayma.
The ruling is that his testimony alone suffices like two witnesses.
2
Understand the story and the claim of karama
Read the story of the camel purchase. Note that Khuzayma testified based on his belief in the Prophet's truthfulness, even though he was not present. This understanding was unique to him, making it a karama.
The uniqueness of his understanding is the basis for ikhtisas.
3
Recognize the principle of ikhtisas and its effect on qiyas
The text states that this ruling is a karama specific to Khuzayma, so it cannot be analogized to others, even those of higher status like the caliphs.
This is a key usul rule: specific exceptions from general rules are not subject to qiyas.
4
Analyze the objections and responses
The passage presents objections: that the hadith does not prove ikhtisas, that ta'lil could make it general, or that it is naskh. Study the Hanafi responses, including the argument that context indicates ikhtisas and that ta'lil would require abrogation.
Note the distinction between takhsis (specification) and naskh (abrogation).
5
Conclude with the usul principle and its application
The well-known view is that this ruling is an exception, like the acceptance of a midwife's testimony to avoid hardship. Thus, it is not generalizable.
Rationality of the ruling does not permit qiyas when ikhtisas is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الرابع/ القياس عنك فيه فلا يعمم) بالتعليل، ولا يبعد أن يقال ليس شرع الكفارة لسد خلة أي فقير كان، بل هو لستر ذنب بطاعة ولا طاعة في أكل نفسه، فإطعام نفسه وأهله في الكفارة غير معقول العلة فثبت ما في «التحرير» ولا ينافيه تمثيل الجمهور للاختصاص به فإن جزئياً واحداً يقع مثالاً لقواعد كثيرة فافهم ومنه شهادة خزيمة بن ثابت فإنه مثل شهادة الاثنين بالنص، ولذا لقب بين الصحابة بذي الشهادتين وهو صحابي جليل القدر استشهد بصفين مع أمير المؤمنين علي بعد شهادة عمار ولما استشهد عمار قال: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم يقول : تقتلك الفئة الباغية فأخذ سيفه فقاتل حتى قتل كذا في الاستيعاب» وقصته على ما في كتب الأصول أنه اشترى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم ناقة من أعرابي وأوفاه ثمنها، ثم جحد الأعرابي استيفاءه وجعل يقول : هلم شهيداً، فقال عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام من يشهد لي»؟ فقال خزيمة بن ثابت أنا أشهد لك يا رسول الله أنك أوفيت الأعرابي ثمن الناقة، فقال عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام : كيف تشهد لي ولم تحضرني؟ فقال : يا رسول الله أنا أصدقك فيما تأتيني به من خبر السماء، أفلا أصدقك فيما تخبر به من أداء ثمن الناقة؟ فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم: «من شهد له خزيمة فهو حسبه» ثبتت كرامة له مختصة به لاختصاصه؟ بفهم حل الشهادة له صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم عن أخباره) ولم يفهم هذا غيره فلا يقاس عليه مثله أو فوقه) كالخلفاء الراشدين رضوان الله عليهم هذا هو الذي رامه الإمام فخر الإسلام بقوله، لكنه ثبت كرامة له فلم يصح إبطاله، ولم يرد أن الكرامة لا تتناول الغير حتى يرد عليه أنه خلاف الواقع، فإنه قد يتشارك اثنان في كرامة واحدة ثم قد يناقش فيه بأن الاختصاص لم يثبت بعد من قوله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه وسلم من شهد له الخ . . وإنما يلزم لو كان هناك مفهوم اللقب والتعليل بفهم حل الشهادة لا يدل على الاختصاص بل يجوز فهمه من غيره من كل مسلم، والحق أن هذا جدل، والسياق يدل على الاختصاص، وحل الشهادة في الأمور الدنيوية بخبره لا يتوقف الإيمان عليه بل الظاهر أنه كان عندهم الشهادة بالمعاينة فافهم والمشهور إنه اخرج من القاعدة، فهو بمنزلة مستثنى عنها ، فلا يجوز إلحاق الغير به، واعترض عليه بأن تعليل التخصيص جائز ، فكما جاز تخصيصه يجوز تخصيص من في طبقته أو أعلى منه بالتعليل، والحق أن هذا ليس تخصيصاً لعدم التلاصق بل نسخاً لقاعدة عامة، ولا يجوز تقليل الناسخ ولو سلم أنه تخصيص فتعميمه فيما سوى هذا المخصص الصحابة إلى هذا الآن فافهم وأنت تعلم أن الاكتفاء به معقول في الشهادة (للكمال التدين) والحفظ وكذا الإخراج عن قاعدة عامة من اشتراط العدد مطلقاً) في الشهادات للاختصاص بالفهم) للأمور على ما هي عليه (كما عقل شهادة القابلة دفعاً للحرج) فإنه لا يشاهد الرجال الولادة وغير القابلة من النساء قلما يشاهد (فليس) قبول شهادته مما لا يعقل كما في شرح المختصر فتدبر
The fourth principle: Qiyas. [The ruling] does not become general through ta'lil. And it is not far to say that the legislation of kaffarah is not to fill the need of any poor person, but rather to cover a sin with obedience, and there is no obedience in eating one's own self; thus feeding oneself and one's family in kaffarah is not rationally understood in terms of 'illa. So what is in al-Tahrir is confirmed. And the representation of the majority for ikhtisas does not contradict it, for a single particular can serve as an example for many rules, so understand. And among them is the testimony of Khuzayma ibn Thabit, for it is like the testimony of two persons by text. Hence he was nicknamed among the Companions 'the one with two testimonies'. He was a noble Companion martyred at Siffin with Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali after the martyrdom of 'Ammar. When 'Ammar was martyred, he said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) say: The transgressive faction will kill you.' So he took his sword and fought until he was killed. Thus in al-Isti'ab. And his story, as in the books of usul: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) bought a camel from a Bedouin and paid him its price. Then the Bedouin denied receiving payment and kept saying: 'Bring a witness.' He (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'Who will testify for me?' Khuzayma ibn Thabit said: 'I testify for you, O Messenger of Allah, that you paid the Bedouin the price of the camel.' He (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'How do you testify for me when you were not present?' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I believe you in what you bring from heaven's news; should I not believe you in what you inform about paying the price of the camel?' Then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify for him, it is sufficient for him.' A miracle (karama) was established specific to him due to his understanding of the permissibility of testimony for him (peace be upon him and his family and companions) from his reports. No one else understood this, so no one equal or above him (like the rightly guided caliphs) can be analogized to him. This is what Imam Fakhr al-Islam intended by his statement, but it is established as a miracle specific to him, so it cannot be invalidated. He did not mean that a miracle does not involve others, such that it would be contradicted by reality, for two people may share a single miracle. Then one may object that the specificity is not established by his statement 'Whoever has Khuzayma testify...', for it would only follow if there were a concept of the title, and the ta'lil by understanding the permissibility of testimony does not indicate specificity; rather, it is possible for any Muslim to understand it. The truth is that this is dialectic (jadal). The context indicates specificity. The permissibility of testimony in worldly matters based on his report does not depend on faith; rather, apparently they required testimony by direct observation, so understand. And the well-known [view] is that it is excluded from the [general] rule, so it is like an exception from it; thus others cannot be attached to it. And it was objected against this that ta'lil of ikhtisas is permissible; just as its specification is permissible, so too the specification of those of his level or above is permissible by ta'lil. The truth is that this is not specification due to lack of connection, but rather abrogation (naskh) of a general rule; and the abrogator cannot be minimized. Even if it is conceded that it is specification, then its generalization beyond this specified [case] among the Companions continues until now, so understand. And you know that accepting his testimony is rationally understood due to perfection of religion and memory; and similarly, the removal from the general rule of the absolute requirement of number in testimonies is due to specificity of understanding of matters as they are, just as the testimony of a midwife is accepted to avoid hardship, for men do not witness childbirth and other women rarely witness it. So accepting his testimony is not irrational, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar, so ponder.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage opens with a discussion on the principle of qiyas (analogy) and specifically addresses the issue of rulings that are khass (specific) to a particular person and whether they can be extended by qiyas. The author uses the example of Khuzayma ibn Thabit, whose single testimony was accepted by the Prophet ﷺ as equivalent to two witnesses, a ruling established by explicit textual evidence (nass). The story illustrates that this was a karama (miracle) specific to Khuzayma due to his unique understanding that the Prophet's reports in worldly matters are as reliable as those in religious matters. The text emphasizes that this ruling cannot be extended to others through qiyas, even to those of higher status like the rightly guided caliphs. The discussion addresses potential objections: whether the specificity is proven, whether ta'lil (rationing) can make the ruling general, and whether the exclusion is a case of naskh (abrogation) rather than takhsis (specification). The author concludes that the ruling is a well-known exception, not subject to analogy, and that its rationality is supported by similar concessions like accepting a midwife's testimony to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
اختصاص (ikhtisas): A ruling specific to a particular individual or situation, not to be extended by qiyas.
كرامة (karama): A miracle or extraordinary event granted to a righteous person, here used to justify the specificity of the ruling for Khuzayma.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Khuzayma's testimony accepted as equivalent to two witnesses, according to the passage?
A) Because of his high status as a Companion
B) Because it is a karama (miracle) specific to him
C) Because of a general qiyas on similar cases
D) Because the Prophet needed a witness

Key Takeaway
A ruling established as a karama for a specific individual is an exception (ikhtisas) and cannot be extended to others by qiyas, even if the rationale seems understandable.
